After having completed for you, O my son, this book, which is the last of the knowledge in medicine with its complement, and having reached the end of it through its expositions and his declarations, I wished to complete it for you with this Treatise, which is a part of operation, that is, surgery with the hand.
For operation with the hand has been laid low in our region and in our time, and the knowledge of it has perhaps entirely perished, and its trace has entirely disappeared, and there remained from it only small descriptions in ancient books, which were changed by hand: and they incurred error and hesitation until its intentions were closed off and its vision was lengthened. It seemed to me that I should revive it with the arrangement of this Treatise in it according to the way of exposition, declaration, and abbreviation: and that I should come with the forms of Cauterii's tools, and the other tools of operation: since it is made from its declaration addition, and from its operation which is necessary.
The reason why a good artisan of it with his own hand is not found in our time is this: because the art of medicine is long, and it is necessary for its author to be exercised before that in the science of anatomy, which Galen narrated, until he knows the joints of the members, and their forms, and their conjunction and separation, and have knowledge of the bones, and nerves, and sinews, and their number, and their egressions, and the pulses of the veins, and the quieting of them, and the exits of the places of them.
And on account of this Hippocrates said that a name with a name is much, and with work is few, and especially in the art of hand.
Indeed, we have already spoken of that at the entrance of this book.
Since those who are not aware of what we have said about anatomy are not spared from falling into the error in which men perish: just as I have seen many of those who are formed from this science and boast about it without knowledge and without experience.
That is because I have seen a stupid doctor cut open a scrophulous abscess on the neck of a woman and cut some arteries in her neck: therefore the woman's blood flowed, until she died in her hands.
And I have seen another doctor who presumed to remove a stone from a man who had grown old, and the stone was large. Therefore he reached him and removed it with a piece of the bladder. Therefore the man died on the third day.
And indeed I had already been called to remove it: and I saw from the size of the stone and the weakness of the man that he would die.
And I have seen another doctor who received a bribe from a certain duke of our land for medicine: and it happened to the black eunuch who was with him, a fracture near the calcaneum in his leg: and the doctor hurried with his ignorance, and tied the fracture over the wound with bandages, and with strong bandaging, and did not let the wound breathe.
Then he healed him according to his own desires. Then he sent him away for several days, and told him not to untie the bandage: and it stood thus until his leg became an abscess, and his foot, and he came to destruction.
Therefore I was called to him: and I hurried to untie the bandage: and following this, there was peace, and he escaped from his pains.
However, corruption was already confirmed in the member, and I could not restrain it.
Therefore, corruption ceased to wander in the member until it died.
And I saw another physician who pierced the carbuncular tumor, and it became ulcerated after days, until its evil was revealed to its lord.
That is, because when cancer is pure from melancholic humor, then it is not necessary to approach it with iron at all, unless there is a member that can tolerate it, so that the whole of it is cut off.
And because of that, my son, it is necessary for you to know that the operation with the hand is divided into two divisions: namely, the operation with which safety is associated, and the operation with which there is danger in many positions.
And I have already awakened in every place of this book, in which operation comes, in which there is fear and fear.
Therefore, it is necessary for you to beware of that and abandon it, so that the fool does not find a way to speak and disgrace.
Therefore, take the measure with solicitude and protection, and your infirm ones with facility and firmness, and use the better way leading to salvation and praiseworthy succession through the grace of God: and leave terrible difficulties of healing: and remove your souls from that which makes you fear, so that doubt may enter upon you in your faith and your benefit.
For it is rather remaining to your glory, and higher in this world, and finally to your quantities.
For Galenus already said in some of his admonitions. Do not heal bad difficulties: so that you are not called bad doctors.
Now however, this Treatise has been divided into three Chapters.
Chapter One.
Of the Cautery with Fire, and the Cautery with Sharp Medicine, arranged from beginning to end, including the forms of instruments and tools for cauterization, and everything necessary for the operation.
Chapter Two.
Of Cutting and Perforation, Bloodletting and Phlebotomy, and Wounds: and Extraction of Arrows, and similar things: and the entire Chapter arranged according to the forms of instruments.
Chapter Three.
Of Restoration, and Dislocation, and Cure of Twisting, and similar things: arranged from beginning to end, including the forms of instruments.
However, before I remind you of the operation with it, it is necessary that I say about the quality of its Jaw, and the harm of that: and in which constitution it appears.
I say therefore, that the speech about the quality of the Jaw of the Cautery, and its harm, is a long and subtle speech, a knowledge, and a hidden secret.
Also many wise men spoke about it, and they disagreed in it: and to me indeed it is insufficient by the words of them, fearing the lengthening.
I say therefore, that the Cautery brings universally to every constitution, which is with matter, and without matter: excepting two constitutions, which are the constitution hot without matter, and the constitution dry without matter.
In a warm and dry compound with matter, they separated. For some said that the cauterizing iron of the juvenile was in it. And others said the opposite of that, namely that the cauterizing iron is not suitable for the illness which is from warmth and dryness: because the nature of fire is warmth: and unsuitable is it, that one should be healed from the illness of warmth and dryness with warmth and dryness.
And he who said the opposite of that said: that by cauterizing, a cure is made for every illness of warmth and dryness which happens in the bodies of men: because when you compare the body of man, and its moistures, to the compound of fire, you find the body of man cold.
And I indeed say by his word: because from experiment he has shown me that many times.
However it is not necessary to come to that, unless he who has already been tested, and exercised in the chapter of cauterization exercise last, and knows the diversity of human compounds, and the disposition of illnesses in themselves, and their causes, and the accidents of them, and the time of them.
And from other compounds there is not upon you fear: and especially in illnesses which are cold and moist. For now all physicians have gathered upon them: and they did not separate in cure with cauterization in them.
And know you children, that from the secret of cure with cauterization with fire, and its goodness above cauterization with burning medicine is: because fire is simple, whose action does not reach, except to the member which is cauterized: and it does not harm another member joined with it, unless a little harm.
The action of medicine reaches as far as to extend from the body: and perhaps it causes difficulty in healing a member, and perhaps it kills.
However, fire, due to its subtlety and goodness of its substance, does not do that unless it overflows.
Indeed, we have now become aware of that through experiment, because of the length of service and study with the art, and position above truth of things: and for that reason I excuse myself from the length of speech.
And if it were not, because it is not allowed for this my book, I would bring to you a secret hidden in fire, and the quality of its operation in bodies of its expulsion, which expels sufferings demonstrated by philosophical speech, which would be remembered by your minds.
And know, my sons, that they themselves disagree in the time when it is fitting to do cauterization, and they set a better time for the truth.
And I say, that cauterization is fitting at every time: because the accidental harm is sunk in the benefit, which is drawn with the cauterizer. Especially if cauterization is for pain from necessary pains, strong, urgent ones who do not tolerate delay: because it is feared that something evil may happen which is greater than the small harm that happens through delay.
And may not fall into your minds, my sons, that which they do not fear, namely that the common people and stupid physicians, namely that to the pain which is healed by cauterization, there is not always return: and they put this consequence, and the matter is not as they think: because cauterization is not, except in place of medicine, which changes the complexion, and dries moistures which are cause why pains happen.
However, the excessive use of cauterizing can be detrimental to the medicine due to its speed of healing, its effectiveness, and its strong influence over the body. It is possible for the sickness to return at a later time according to the nature of the infirm person, the location of their sickness, and its strength. Also, it can be caused by the accumulation of excessive substances within their body, or from foods and similar causes that led to the application of the cauterization unless the sickness returns.
A subtle sickness in a member with few excessive substances and moisture, such as a tooth cauterization due to pain and similar causes, is possible that this pain does not return in it. But this happens in few cases.
Indeed, the common saying that cauterization is the last of the medicines is correct, not as they intend in it: because they believe that there is no cure that corresponds with the medicine, nor with another after the fall of the cauterization.
The matter is indeed the opposite of that, and their intention, that cauterization is the last of the medicines, is not so, unless when we administer modes of cure in some sicknesses, and those medicines do not correspond: then we administer at the end of the matter cauterization, and it corresponds: then it falls, that cauterization is the last of the medical arts, not according to the intention which the common people and many foolish physicians understand.
The ancients indeed said that cauterization with gold is better than cauterization with iron: and they did not say this unless because of the equality of gold, and the sublimity of its substance: and they said that it does not make pus in the place of cauterization. However, it is not absolutely true that I have already proven and discovered that it does not work in certain bodies without other things.
And a cautery with it is good, and better than with iron, as they said. However, when you put the cautery into the fire from gold, it is not indicated to you when it is burned according to the amount that you want, because of the redness of gold: and when it approaches the heat, and if you add more to it, it melts in the fire and turns into sheets.
Therefore, the craftsman falls from that into the occupation: and for that reason, the cautery with iron is made by us faster and closer, from straightness to the operation.
And indeed, I have already arranged this Chapter on Cautery, according to chapters: and I have arranged them from head to foot, so that those seeking it may find what they want from it.
Chapter 2.
This cauterization is applied to the dominion of moisture and cold over the brain: which two are causes of sweat, and multitude of discharges of humors from the head to the parts of the eyes and ears, and multitude of sleep, and pain of the teeth, and pain of the throat: and universally all kinds of distress, which occur from cold, such as paralysis, and sweats, epilepsy, and apoplexy, and similar diseases to those distresses.
The method of cauterization is, that you order the sick person: to be emptied at first with a cleansing solution, head three nights, or four, according to what requires the power of the sick person, and his age, and his custom.
Then instruct him to shave his head with a razor. Then make him sit between your hands in a square position, so that he has already placed his hands on his chest.
Then place the root of your thumb on the root of his nose between his eyes. Whenever your middle finger reaches that spot, mark the location with a pen.
Then heat the cauterizing iron of olive oil: its form is as follows.
Then place it on the marked spot with the pen, with a downward movement, as your hand is gradually tightened, and you turn it back. Then quickly withdraw your hand, and look at the spot.
If you see that the amount of bone from the skull is equal to the amount of alkali or zeuberg, then lift your hand. And if not, repeat your hand with the same iron, or with another if it is cooled: until you see the bones that I told you.
Then take some salt and dissolve it in water, and drink the solution with the wound, and place it on the spot: and leave it for three days.
Then place the salt water drunk on the wound on butter, and leave it on the spot until the scab of the fire is destroyed. Then care for it with the ointment tetrapharmacon until it is healed.
Now they have said that the more the wound remains open, the more pus is emitted: therefore it is better and more healing.
And some of them said that the skin should be cauterized until the bone: and the cauterizing iron should be held until something of the density of bone is burned.
Then it is scraped after what was burned from the bone, then it is cared for.
Some say that when the cauterizer reaches the last part, it should be pressed against the bone until an impression is made in the form of a crescent: or with an instrument like that which women place between their teeth for the purpose of learning the alphabet: and they believe that vapors from the head will escape through this place, and the wound will remain open for a long time.
Then it should be dressed until it heals.
To me, however, these two kinds of cauterizer do not appear at all except in certain men according to the way of fear.
And it is better to leave it alone with its own health, in my opinion.
For the head becomes weakened from the solution of its natural continuity, just as we have shown in other members: and especially when the head of an invalid is weak by nature: and indeed the first kind of cauterizer is more saving and better for me, and I use it: therefore, work with it in health.
Head III.
When there is chronic pain in the whole head, and it is prolonged in the invalid, and he uses hemlock, and coals, and head-cleansers, and oils, and plasters: Especially if he has already been cauterized with the one cauterizer which we have mentioned, and does not apply anything from them: then consider. For if the head of the invalid is strong by nature, and is not weak, and has found a violent cold: then cauterize with another cauterizer under it slightly. Then cauterize it on top of all the horns of its own head with the cauterizer, so that the skin does not pass through, and a quantity of bone is exposed, as we have mentioned. And cauterize it with a single cauterizing iron at the back of its head, in the place called the "uas": and it is the location where the windpipe is placed: and raise your mat (or blanket) in this, and do not uncover its mouth. For indeed it has found a remedy for that very severe pain, and different from the pain of all other cauterizations of the head.
And I will call this cauterizing iron in its place: and it must be a cauterizing iron by which the horns of the head are cauterized, and the back of its head more subtly with the cauterizing iron by which the middle of the head is cauterized.
HEAD IV.
WHEN PAIN AND SORENESS OCCUR IN A PART OF THE HEAD, AND THE PAIN EXTENDS UP TO THE EYE, AND IS CLEANSED WITH REMEDIES FOR CLEANSING THE HEAD, AND THE REST OF THE CURE IS ADMINISTERED, AS I SAID IN THE DIVISIONS OF ILLNESSES, AND IT DOES NOT HEAL ALL OF IT: THEN CAUTERIZATION IS DONE IN TWO WAYS: EITHER CAUTERIZATION WITH A SHARP MEDICINE BURNING, OR WITH AN IRON.
BUT THE CAUTERIZING IRON WITH A SHARP MEDICINE BURNING IS, THAT YOU TAKE ONE Tooth of garlic, AND REMOVE ITS SHELL, AND CUT OFF ITS EXTREMITIES FROM BOTH SIDES. THEN CUT THE PLACE OF THE PAIN AT THE TIME WHEN THE BROAD LANCET IS USED, UNTIL THERE IS A LOCUS UNDER THE SKIN, IN WHICH THE TOOTH IS CAPTURED.
THEN INSERT IT INTO ITS SKIN, UNTIL IT IS HIDDEN: THEN STRAP OVER IT WITH A PIECE OF CLOTH IN DECENT CONSTRICTION, AND LET IT GO FOR FIFTEEN HOURS, THEN DISSOLVE IT, AND EXTRACT THE GARLIC, AND LET HIM REST FOR TWO DAYS, OR THREE: AFTER THAT, PUT ON IT BANDAGE SOAKED IN BUTTER, UNTIL THE PLACE BECOMES PUS: THEN CARE FOR IT WITH OINTMENT UNTIL IT HEALS.
And if you wish to do this with certain burning medicines, which I have written about in my twelfth treatise on Burning Medicaments.
However, the cauterization of that with iron is done in this manner. The cauterization with fire, which has this form.
And it is called the Clavil, because its form is like the form of a claw, in which there is some curvature, and in the middle of it is a small elevation.
Then place it on the spot and hold your hand: and you will turn the iron gradually with speed: and the quantity that is burned from the thickness of the skin, is like its middle. And raise your hand, so that the artery, which is below, does not burn and there is no loss of blood flow.
Then take the wound and soak it in salt water, and place it on the spot, and leave it for three days: then place the wound with butter: afterwards care for it with ointment until it is healed.
And if you wish, cauterize this hemicrania with the second edge of the small cauterizer. And avoid the incision of the artery in this hemicrania, not the ancient one properly.
¶ On the method of cauterizing in the ancient hemicrania.
When you are treating the hemicrania, with what we said about the previous cure, and what we said in the divisions of ailments, and it does not benefit from the cure: and you see from the ailment, that what we said about the first cauterization with medicine, or with the cauterizer with fire, does not suffice for it, then it is necessary to burn the small cauterizer, until it becomes white after the sign of pain with a line, whose length is the middle of a finger, or something like that: and place your hand halfway, and hold it until you cut the artery, and go through to the bone.
However, it is necessary for you to guard against the continuation of the jawbone, which moves during chewing, so as not to be burned by the side or the nerve that moves it, from which a spasm may occur.
And let this be over the guard and the precaution against the flow of blood from the severed artery. For in its severing there is fear, and especially for him who does not know what it does, and is not studious or experienced: and he leaves the operation with it first.
And I will come with the remembrance of the management of the flow of blood from the artery according to its own manner and in its own place in this book.
If you see from the pain that this cauterizer does not suffice for him, and you see the weak body bearing the cauterizer in the middle of the head, as we have narrated, take care of the wound until he is healed.
And if you wish, administer the cauterizer which we said in the chapter of extracting the artery with a cauterizer having two knives. For this cauterization is better and more fitting.
On the method of cauterizing in ear pain.
When pain occurs in the ear from cold, and it is cured with solutions, and the rest of the cure as we said in division, and the pain is not removed, then cauterize with fire: and this is what is called a prick, whose form is this.
Then pricks with it after its ignition around the ear entirely, as it is turned: or around both, if the pain is in both. And withdraw yourself with the cauterizer a little from the root of the ear after you have marked the places with the cauterizer: and let the quantity of the cauterizer be ten pricks in every ear, and about that.
Then treat the affected areas until they are healed.
On the method of cauterizing in torture.
Chapter 7.
The torture that is cured with cauterization is only from the types that occur from phlegm, as we said in the divisions of illnesses.
And the absence of cauterization of the type that occurs from dryness and spasm of the nerve.
When you treat this type of torture with honey, and capitpurges, and gargarisms, and your cure does not help, then it is necessary for you to cauterize the sick person with three cauterizations: one at the root of the ear, and second a little lower from his time, and third at the junction of the two lips.
And place your cauterization on the opposite side of the weak part. Because softening does not occur except in the part that appears healthy.
And the form of cauterization is to cauterize the sick person with the cauterization directly at the tip of the upper ear under the horn of the head a little: and another in the time: whose length is according to the length of the thumb. And place your hand with the cauterization until the quantity of half the thickness of the skin is burned.
And this is the form of the cauterization, and it is a species from a knife, whose form was mentioned before: but it is not too sharp, as you see: and it is necessary that the knife be a little too thick.
Then treat the affected areas with what preceded until they are healed.
On the method of cauterizing in old apoplexy.
When apoplexy is old, and you treat it with what we said, and your medication does not help, and the sick person does not have a fever, then cauterize him with four cauterizations on all the horn of his head, and with the cauterization in the middle of his head, as we said, and with the cauterization in the back of his head, according to what preceded: and the method of cauterization should be according to what preceded.
Even cauterization is performed with a cautery on the mouth of the stomach: and it is more final.
Then it is treated, with what preceded it.
Chapter 9.
It is necessary that in the drink first give great hiera powder, and purifying pills cleanse the brain.
Then shave the head of the sick person all over, and place on his occiput the plaster of synapi described in the treatise on plasters: and place it several times.
For this is indeed the method of cauterization: and do it according to order, as I said there.
If therefore he is healed by this, it is good. If not: then perform three cauterizations on the posterior part of his head, which are descending from the superior part of the head down to the lower part of the eye: and place between every cauterization the thickness of a finger.
Then treat the cauterization, with what preceded it.
But if you wish an addition, and the sick person is tolerating this: then perform cauterization on the middle. If you wish an addition: then cauterize him over two horns.
Then treat him, until he is healed: and let the cauterization be oily according to the form which was previously given.
On the method of cauterization in paralysis, and softening.
Chapter 10.
It is necessary that you proceed in the cleansing of the head with hiera, and with what we said.
Then shave the head of the sick person: afterwards cauterize him in the middle of his head, and with a cauterization on every horn of his head, and on the back of his neck, and three on the spines of his neck.
If you lack the ability to tolerate many of these softening methods for the body and are weak, and the pain is strong: then cauterize it with four cauteries on the spines of the back, and the last one with a cauterizer until it burns the most of its skin, and raise your hand. Then care for it until it heals: and thus cauterize with oil.
On the method of cauterizing in epilepsy.
An epileptic should not be cauterized unless he is the one whose epilepsy is from phlegm.
Therefore it is necessary to cleanse his brain first with vinegar, and with the rest of the cure which we mentioned in division: when he is weak, or is not able to bear the taking of medicines.
But if it is a child who does not bear medicines, then the gargle is administered, and cleansing mastications of the brain are given before many days with good nutrition.
Then shave his head, and then cauterize him with a cauterizer in the middle of his head, according to what preceded in method: and with another cauterizer in the back of his head, and on every horn of his own head with a cauterizer. But if he is weak and strong, and is able to bear it, then cauterize him with the cauteries which I said in having paralysis, and softening of the body on the spines of the neck, and the spines of the back: and the cauterizer should be oily according to the method which preceded.
But if he is weak, then place the thin cauterizer in this way.
On the method of cauterizing in melancholy.
When the cause of melancholy is corrupted humors and thick phlegm, then cauterize with the cauteries we mentioned in one having paralysis.
And if the cause of melancholy is an excess of humors flowing down to melancholy, and there is a weak moist body, then give him a drink that cleanses his brain, according to what preceded in division: then shave the sick head, and make afterwards a well-made tortellini from linen, like a circle.
Then place it in the middle of the head: and the sick one sitting squarely held from every part.
Then present the liniment. And it is more fitting from old butter. And warm it gently over a fire with measured heat, which the finger could bear when inserted into it. Then evacuate it in the middle of his head in a circle, and let him go until he is cooled.
Do this for the sick one once a week, with good management of his other affairs, until he is healed.
Or if you wish, cauterize it by making small points as much as possible, except that you hold the hand with the cauterizer: indeed it should be smelling.
For this kind of cauterization humidifies the brain with quality.
Then place on it a wet cloth soaked in butter, or chicken fat.
¶ On the manner of cauterizing in water flowing down to the eye.
Chapter 13.
When the beginning of water is declared to you in the eye by signs which I said in division, then begin and give the sick one a drink with it that cleanses his head.
And guard him from all moistures, and make him sit in the bath, on fasting days for several days.
Then instruct him to cut off his head and cauterize it in the middle of his head. Then cauterize it over the two temples with two cauteries, if there is an onset of water in both eyes at once: or from one side, if there is an onset of water in one eye: and cut off all the veins and arteries that are under the skin: and let the cauterization be long in the width of the temples: and beware of blood flow.
If you see anything from it, then cut it off immediately with any possible medicine: and I will come with wisdom, which is in the extraction of arteries, and their cutting, and caution against blood flow.
And sometimes it is cauterized on the neck, under two bones, with two last cauterizations produced.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in the eyes of olden times.
When the tears of the eyes are olden, persistent: and they are on the veins, and arteries that are in the manifest exterior of the head, it is verified that that is from superfluities cold, phlegmatic: then cauterize with the same cauterization that I told in the onset of water descending, cauterization in the middle of the head, and two cauterizations over the two temples, and two cauterizations in the neck under two bones. And if you need additional, then cauterize it on every side of the eye carefully, over the extreme of the eyebrow with a small cauterization.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in the nostril discharge.
When you treat it, with that which we said in the division, and there is no remedy: then hasten, and give in the weak medicine for three nights: then cut off his head, and cauterize it in the middle with a fat cauterization. Then, cauterize the eyelid with a cautery hook, applying two cauteries, one above each eyebrow, just beneath the hair.
And guard against the artery, lest you cut it.
And this is the shape of the cautery hook.
On the method of cauterizing for relaxation of the eyelid.
When the eyelid is relaxed from pain or moisture, then cauterize the eyelid with a single cautery and this lunar cautery.
And if you wish, cauterize it above each eyebrow a little with two cauteries in every part: and they should be extended from both temples: and the length of all the cauteries should be according to the length of the eyebrows: and do not let your hand touch the cautery, but according to the quantity that burns the third eyelid.
On the method of cauterizing the eyelid when hairs point towards the eye.
The cautery in this case is according to two methods: either a cautery with fire: or a cautery with burning medicine.
In the cautery with fire, however, instruct the sick person before it, so that he may let go of his hairs, if it is from those who remove them, until they are extended and evened out. But if they point at his birth: then close his eyes with a bandage, so that they may not move, until they are born.
When they are born and evened out, then place the head of the sick person in your lap: then mark on the eyelid with a hot iron, a sign that it is according to the figure of myrtle leaves: and let the beginning of the sign be near the hairs.
Then place a moistened cotton pad on the albumen or on the mucilage of psyllium over the eye.
Then apply a cauterizing iron with this shape.
Then cauterize over the shape you indicated gradually in several strokes, until the surface of the skin is burned, which appears like the figure of a myrtle leaf, entirely.
And the sign of your work's health is that if you see the eyelid of the eye already contracted and the hairs raised at the point of the eye.
So wash your hand then, and let it rest for three days.
Then place a cotton pad with butter on it over it until the eschar is removed. Then care for it with ointment until it heals.
If some of the hairs return after an hour and the eyelid softens, then repeat the cauterizing iron on that spot, as you did first.
But if the hairs are on the lower part, then cauterize that spot until it returns to its natural place: and so it will not prick the eye with the hairs.
You should order the sick person to let go of the hairs until they grow and become equal. Make a shape of a myrtle leaf from paper and cloth.
Then take from the known soap and from the unsoaked chalk of each ounce I or about that: then rub them together with good friction, and make it with speed, so that it does not freeze. Then take a piece from that on the cloth you made like the shape of a myrtle leaf, and place it on the eyelid of one or both eyes. And place under the eye a moistened cotton pad in an egg white: and let the head of the sick person be in your lap.
And place your finger on the medicine, and press it slightly. And you move it whenever the sick person feels the bite of the medicine, since its bite is like fire.
While therefore he persisted in what he found to be the bite, then let go of the medicine, and move it with your finger. When therefore the bite is quieted, then remove the medicine, and wash the eye with water.
And consider then, if you see the eyelid raised, as it is raised with contraction with fire, or with incision, it is good: and if not, then repeat on it from the medicine on the place where it does not imprint the medicine, and does not stain, until your operation equals, and the eye contracts.
Then place on it a cotton pad with butter, until the burn of the skin is eradicated. Then care for it with diaphenhydramine ointment, or another, until it is healed.
And it is necessary for you at the operation, that you guard the last guard, lest something fall into the eye from the medicine.
If the eyelid softens after days, and something fighting from the hair is in the eye, then repeat the medicine on that place which softens from the eyelid properly, as you did first. Then care for it, until it is healed.
And this is the shape of the leaf of myrtle.
And know that the eyes of men vary in size and symmetry. Therefore according to that be your consideration: and do not hide the path of righteousness to him who has a desire for this art.
On the method of cauterizing a lacrimal fistula.
When you are treating a fistula, since as we mentioned in the divisions of diseases, and your cure does not succeed: then, it is necessary for you to cauterize it according to this method.
Instruct the patient to place his head in your lap, and hold his head between his hands thus, so that he does not move, nor act with his own head.
Then place a cotton swab soaked in a solution of oui, or in a mucilage of psyllium on his eye: then heat the cauterizing iron, whose form is thus.
Let it be concave, like the form of the pen feather of a quill from one end, with which the cauterizing iron is made: and if you wish it to be piercing up to the other end, and if you wish it to be upwards, then test thus.
However, this concave is better for your work.
Then express the fistula, if it is open, and remove the pus from it, and dry it: and if it is not open, then open it, and remove its pus.
Then place then on it the cauterizing iron, which is made fiery.
And hold with it your hand for a moment near the cauterizing iron from the eye, to the part of the nose, so that your hand does not err, or disturb the sick person: and place the cauterizing iron in the fat of the eye, and corrupt it.
If therefore you reach the beginning of your cauterizing iron up to the bone, it will be good. And if not: then repeat the cauterizing iron once, or twice, if you need it: and let it go for three days.
Then place a poultice with butter on it, and care for it with a drying ointment until it heals.
If it has passed forty days and is not healed: then place a sharp, corrosive medicine on it until the bone is removed: and cut it according to how it comes in its chapter.
And there is another method of cauterizing a fistula, which some of the first ones said. Bend to the place of the fistula, and plug it: then place in the wound a thin cannula, that is, a thin needle, whose form is this. And pour in a quantity of drachma from the melted lead, and hold your hand with the cannula well retained, and do not move it at all weakly, so that it does not run, or the melted lead reaches his eye.
And it is necessary to place on the weak person's eye a poultice soaked in white of egg, or in water.
For lead burns the place of the fistula, and heals it with a marvelous cure.
If the fistula is healed, with what we said from cauterization, and cure, it is good. And if not, then it is necessary to administer the opening of the nose, and reduce the fistula to the course of the nose, according to how it comes to its proper place.
On the method of cauterizing in wounds of the lips.
Frequently wounds occur in the lip, which are called "pili," and especially in the lips of children.
When therefore you care for these wounds, with what we said in the division of diseases, and not a cure is combined, then a small cauterizing iron, according to this form.
And let its concavity be according to the sharpness of the knife.
Then place it quickly on those incisions, until the cautery reaches the depth of the incisions.
Then care for it with the caustic, until it heals.
¶ On the method of cauterizing a mouth ulcer.
When an abscess occurs at the root of the gingiva, or in the palate, or in the roots of the teeth: then it produces pus, and bursts: afterwards it becomes putrid, and pus runs out, and a fistula forms: then care for it, and the cure does not improve in it, then it is necessary to use a burning cautery according to the amount that fits into the fistula. Then insert it into the opening of the fistula, and hold your hand until the burning iron reaches the depth and end of it: do this once or twice.
Then care for it after that, with what we said about the cure until it heals.
If therefore the pus is cut off and healed, it will be good. And if not, then it is necessary to expose the place, and remove the bone of the corrupt part according to what comes into its head.
¶ On the method of cauterizing gums, and molten teeth.
When the gum is molten due to moisture, and the teeth are moved, and you care for it with medicines, and it does not improve: then place the head of the sick person in your lap.
Then a burning iron, of which the shape will come after these, so that you place a cannula on the tooth: and insert the burning iron into it quickly: and hold your hand for a little while, until the sick person feels the heat of the fire has reached the root of the tooth.
And retract your hand: then repeat the cauterization several times, according to what you wish.
Then the sick person will fill their mouth with salt water and hold it for one hour: and then spit it out.
For the tooth is strengthened by motion, and the jaw becomes soft and contracts, and thus the corrupted moisture is dried up.
Chapter on the method of cauterizing in tooth pain.
When the toothache is due to coldness, or there is fever in it, or worms, and no cure is found with medicines: then cauterization is done in two ways: either cauterization with butter: or cauterization with fire.
But cauterization with butter is, so you take calf's butter, and boil it in an iron spoon, or in a vessel. Then take a cloth, and cover it over the end of the tooth. Then submerge it in the boiled butter: and place it on the painful tooth quickly, and hold it until it cools: then repeat it several times, until the power of fire reaches the root of the tooth.
And if you wish, submerge a cloth, or a rag in cold butter, and place it on the painful tooth: and place a hot iron on it, until fire reaches the depth of the cavity of the tooth.
But cauterization with fire is, so you direct it to a tube of air, or an iron tube. And there should be something thick in its body, so that the sharpness of fire does not reach the mouth of the sick person.
Then cauterize with fire, whose form will come: and place it on the tooth: and hold your hand until the cauterization cools.
Perform this procedure several times, as the pain will be alleviated either on that same day or on another day.
And it is necessary for the sick person to fill his mouth with good charcoal and hold it for one hour, then spit it out.
This is the shape of the cauterizing iron.
Cauterize with any tip of the needle according to what is possible; and this is the shape of the cannula.
On the method of cauterizing in Strophuli.
When Strophuli are caused by phlegm, and by cold humors, and they do not obey the digestive process through medicines, and you want to quickly promote their digestion: then use a flat cauterizing iron, whose shape is this.
Having two open ends, so that smoke comes out from the cauterizing iron through the other end: and place it on the abscess once, and twice if you need to, until it reaches the depth of the abscess.
If the abscess is small: then place the cauterizing iron according to the size of the abscess.
Then let it go for three days, and place on it a compress soaked in an infusion, until the burn caused by the fire is removed.
Then care for it with tooth ointment, until the shape of the cannula is healed.
On the method of cauterizing in a hoarse voice, and in constriction of breath.
When moisture is accumulated on the bronchial tube, and especially when it is with a cold temperament, then it is necessary for the sick person to be evacuated first with dissolved medicines.
Then cauterize the wound itself at the root of the neck in a hollow place: and be careful not to let the cauterizer touch the throat, nor on the skin, unless something of it.
Then cauterize the wound itself with another cauterizer at the junction of the neck in the last spinal process of it: and let the cauterizer be narrow according to the mode that preceded.
Then care for it with what came before, until it heals.
¶ On the method of cauterizing in illnesses of the Lungs, and Cough.
When Cough and illness of the Lungs are from moisture and cold, and the sick person does not have fever, nor phthisis, and the illness is old: then cauterize it with two cauterizers above the wishbone in hollow places, gentle, empty. And with another cauterizer in the middle of the chest between two breasts: and let the cauterizer be a needle according to the form that preceded.
And if you want your cauterization to be by puncturing with the cauterizer called Punctum, whose form preceded in puncturing of pain of the ear: and let there be punctures from thirty punctures almost to another.
Then care for it with what came before, until it heals.
And now let the cauterizer have three branches: according to this form. Why relieves with it cauterization, when you do with it once three cauterizers.
Chapter 27.
When the head of the arm is dislocated by the cause of moisture, and it is not set in the hour of its return from dislocation, until it has that habit of returning to it, then dislocate it from a small movement, which happens as we have already testified there, then you should reduce the dislocation in the first. Then the invalid should be laid upon his back, or on the sound side. Then cauterize the bedclothes, until it penetrates it up to the other side, and the figure of cauterization comes with four cauterizations.

And this is the form of a cauterizing iron having three wounds.
And sometimes one is added to this manner, wherefore they are eight cauterizations.

¶ Of the manner of cauterizing the stomach.
When a fever and much moisture occur in the stomach, until they extract it from its connection, and multiply cataracts upon it, and frequent modes of cure, and do not bring relief: then it is necessary that the invalid should be laid upon his back, and extend his legs, and his hands. Then cauterize with three cautery needles, the cautery needle under the ear of the chest in the quantity of a finger's thickness, and two cautery needles below from both sides of the cautery needle of one, until it reaches the triangular shape of the cautery. And stretch them apart so that they do not touch each other when they make pus.
And let the depth of the cautery be the thickness of two-thirds of the skin.
And let the shape of the cautery be according to this form without addition: and if you wish to cauterize with a large cautery in the middle of the stomach according to this form, and let the cautery be according to the shape of a circle according to this form.
And the stomach is to be cauterized by pricking it where it is touched by this cautery: and it is, that the signs above the stomach are pricked according to the quantity, which you wish with the encaustro: then cauterize it with the cautery needle: then care for it with the remedy that preceded until it is healed.
¶ On the method of cauterizing Epar cold.
When it happens in Epar that pain occurs from cold and wetness, or from thick sweating, until it goes beyond its natural exit, and the sick person is cured, since we have said what we said, and it does not help him: then it is necessary for the sick person to be stretched out on his shoulder, and signs are pricked with three cautery needles according to this form, and the same thickness of the skin below Epar, where the arm of a man reaches: and let there be space that is the thickness of a finger between each cautery: and let the cautery be according to the length of the body straight: and do not press your hand with the cautery too much.
And let the quantity of what is burned be equal to the thickness of the skin, and let the quantity of the middle part not be added: and let him who stands on his feet be weak.
But if he is not standing, then let him who lies down, who has already extended his legs and raised his arms.
This is the shape of the cautery.
And it is possible for you, with this cautery, to cauterize with a scalpel when you are with skill and wisdom in the art.
And guard yourself, so that you do not proceed too far in cauterization, and the thickness of the skin is burned throughout, why the whole body is burned, and reaches the intestines: for the skin there is thin, so you know that.
On the method of cauterizing abscesses in the liver.
When it happens, and you want to know if that abscess is in the liver flesh, or in its tunic: then if it is in the liver flesh, it attacks the weak with pain, and there is gravity without sharpness: and if it is in the tunic of the liver, with pain there is very strong sharpness: and you see already, because its cure has tired out the doctors.
Therefore it is necessary that the weak person lie down on his neck. Then the shape of the place of the abscesses with the cautery: then burn the cautery that resembles a ray. And this is its shape. And cauterize with that cautery one, until the whole skin is burned, and it reaches the intestines, until all the pus comes out: then cure him with the cure of the wounds, until he is healed.
And it is not necessary to use this cautery species, unless whose study in the art of medicine is prolonged: and through whose hand these illnesses with trial several times: then for he dares on this operation.
It is indeed better to let her go, with me.
On the method of cauterizing in Pleurisy.
The ancients said, a cautery with the roots of Aristolochia should be applied to cold Pleurisy in this manner. And it is that you should take from the dry roots of Aristolochia, a longer root, which is found among them, and it should be as thick as the size of a finger. Then immerse it in oil: and burn it in the fire. Then cauterize it with a single cautery in that which is between the continuation of the backbone with the neck, and two small cauteries under the chin slightly declining to the part which is under the beard.
And with two cauteries also in that which is between the fifth and sixth rib declining to the backs a little: and with another cautery in the middle of the chest, and with another above the stomach. And with three cauteries from the backs: one in that which is between two spatulas: and with two cauteries from two sides of the chest, lower cauterie which is between two spatulas.
And it is not necessary to press your hand with the cautery, but rather it should be in plain sight of the skin smelling.
And indeed some ancients said that from men there are those who use a cautery from a similar iron rod: and they burn, and they put it inside in that which is between the ribs, until it reaches with it to the apostem, and the pus comes out: as we said in the apostem of Epatis.
But in this piercing with the cautery there is from fear, that either he dies weak immediately, or it happens in the place of a fistula, which has no cure.
Chapter 32 on the method of cauterizing the spleen.
When you are treating a splenic affliction, since as we mentioned earlier, the cure lies in dividing the afflictions, and your treatment does not succeed, then cauterization of it is done in three ways, all of which are correct.
One of which is to perform three or four cauterizations along the length of the spleen according to the shape of the liver cauteries, whose figure precedes it.
And let there be between each cauterization a thickness of the digit's breadth, or a little more or less.
And let the method of cauterization be as we mentioned in the cauterization of the liver equally.
And do not press your hand against the cauterizer: and let the patient be weak and lying on his back.
Another method of cauterization is: to have the cauterizer with two wounds, as we mentioned in the chapter on dislocation of the humerus: and raise the skin which is on the spleen directly, where the elbow of the weak left arm reaches: and let your elevation be according to the width of the body, so that the cauterizations fall according to the length of the body.
Then insert two burning wounds, until you penetrate the skin from the other side: then remove the cauterizer: so there are four cauterizations.
And if you wish to cauterize with another cauterizer having three wounds.
Then care for the cauterizer after you have released it, to emit pus for many days: for it is more helpful than all the other things that preceded from the cure.
Chapter on the method of cauterizing in hydrops.
The cauterizer does not fall into hydrophobia unless properly trained.
When you treat hydrophobia with the methods of cure that we mentioned in the division, and do not combine the cure, then it is necessary to cauterize the patient four times around the umbilicus, and with a cauterizer on the stomach, and another on the epar, and one on the spleen, and two cauterizers after the back between the spines, and one in direct pectoris, and another in direct stomachi: and let the depth of the cauterization be close to the thickness of the skin.
Then dismiss the cauterizer open, so that it emits pus over a long period of time.
And do not remove the sick person from treatment after cauterization with him, for it is necessary that two intentions be gathered to him: and he will hasten to him with the help of God.
The form of the cauterizer with which the belly is cauterized should be closed, according to its previous form: and the form of the one with which the back is cauterized should be olive-oil-like, according to its previous form.
On the method of cauterizing feet and legs.
When abscesses form in hydrophobia and are filled with yellow water: then it is necessary to cauterize on the back of the foot in the nocrati, which is between the auricular and anular: and lift your hand with the cauterizer, and do not twist it: then lift your hand: and do not rub it at all.
For the yellow water flows out, and the cauterizer should be according to this form.
Then make two cauterizers on both legs, and let the cauterizer be according to the length of the leg, one under the knee, and the other below it, around the middle of the leg: and two cauterizers on every hip: and dismiss the cauterizer open without treatment for a long period of time: so that some water flows out from it: then cure him with the rest that we said.

On the method of cauterizing hemorrhoids.

Of the method of cauterizing a fistula in the anus.
Chapter 38.
When the sick person does not obey the incision and operation that we have narrated in its place, and is afraid of it, perhaps he will be healed with a cauterizing iron.
When therefore a fistula occurs and is deep, pus flows from it, and corrupt moistures. Therefore what is more fitting is to probe it with a thin needle. Then know the quantity of its depth with the needle.
Then apply a cauterizing iron that resembles a needle. Then insert the burning iron into the fistula and the quantity in which it entered the clod.
And repeat the iron over it, until those corrupt bodies are burned, once or twice or three times, according to the quantity of your need.
And guard yourself from burning of the nerve, if it is there, or great wound: or if the fistula goes to the body of the bladder, or to the body of the intestine, then guard yourself from all these places.
And do not do that, unless when the fistula is in a fleshy place: and you think, because it is not piercing.
Then care for the place until it heals.
But if the place is sealed, and the materials are cut off from it, and it remains like this for a long time: then you know that it has healed completely.
And if the materials are not cut off from it, then you know that it is piercing, or there is a rotten bone in its depth, or something like that from those: whose memory will come back to its place.
