On the method of cauterizing in sciatica.
When pain occurs in the anus and the cause of this is cold and moisture: and the infirm one is cured with him, as we said in division, and the cure does not reunite, and it is renewed: then it is necessary to dissolve the infirm one from gross humors with fetid pills, or with artificial pills, and similar. Then cauterize him.
And the method of cauterization depends on two methods: either with a cauterizing instrument burning with medicaments, or with fire.
A cauterizing instrument with fire is done in many ways.
One of these methods is to cauterize on top of the pivot stone of his anchor, in a triangular shape, according to this form. And make them either deep or shallow. And let there be space that is the thickness of each cauterization according to the size of a finger: and let the cauterization be oily.
Sometimes, however, the cauterization is done in the middle on top of his anchor. Therefore there are four cauterizations.
And if you wish to cauterize with a circle, whose preceding form is in the cauterization of anchor dislocation, one: so that it contains the whole anchor.
And burn the thickness of the skin entirely.
This is the method of cauterization in Sciatica, when the pain adheres to his anchor and does not extend up to the hip and leg.
But if it extends up to the hip and leg, then cauterize him with two cauterizations on the hip, on the place where he indicates the weakness, in which is the pain, and with your cauterizing instrument on the thigh four fingers towards the sylvestern part: and let the cauterization be knife-like.
And let the depth of the cauterization be according to the thickness of the skin.
But if he indicates that the pain extends up to near the toes of his foot, then cauterize him there where he indicates with your cauterizing instrument, three, or four, or more, if it is needed by him.
If there is an indication of pain under the knee towards the leg, then cauterize that spot with a single knife.
And always remember in all your cauterizations, so that you do not burn the nerves or a large artery, and thus cause harm to the weak body, or contraction.
And I myself have seen one and another from those who cauterized above the knee, and ended up in cauterization, and the leg became swollen, until a tumor followed the foot, and it was perforated entirely, and the entire foot rotted: then diagnosis of the abdomen occurred, and death after that.
If the pain is in both parts at once, cauterize each according to this method.
And some wise men said in cauterization of the ankle, which is this method. Make a similar spatula from iron, whose diameter is the middle of the palm: and it should be at its opening according to the thickness of the nucleus of the finger, or slightly less: and inside that spatula there should be a third spatula.
And there should be a space that is between each spatula by the thickness of the nodule of the thumb: and they should be open on both sides: and their height should be like a nodule, or two nodules: and make them a handle from iron properly fitted in the spatulas.
Then it should be heated in the fire until it glows red, and throw sparks: then it should be placed on a pillow of the weak ankle lying on the healthy side. Then cauterize him with three round cauteries in one stroke.
Then leave him for three days. Afterwards, apply plasters with butter: and let the open wound heal over many days. Then care for it with ointment, until it is healed.
Albucasis says, "In this manner of cauterizing, my son, we have been very little used, because of the fear of its appearance: and therefore, because we find few who are willing to wait over it.
Nevertheless, it is from good cauterizations that he who suffers and finds with him the place of his.
The cauterizing iron with medicaments is burned, so that you make two smae having a perforated ring, into which the card of his door descends from the air, or iron, length of the wall: whose height they are two knots, or as themselves.
And there is space that is between both quantities of thickness of the finger, and they are open below and above: and there is that they contain themselves to each other, according to this form.
Then lay it on the anchorage of a pitcher, sick lying on the healthy side. And press your hand on the anchorage of a pitcher much. Then pour between two circles from hot water, which is heated with fire a little, and hold it for a certain amount of time: and the sick bears its bite, and its burning, for he found its bite like fire, until the bite rests.
Then clean your hand with the tool, and remove hot water from the anchorage all with sweet water: then let it rest for three days.
And place on it butter, until the blackness of the burning is removed: and let it rest for several days, and drain from it pus. It is the last remedy for a wound.
Then treat it with ointments until it heals.
If the pain extends to the hip or leg: make a splint in that which contains water, as you did in the equal anchor.
And this is the method of hot water: and I have already written it in the treatise on the rectification of medicines. Take alkali and unburned lime each one part of the same weight: grind both, and put them in a new pot, whose lower part is perforated with a small hole of the same size as the radius: and put another glass pot under the bottom of the pot: and pour over the alkali and lime from sweet water, which covers both through your finger: after which you press it with your hand good compression: and leave the pot, until the sharp water flows down the lower part of the glass pot.
Then gather all that water and pour it over another lime: and cook, until it is renewed.
For this will then be very strong acid, which is administered in many medical operations, and in the cauterization of the remaining limbs. Because it performs the operation of its fire.
And from the medical remedies with which the anchors are cauterized, also as tesserae, and melted anacardium, and lime with soap, so that both are mixed. ¶
And indeed Galen himself related in his writings the cure of a certain man from ancient times, by which he was cured of the pain of the anchor and the sciatic vein: and praised it very much. And he said that it did not need other cure, and because he was healed from one vice, until he related, because perhaps he had entered the bath carried, and came out of it already healed.
And it is to be taken from the fresh green of seitaragi: and if it is not found, take the dry, recent one, and pound it thoroughly with a little fat, and place it on the anchor where the pain is, or in the leg, or in the hip: and tie it, and let it remain for three hours, or according to the quantity that the sick person feels sedation of the inflammation. Then immerse him in a bath.
When therefore his body becomes moist, immerse him in a chair. For the pain retreats, and he is healed.
And know that one should not use a cautery with these remedies, unless after evacuation of the body.
And Dioscorides who said that, when donkey dung is applied with it to the sciatic nerve, it brings him relief: and a cautery is made in this way. Take wool, and pour oil on it old, and place it on the deep place, which is between the thumb of the foot, and between the heel, and is closer to the heel.
Then take donkey dung dry, and burn it in fire, until it becomes coal.
Then place it on the wool, and let it go, until it is extinguished. Then repeat that. Do not therefore stop doing it, until the sense reaches above the remedy up to the hip, and the pain rests.
And this method of cautery is called the cautery of Vaccinium.
§ On the cauterization of the pain of the back.
Sometimes pain occurs in the back from many causes, or by accident, or by blow, or by excessive evacuation, and similar things, from the infusion of cold and wet matter: and cautery does not fall, except in this kind alone, which is made from the infusion of cold matter.
Therefore, after evacuation of the sick with foul-smelling pills and similar ones, they should be placed on the back where the pain is, three lines according to the width of the sick person's spine, after which signs with a hot iron in every line five cauterizations, or more according to the amount that comes from the tolerance of the sick person by its virtue: and let the cauterization be made with a cauterizing needle.
And if you wish, cauterize three times or four with a middle cauterizing needle, in this form.
On the method of cauterizing in the beginning of gibbosities.
This affliction often happens to small children.
And the sign of its beginning in children is: that which happens to him a tightness on his breathing and movement: and it is found in the last rib of the back and its knots, which already begins to rise above the other ribs.
When therefore you see that and wish to do it, then cauterize that with a cauterizing needle which is a circle in this form.
And he should take the cauterizing needle over every part of the rib equally: and if you wish to cauterize around the rib with a pointed cauterizing needle two lines, or three: and they should be close together.
Then care for the place, until he is healed with that which we said.
And beware, that you do not give the cauterizing needle in gibbosity, which is made in a spasm of the nerve.
On the method of cauterizing in gout, and pains of the joints.
When pains of the joints are from cold humors, which are poured out to each limb of the body, then when they occur in the feet, it is according to the custom of physicians, that they call that gout properly.
When, therefore, podagra (gout) of a cold cause is being treated and the pains are not removed, then the burning instrument will remove them.
And it is, that after the evacuation around the joint of the foot, with many burnings, the burning instrument should be olive oil.
And if you lack to make pricks on the face of the foot, then make with the burning instrument a prick. But if the pains ascend up to the knees, or other joints, and this often happens, then burn it over all the knee with three burnings, or four from every part, with this same burning instrument the Hamstring.
But if you need more of this burning instrument to you, then burn it. And do not submerge your hand with the burning instrument, but rather it should be about the thickness of the skin only.
But if the pains ascend up to the knees and back: then give what we said from the burning instrument in its chapter.
But if the pains are only in the hands: then make pricks around the wrist, as two lines turn.
But if there remains from the pains in the fingers: then make pricks on each joint of the finger, and on the palm of the hand.
But if the pains ascend up to the elbows, or shoulders: then burn both from every part.
And do not evacuate the weak from good regimen, from receipt of medicines. For if good regimen is made, and the phlegm is evacuated, it will be healed with the help of God with this burning instrument.
¶ On the method of burning in ruptures.
When a rupture occurs in the groin and the intestine or bladder descends to the testicle, and it is near the beginning: then you should order the sick person to abstain from eating on that day. And let him use laxatives so that feces may descend from his intestines.
Then let him sit between your hands on his back: and order him to hold his breath until the bladder or intestine appears.
Then let him reduce it with your fingers, and mark with a hot iron under the rupture on the edge of the lip, with a sign whose extremity is similar to the middle of a circle towards the upper part of the body.
Then let him heat the iron, whose shape is as follows, until it becomes white, and then throw sparks. Then let him reduce the intestine or bladder to its original shape. Then let him place his hand on the place so that the intestine does not exit: and you have already opened between the legs of the sick person, and placed under it a pillow, and another servant on his legs, and another on his chest who holds the hand.
Then let him place the iron on the sign, with your hand holding the iron upright. And hold him until you reach the mouth with it: or repeat with it another time if you did not reach the mouth with it the first time up to the mouth.
And carefully observe from the exit of the intestine during your cauterization, lest you burn it and cause harm or death or great evil through it on the sick person.
And know that when you cannot find a cautery, your operation is not complete.
And it is necessary for the cautery to be delicate for children, according to their size.
Then care with other ointments until it heals.
And let him be weak lying on his back for forty days, until the wound is sealed.
And it is necessary to give him food of a length of time for his healing, which soothes his belly: so that the intestine does not exit during defecation and excretion.
Then when he wants to get up after forty days, then give him a well-made bandage, and hold it for another forty days.
And reduce his labor, and food and drink intake, and violent voices.
For when he uses this regimen, thus heals completely with healing.
And I will tell the healing of ruptures with incision in his chapter.
When however the rupture occurs in the remaining belly, and they are beginning, and you want not to add, then cauterize his rupture with a round cautery according to its quantity: and let that which is burned from then be like the third of it. Then care for him, with what we said: and he should not be added.
And now some have said: to cauterize the rupture with a triangular cautery, according to this form.
After it is signed with encaustic, and a line is placed which is through the width in the upper side of the rupture, and another line to the lower. And place your hand in the middle with the cautery closed.
But the first cautery is easier and better.
In the case of pain due to a wound or blow, this is the method of cauterization.
Chapter 48.
When it happens to certain members due to a wound or blow, and the pain persists for a long time and does not improve with medication, then it is necessary to cauterize with a pointed cautery.
And the cautery should be of a size and strength appropriate to the member, its weakness, its power, its twisting, and the pain caused by it.
If therefore it is healed by the first cauterization, it is good. If not: then repeat the cauterization on it.
Because of the habit of these pains, they often change from one member to another that is close to it. Therefore it is necessary to follow them with a cautery until the sick member is healed.
In the case of leprosy, this is the method of cauterization.
Sometimes leprosy is healed by the greatest cauterization. Especially the kind of leprosy that is caused by the putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy, when you want to cauterize it, consider.
If therefore the leprosy is incurable, and you have treated it with what we said in the division, and it has not descended nor stood still, and you fear that corruption will spread over the whole of its complexion: then cauterize it on the head five times: one in the middle of the head, and the second below towards the front of the hair, and two on the two horns, and one behind on the nape of the neck.
And finally your hand with the cautery a little, until it imprints a small impression on the mouth, and the skin is loosened: so that the heavy breathing of the vapors is relieved, and cauterize also on the spleen, according to what preceded.
If the leprosy has already spread over the sick person and is manifestly visible, then it is necessary to cauterize with these cauteries, which we mentioned at the beginning, and with a cauterizer on the tip of the nose, and with two cauterizers on the two maxillae, and with two cauterizers on the spines of the neck, and six on the spines of the back, and one large one on the buttocks and one above it, in the middle of the buttocks: and two on the knees: one on each knee, and two on the shoulders, and two on the elbows, and two on the tendons of his chest: and cauterize him over every joint, from the joints of his fingers of his hands and feet: and cauterize over every heel of his feet, and the wrists of his hands.
And beware of the nerves that are on the back of the last heel, so that you do not burn them.
And sometimes cauterize with a cauterizer on the beak of the tongue, and another on the mouth, and another on the esophagus.
And know that the more you add a cauterizer, the greater the relief and the better it helps.
And know that the sick person does not feel pain from the cauterizer, as healthy people do: because his body is already numb.
And it is necessary that the cauterizers be of a size and shape according to the limbs and joints: as was previously specified from the types of tools.
Then care for the cauterizer with flour of herb mixed with honey, and the rest of the cure, until he is healed.
¶ On the method of cauterizing in a stupor.
When a certain limb is numb and is treated with medicines, oils, and plasters, but does not heal, then burn that numb limb with cauteries, according to the size or extent of the limb.
And let your cautery penetrate slightly into the thickness of the skin. Then care for it with ointment until it heals.
And sometimes cauterize it for a certain numbness that occurs in the hand, and foot, on the spine at the exit of the nerves that move that limb: and the numbness will be removed.
But do not presume over it, unless he is wise in the anatomy of limbs, and the exit of nerves that move the body.
Chapter 61.
When Albaras is not covered with anything from the skills of medicine: then cauterize it slightly on that deep cautery, according to the thickness of the skin, until the whiteness is removed, and its color changes.
Then care for it with flour of herb, and lentils with rose oil, and leaves of arnoglossa, and blood of dove, and blood of goose: each of these is one part: mix all these, and they will be poured on cloth, and adhere to the place, until it heals.
On the method of cauterizing in Cancer.
When cancer is beginning, and you want to stop it: then cauterize it with a circular cautery around it, as it turns.
But wise men say, that it should be cauterized with the last cautery in the middle.
To me, however, it does not appear that way: for I fear lest it should fester: and I have seen this thing often enough.
It is indeed better, to cauterize around it with a circle, as we said: or with many cautery-irons.
On the method of cauterizing in Albucasis.
When someone has Albucasis, and the maturation is delayed, either because of excessive bleeding which he causes, or because of old age, when he is an infirm old man with little blood, or because of time, and you wish to hasten the maturation of Albucasis, then cauterize around it with many small cautery-irons by pricking. Then let it go. For it will hasten with the maturation.
But if you wish to make a perforation in it with a cautery, then use a cautery-iron of this form.
And place it in the middle of Albucasis, until it penetrates the skin: and let the cautery-iron be weak from that which follows, to ease the course of the pure.
Then care for it until it is healed.
On the method of cauterizing in a corroding wound.
Chapter LXXXIV.
A corroding wound is not other than a corruption in a moving member, and it corrodes it: just as fire consumes dry wood.
If therefore you see a corroding wound in a place which can bear a cautery-iron with fire, then use many cautery-irons, small and large, according to what is suitable for that place where the corroding wound is.
Then cauterize it from all parts until the whole root of the corruption is removed, and nothing remains of it entirely.
Then let him rest for three days, and apply powdered sulfur mixed with oil to the cauterized areas until all the scabs are removed and all corruption is eliminated.
Then care for him with flesh-generating ointments.
If therefore you see that after three days flesh is growing in a healthy manner, free from corruption, it is good.
And if not: then repeat the cauterization on what remains of the corrupted areas.
And apply a sharp medicine when necessary for corrosion. For it rises in the place of the cauterization.
However, the cauterization with fire is a faster method of healing: and indeed I have already spoken of its division with sharp medicine; therefore take it there when you need it.
Of the method of cauterization in Claus and Verucis.
Chapter 50.
Frequently it happens in the lower parts of the feet that this ailment occurs: and it is a rough, running sore that injures the foot.
And indeed the cauterization in them is according to two methods: cauterization with fire, and cauterization with hot water.
However, when with fire, it is made like a hollow feather of a pen: which is made from iron, according to the amount that it contains the claw on all sides: and it is thin at the edge.
Then place it burning on the claw. Then turn your hand with the cauterization around the claw, until the cauterization reaches the depth of the claw: and let him rest for three days, until it begins to emit pus. Then apply plasters of your choice with sulfur, crushed with salt: and let the plaster be applied to him at night. He will be uprooted from his roots.
Then care for the wound with a generative flesh ointment until it heals.
If they are not converted and often occur on the surface of the body, especially on the hands and feet: then apply heat to them with hot water: and take a cannula from the air, or iron, or from the feather of a turkey dove: and place it on the hole, or althelul. Then throw in the cannula from hot water a small amount: hold your hand and turn it with your hand compression for a while, so that the edge of the cannula is pressed into the root of the nail, and the hot water finds a way to the depth, to the root of the nail: and wait for the weak one for an hour on the sting of hot water.
Then let him go, for the nail is uprooted with its roots.
So do with them one after another, until you come over all who are from them on the body.
Then care for them after they are uprooted with that which generates flesh from ointments.
¶ On the method of cauterizing in Tremor.
When it happens to someone with tremor from cold in the nerve, or from quartan fever, or from something else: then it is necessary to cauterize him with four or five cauteries on the spines of the back, and between every spine a cauterization, and in his chest a cauterization, and on his stomach a cauterization.
For the tremor is quiet with the oil cauterization, and hastens the health of the cold sickness.
¶ On the method of cauterizing Albathir.
Chapter 57.
Sometimes foul blisters, that is, boils, are expelled from the body, which arise from corrupted coarse matters.
Therefore, when they appear, they should be cauterized over the entire head of the blister with a thin cautery and with myrtle wood, whose end is burned with fire. Or with the root of long-leaved achillea. Or with a lens-shaped cautery.
And sometimes they are cauterized in this manner at the beginning of their expulsion: and they do not increase: and the excess is broken, which causes them, and they are cured from them.
However, it must be done after evacuation with venesection.
Of the manner of cauterizing in the flow of blood from the artery in a wound.
Many times it happens that the flow of blood from an artery which has been cut at a wound, which happens externally, or at the incision of an abscess, or a cauterizing iron on the member, and similar things to them: and it is difficult to remove it.
When therefore it happens to someone that thing, then hasten with your hand to the opening of the artery, and place on top of it your finger: and press it much, until the blood is blocked under your finger, and nothing comes out from it.
Then place on the small cautery of wax and many more: and blow on them until they are burned greatly.
Then take from them one, or a few, or many, according to the wound and the place in which the artery is broken, and place the cautery on the vein, after which you remove your finger quickly: and hold the cautery until the blood is cut.
If the thorn is expelled from the wound and the finger is cut off from the opening of the artery, and the heated iron is extinguished, then take another heated iron quickly, from the irons that are prepared in the fire.
Therefore do not cease to do this with one after another, until the blood stops flowing.
And beware, lest you burn the nerves which are there, and another evil may occur on the weak part.
And know that when blood flows from the artery, then it is impossible to remove it: especially when the artery is large, unless with one of four methods. Or with an iron, as we said. Or with the extraction, when it is not extracted. For when it is extracted, the ends of it are contracted, and the blood is cut off. Or it is tied with a strong ligature. Or medicines of proper property are placed on it, which is to cut off the blood and tie with a decent compression.
But whoever administers the cutting of it with a ligature and tying with a cloth, or the position of things that burn and similar, does not give it to him completely, unless rarely.
But if something happens to him of that, and he is not present with a physician or medicine: then he begins with the position of the finger index over the opening of the vein itself, as we have said, and the compression of it greatly, until the blood is blocked from the upper part of the wound, and on the artery. And the finger is not removed, above it with cold water of great cold always, until the blood freezes, and thickens, and is cut off.
And meanwhile he considers in it what is needed from the iron, or from the medicine.
On Incisions, Punctures, and Bloodletting in Wounds and Similar Cases.
We have already mentioned in Chapter One that all pain which is suitable for the use of a cauterizing fire and burning medicine, along with its causes, reasons, instruments, and forms of cauterization.
And I placed chapters from head to foot there.
And I proceed in this chapter the same way: so that it may alleviate those seeking the sought.
And before I begin that, it is necessary for you to learn, son, what is in this chapter from the fear of that which is in Chapter One about cauterization.
And for that reason, it is necessary to have greater caution in it, because in the operation which is in this chapter, often falls evacuation with blood, with which stands life at the opening of the vein, or incision over an abscess, or opening of exit, or cure of wound, or extraction of arrow, or incision on stone, and from all these, it is associated with trembling, and fear, and falls in many of them death.
And I advise you not to fall into that in which is hesitation, for sometimes such people come to you in this art with such ways of men and their weaknesses. For from them is he who is angry with his pain, and is light in him towards death: because of the vehemence of it which he found from his weakness and length of his malice. And with pain is from fear which signifies death.
And from them is he who gives his song, and enriches you with it, hoping for health, and his pain is destructive.
Therefore, it is not necessary to consent to him who comes to you from among them whose manner is such. And your caution should be more urgent than your greed and your ravenousness. And do not presume upon anything from him unless after a certain certain knowledge which verifies with you that succession is praiseworthy to which he arrives.
And use them in the treatment of all your sick, for diagnosis and indication of what is fittingly for their health.
For in him is to you a helper for the acquisition of fame and glory, and memory and praise.
May God breathe into you, O son, his understanding, and not take from you direction and inspiration: for that is in his hand.
And indeed I have arranged this Chapter by distinguishing it into chapters, according to what preceded in the chapter of Cauterization, from the scalp to the feet: so that it may be alleviated to you what you seek from him and what you need.
¶ On the treatment of water that gathers in the heads of children.
Chapter I.
Know that this infirmity often occurs to children at birth: or when the midwife tightly binds the head of the child without gentleness.
And also when it happens for an unknown cause which is not known.
And indeed I have not seen this ailment in other than children: and to all of whom I have seen from them hasten death: therefore it seemed to me to leave the operation in it.
And indeed I have seen from them a child whose head was filled with water, and his head was glorified every day, until he could not sit on himself, because of the greatness of his own head: and the moisture increased, until he died.
This moisture either accumulates between the skin and bone, or beneath the bone above the sinew.
And if the operation is performed on moisture between the skin and bone, and it is a small abscess, then it is necessary to make a cut in the middle of the head, one in width, and the length of the cut should be like two nodes, until the moisture is drained.
This is the shape of the incision.
If therefore the moisture is more increased, and the abscess is larger, then place these two cuts, according to this form.
And if the moisture is beneath the bone, and the sign of it is, that you see the edges of the head open from all parts: and water is pressed when you press it with your hand to the insides, and it does not hide itself from you, then it is necessary to make three cuts in the middle of the head, according to this manner.
And after the incision, extract all the moisture. Then bind the cuts with cloths and cotton. Then rub it above with wine and oil until the fifth day.
Then dissolve the ligament, and care for the wound with compresses, and ointments.
And do not dismiss binding the head with equality. And feed the sick person with all food dry and little moisture, until the limb is strengthened and healed.
And another manner of incision is, that you consider where the size of the abscess appears, and the collection of water.
For when it is often in the back, or in the forehead, or on the right, or on the left.
Therefore ascend with the incision where the abscess appears to you and is full of water: and cut it according to what is possible for you.
And observe, lest you cut the artery, and blood flow occurs, and the sick person dies from that flow with the discharge of moisture.
On the incision of arteries which are after the ears.
Chapter 2.
When a person has a catarrh to the eyes, or to the chest, and that is not cured by medical treatment: then the last cure for that person is the incision of those two arteries.
Therefore when you wish to incise them, it is necessary that the sick person bend his head. Then rub the place with a rough cloth, so that the arteries appear. Then the sick person ties his neck with any of his cloths. Then consider where the vein pulses. And the locations of both are locations which are after the ears depressed: and it is rarely hidden, unless in some men.
Then mark with a hot iron on both: and incise both with a narrow knife on each side, the incision going to the bone: and let that be done across the width of the head.
And if you wish, insert a narrow knife under the artery, and incise it to the upper part with the incision.
And let the length of the incision be like two fingers joined together.
For when the vein is incised, blood escapes with a pulsating flow, which jumps to the inside frequently.
But if the artery does not appear to the senses, then it is necessary that you measure from the ear the distance of three fingers. Then mark with a hot iron, and incise until the bone.
And that which is to be emitted from the blood is six unciae, and perhaps you may emit more or less from it. According to the appearance of the quantity that seems to you due to the weakness of the patient and the filling of his artery, do that.
Then consider the wound. Then if there remains at the bone from the siphon anything, then cut that, so that it does not happen that a hot abscess occurs: then bind the wound with lint from a cloth.
Then care for him with ointment until he is healed.
¶ About the extraction of arteries that are in the temples.
Chapter 3.
When it happens to a man that he has ancient hemicrania, or sharp catarrh because of acrid humors, and heat in the temples, or old bile, strong, and similar to those: and he is treated with the methods of cure of medicine, and does not bear it: then we have experienced these ailments extraction of arteries from the temples, or cauterization of them, as we have narrated.
And the method of operation in their extraction is, that the sick one shaves the hairs that are in the temples, and directs himself to the artery that appears in the temple. For indeed it is shown to you from his pulse, and rarely is hidden unless in a few men, or because of the vehemence of cold.
But if it is hidden from you, then the sick one binds his head with any of his cloths: then he rubs the place with a rough cloth. Or steam the place with hot water, until it appears to you by a clear appearance. Then take the little lancet, which I formed a little before. Then scrape with it the skin with ease, until you reach the artery. Then thrust in it a hook, and extract it towards the upper parts, until you have extracted it from the skin, and make it go away from the garments that are under it from every part.
If however the artery is thin: then cover it with the tip of the needle. Then cut from that part according to the length at which their tips contract and do not cause blood flow. For if it does not cut and if it is not cut off, the blood will not rise completely.
Then evacuate from the blood six ounces, up to three.
If however the artery is large: then it is necessary to tie it in two places with a strong double thread of silk or of hair, as not to rush to its putrefaction before the consolidation of the wound and that blood flow does not occur.
Then cut the superfluity which is between the two knots. Do this at that hour or after another hour.
And if you wish, cauterize it with a cauterizer up to the bone, with a scalpel, until their tips cut and it stands in the place of that work.
And it is better work, unless if he is weak and has a fever or of hot constitution. Because the cauterizer is of those that help to end moistures. Therefore it is a better remedy.
And after the extraction of the arteries, the place should be filled with old cautery: and they should be placed on it well-made pads.
And after the solution, it should be treated with dry medicines that make flesh grow and with liniments until it is healed.
If however in the meantime while you are operating blood flow occurs from the artery, then rush to cut it with a cauterizer or to fill the place with zeolite: and hold your hand, until the blood is cut off. If nothing of those is present with you, then place it on the place of your finger until the blood congeals. And rub the place with strong cold water until the sharpness subsides and it contracts as it should.
And because it is lighter and easier to extract the artery, it has a cauterizing knife with this cauterizer having two blades: let the sharpness of the two blades be like alum. However, they are much less sharp than two knives. Since if they are as sharp as two knives, each freezes quickly: and they do not cut the flesh with speed. But since there is a little thickness in them, the heat of the fire is held in them, and the flesh is cut quickly: therefore it is better for every work, and lighter and easier.
And this is the form of the cauterizer.
And let there be a space between the two blades that is as thick as the thickness of your finger, after you have marked two places with the cauterizer: and put both hot ones, until they reach the bone, and cut the vein in two places: so that it is lengthened between its ends. For they do not harden completely with this cauterizer.
Chapter IV.
¶ On the care of the course of sharp and frequent tears from the eyes.
When the tears are frequent and their course is from the eyes which are above the skull externally: and nothing of medicine is applied to them with other medicines, and you see the face of the sick already red, and feels in his forehead a walk, as if it were the walking of ants: and his eyes are weakened, humid, so that already the hair on them has been worn away by corrosion: and his eyelids are heated from the sharpness of the tears: then the ancients needed in their cure of these this operation, and called it a cure with the Sword.
And it is, that you command the sick one to shave the hairs that are on his forehead. Then, you should make three evenly spaced incisions across the forehead according to its length: and let the length of the incision be about two fingers, and one incision should be evenly spaced with the length of the nose in the middle of the forehead, and the second according to the length slightly above the shoulder blades, and the third on the other side: and beware of the incision of the arteries that are on both sides: and extend your hand away from the continuity of the two jaws, and let the entire length of the incision be about three fingers joined together: and let there be a prepared piece of sponge or dry cloth with which to absorb the blood.
Then, insert a two-bladed sharp instrument, of which the following is its shape. From the incision that is on the temple side, up to the second incision: and scrape off with it all the skin that is between the two incisions, along with the sphincter, which is above the bone. Then do the same from the middle incision up to the second incision. Then remove this instrument and insert another instrument, called a sharp-edged knife, from one side gently, not sharply from the other side. And this is its shape.
And place its sharp side towards the flesh and skin, and its gentle side towards the bone: and push it until it reaches the middle incision: and cut off with it all the vessels that descend from the head to the eyes: except that the incision continues up to what appears of the skin.
Then do the same in the middle incision up to another incision.
After an equal amount of blood has flowed out, press the areas where the clotted blood is located.
Then place linen soaked in old cooked linseed in every crack, and place on top of them damp cloths soaked in wine, oil, or vinegar. And be sure that the abscess does not become hot.
And on the third day dissolve the bandage, and administer a large infusion with warm water. Then care for it with basilicon ointment, and with other remedies used to treat wounds: until it heals.
Chapter 5.
¶ On the care of sharp tears and catarrh from the interior of the head to the eyes.
When sharp catarrh occurs to someone frequently, sharply, and constantly: and you see his eyes weakened, small, and already weakened in appearance: and the eyelids are ulcerated, and hairs fall out from them, and there is a sharp pain in the depth of the head, wounding, and following sneezing: then take from these accidents that those materials, and catarrh do not come, except from many vices.
And a better cure for them is this. And it is, that you command the sick person to shave his forehead. Then cut one incision in the middle of his forehead, or another a little wider in width, and begin with the incision from the left temple to the right temple: and let the incision be up to the bone: and keep your hand away from the moving jaws at chewing: until when the bone is exposed: and dry all the blood with a sponge.
Then separate between two lips of the incision with old cooked linseed, or with linen cloths. Then tie it above with swabs: and drink swabs with wine and oil, so that no heat abscess may occur.
And when you untie it, and see that the heat abscess is already diminishing: then it is necessary to knead the mouth, until flesh begins to grow in it.
Then care for it with an evaporating regimen that causes flesh to grow: as if you take two parts of wheat flour and four parts of pitch: and prepare a plaster from them, and administer it to the birth of flesh in these wounds.
Chapter 6.
¶ On the care of that which falls into the Ear.
Everything that falls into the ear is one of four kinds: either a mineral stone, or a stone like it, such as iron and flint: or it is from a plant, such as peas and beans: or it is a fluid, such as water, and vinegar, and the like: or some animal.
When therefore a stone, or kind of stone from those which do not add and grow in the ear, falls into the ear, expose the Ear alone: if therefore you see the stone, then pour something from broken oil, or sawdust, into the Ear. Then administer its extraction, and make him sneeze with the condensed [substance], and open the nose with an onion at the approach of sneezing, after you have placed in the vicinity of the ear fragments of cloth, or wool, and extend the ear to the superior [part].
Often indeed it goes out with this care.
If however it does not go out, then administer its extraction with Gesti, that is, finely ground pizzarol: whose form is this.
If he goes out with his clothes on, it is good.
And if not, then administer the extraction of his tooth with a blunt-ended, fine, thin hook of few doublings.
If he does not come out through that, then make a canula of air, and insert the end of the canula into the ear hole a lot, and put a softened piece of clay with oil around the canula so that there is no wind except for the canula: then extract it with your strong attraction.
Very often he comes out with what we have mentioned. But if he does not come out this way: then take from helkalimbat, or from visco, that is, prepared glue with which birds are caught, a small amount: and put it on the end of the radius after you have wrapped it in a cloth properly placed: then insert it into the ear hole when you have dried the ear from moisture.
If he does not come out with all that we have mentioned, then hurry to break it before an abscess of hot pus, or spasm, occurs.
And the method of incision is, that you use a lancet on the weak one in the first place in the cephalic: and extract it from his blood according to the measure of its strength. Then make the weak one sit between your hands, and turn his ear to the superior parts, and make a small incision in the root of the ear at the fatty part of him in the depressed place: and let the incision be in the shape of a crescent moon until you reach the stone: then take it with that which is possible from your instruments.
Then sew his incision from your hour with speed, and care for it until he is healed.
If what falling into the ear is from one of the grains that grow and swell: then administer the extraction of it.
If it still does not obey you at the end, then take a thin, delicate spatula in this form.
And administer with it the incision of that kind from the grains that fall into your ear, and do not do it when you think that that grain is already moistened by the vapor of the ear, until you place many pieces of it: then extract them with hooks, or with a thin instrument, or with suction, as we said, for its extraction is relieved.
But in the water that enters your ear, it is necessary to use a weak sneezing with the disinfected first: and now it has filled its own ear with a little old cooked one: and it is lying on that ear, in which there is water. Therefore if it comes out through that, it is good.
And if not: then take many stones, according to the length of your finger, thin, gentle, and heat them with fire for a while, and the weak one inserts one of them into the hole of its ear: and he salts one of his feet from that part, and strikes with another stone on the stone that is in the ear. Therefore do not stop doing it with the stone and the stone until all the water comes out.
And now the water comes out so that you take one from the parpyro, or from the junco, and insert one of its ends into your ear: and light the other end with fire, until it is burned a lot of it. Then repeat the junco again, and do it many times, until all the water comes out: and extract it with a cannula as was prescribed in the stone.
But in the extraction of the animal that enters it, if it is small of body, like a flea, and similar to it, care for it as I said in division.
However, if it is a large body part that is visible to the senses: then perform its extraction with forceps and hooks, and its removal is easier than all those held in the ear.
However, in the extraction of worms generated in the ear, when you care for it with what we mentioned in division and in the treatment of distillations, and your cure does not combine: then you must look at the ear in the sunlight. Therefore, if something appears there from the worms, then extract it with forceps or with fine hooks.
But if nothing appears there, then take a cannula, whose form is this: narrow below, wide above: and insert its fine end into the ear according to the amount that an infirm person can bear: then suck with it strong suction. Do this many times, until all the worms come out.
But if they do not obey you to exit, then wrap the cannula with ash, as I said in the stone.
But if they do not come out with that which we said: then perform distillations which the ancients have been experienced in in the piercing of worms: and you will find it in the treatment of distillations.
And let your effusion be what you pour out oil and medicines into the ear with this instrument, whose form is depicted here. Just as you see make it from silver, or from brass, below narrow, in which there is a small hole, wide above.
Therefore let the pushing that is in the hollow of the cannula be made from brass properly. And if you wish, take a ray, and wrap it in the end of it with a proper wrapping: then project oil, or succum, or whatever you want from these medicines into the cannula: and it is in the ear: then insert the ray with cotton above, and press it gently by your hand until the oil is pushed into the hollow of the ear, and he feels it inside: and that which is poured into the ear should be already warmed with a little fire: and beware that what is distilled into it is not very cold: for medicines do not tolerate that.
Chapter VII.
¶ On the care of the accidental wounding of Gold (possibly a reference to gold fillings or dental work).
Sometimes, certain infants emerge from their mother's wombs unharmed, not having been pierced.
And it also happens to some men that the wounding of the ear occurs in the opening of the ear due to an injury or flesh born in it.
And this wounding of the ear sometimes occurs in the deep opening of the ear, which vision does not reach: and sometimes it happens to the outer part of the opening, and vision reaches it.
Therefore, that which happens in the deep part of the ear, and which does not include the scope of vision, is often difficult to heal in many positions.
And in that which vision reaches, it is necessary to place the ear of the sick person in the sun, and look at it: then if you see the wounding appearing, open it with a thin, subtle spatula, whose form is as follows: its end is small, and has a slight width; and the rest of the spatula is two-sided, smooth: so that it does not hurt the ear.
If therefore the wounding is born from flesh in the opening of the ear: then hold it with a thin tweezer, and cut it with great force until all the flesh is removed.
If the wounding is in the deep part of the ear: then take a thin, smooth, warm needle, and heat it with a small fire: then put it into the opening of the ear.
If therefore you feel the wounding with that which the sick person has, when he has great difficulty hearing, try to open it with ease: and beware, lest you wound the nerves of the ear.
Then place in the ear, linen according to the quantity of the foramen's width, which you have soaked in Egyptian ointment. Make it for several days until you are secure about the consolidation of the wound.
Or take linen and soak it in rosewater, and sprinkle powdered zeig on it, and use it thus.
If you see that the ear is already abscessing, then it is necessary to remove the linen and let it with another piece of linen, which you have soaked in rose oil, until the abscess sits warm: then care for it until it heals.
But if bleeding occurs, then immerse a sponge or cloth in cold water and place it on the ear: and use the remaining cure, which stops the aforementioned blood flow in the treatment of distillations.
¶ On the care of Althaea's eyelids.
Chapter 8.
These Althaea's which occur in the eyelids of the eye, sometimes are moist, and sometimes are dry.
Therefore you must hold them with tweezers: or with an unguent, and cut them with a lancet from their roots. Then place powdered zeig on the spots.
But if blood flows from them, then cauterize them with a fine lens cauterizer.
And to cauterize them is better after the incision. For often they return when something remains from their roots. And when they are cauterized with fire, those roots burn and do not return.
¶ On the care of Granatum's eyelids of the eye.
Chapter IX.
It frequently happens that something similar to a storm (Grando) occurs in the eyelids due to its strength and hardness, and because of this it is called Grando. It is an accumulation of thick moisture above the upper eyelid and below the lower eyelid.
Therefore, the operation in this case is to consider whether it is Grando that is proceeding from what appears from the eyelid and moves to all parts, and its nature is easy.
Therefore, find a cut above it in width. Then scrape it from all parts with ease until it becomes smooth. Then suspend it with a probe and cut it off.
But if the cut of it is not prepared for you unless after you penetrate the eyelid with an incision a little, then it harms the weak one in some way.
But if the cut is large, then gather it with a suture and care for it until it heals.
And if it is small, you will not encounter harm from it. For the ointment restores it and fleshens it.
And if Grando is declining towards the inner parts of the ear towards the inner surface, then turn the eyelid and suspend the Grando with a probe: but you will need an incision and press it from all parts.
But if the eyelid is lengthened by an incision, it does not harm it in some way.
Then wash the eye after the cut of Grando with salt water: and care for the place with it that fleshens until the weak one heals.
¶ On the care of Axirnath of the eyelids.
Chapter X.
Axirnath is a fatty substance that forms in the eyelids of the upper eyelid: and it particularly affects children: and it makes their eyes heavy, and they get cataracts in the mornings, and they cannot see the light of the sun, because their tears rush to them, and because of this you see them lying on their faces all the time, and they sleep on them, and their eyelids are wet under the swollen eyebrows, which has already been covered by inflation: and the protrusion of Axirnath is visible to the eye, and when you press it with your fingers, you feel Axirnath between them.
And the method of operation for this is that the sick person puts his head on your lap.
Then take a linen cloth and prepare linseed in it, and make a circle from it of the size that contains Axirnath from all sides. Then place him on it, and press with your fingers from all sides, so that Axirnath is gathered in the middle of the circle.
Then find in the middle of that moisture with a sharp lancet making incisions of width, and let there be no incision larger than that which is made in phlebotomy in depth.
Or it is necessary to make an incision in the whole skin, until you reach Axirnath, for in many arrangements Axirnath proceeds from the incision according to the shape of a white fat slice.
Then extract it with the cloth that you have placed between your fingers to the outside: and you turn your hand to the right and left, until it is spread: and beware, do not add to the incision, so that it does not reach with the lancet to the eye, and you hurt him.
If, however, Axirnath does not appear to you at the beginning of the incision, you will add it with some ease into the incision until Axirnath proceeds. Then extract it, as we said.
Then immerse the cloths in vinegar and water, and place them on the spot, and bind it with bandages.
And there are some who apply salt to it, and place it in the hollow of the incision, so that what remains from that moisture may melt.
Then care for it, until it is healed.
But if an abscess occurs in that place, then care for it with soothing plasters, until it is healed.
CONCERNING THE WAYS OF ATAXMIR'S EYES, THAT IS, WHEN THE EYEBEAM SOFTENS THE EYES, WHEREBY IT BECOMES SUCH THAT IT TEARS AS IT SHOULD NOT.
CHAPTER 11.
WHEN ADDITIONAL HAIR IS BORN IN THE EYEBEAMS BEYOND ITS NATURAL COURSE UNDER THE HAIR, AND IT AGES: THEN IT HARMS THE EYE, AND CAUSES THE ONSET OF AILMENTS, SUCH AS FREQUENT TEARS, AND SOFTENING OF THE EYEBEAMS, AND WHITE OF THE EYE, UNTIL THAT BECOMES THE CAUSE OF DESTRUCTION OF THE EYE.
AND ATAXMIR'S EYES ARE CURED ACCORDING TO FOUR WAYS. OR BY CAUTERIZATION WITH FIRE. OR WITH ACUTE MEDICINE, AS PREVIOUSLY STATED IN THE CHAPTER ON CAUTERIZATION. OR ATAXMIR'S EYES ARE CURED BY INCISION AND SUTURING. OR BY CANNULAS, AS I WILL SAY.
IT IS NECESSARY TO PLACE THE HEAD OF THE INFIRM ON YOUR BOSOM. Then turn the eyelid of the eye with your left hand.
If it is turned, it is good. And if not: insert the needle into it, where the thread is from the lower part of the eyelid, and make the needle penetrate with the thread from above, and let it be near the hairs, that is, near the margin of the eyelid, where the hairs grow: and pull the thread upwards with the eyelid, and turn it with a forceps.
Then find in the inner part of the eyelid under the added hairs with a probe entering from the larger lacrimal canal up to the smaller one.
Then remove the thread, and place a small amount of cotton or cloth under the eyelid: then mark on the eyelid with a cauterizer, which is like the shape of a myrtle leaf.
However, it must be made like the shape according to the quantity and elevation of the eyelid: because it is already varied among men.
For there are those who need that a large amount of it should enter from the eyelid according to the quantity which is softened from the eyelid.
Then with a probe find above two lines which you marked, and begin from the larger lacrimal canal up to the smaller one, and let there be a slit near the natural hairs, like the size of the radius.
Then insert a hook into one of the two angles of the skin. Then scrape it all off. Then gather it with a suture two lips, with a needle and fine wool thread: and wipe off the blood, and make what is superfluous from the threads over two eyebrows, with some things that cover, if you want to do that: and if not, do not care.
Then let go of the suture and thread for three days, or four; afterwards care for that.
And if you wish, let go of the wound without suture, and care for it along with that which dries and constricts. For the eyelid is raised at the sign of the wound and its union: but a better one is to come.
This method of healing, the ancients taught Ataxmir.
However, there is anxiety over the weak one, and it is from good operation, and there is not in it fear.
And another method is in Ataxmir also: and it is, that the signs above the eyelid are shaped like a figure, which is like the figure of myrtle leaves, as we have told.
Then raise the eyelid with three separate or joined needles, according to this following form, then cut off what exceeds with small scissors, according to this form, with equality of incision.
But if it is not possible for you to hold the needle, and it is not equal: then take a needle in which is thread, and insert it in the middle of the figure: and insert another thread near the lacrimal larger, and thread near the lacrimal smaller: and gather the threads with equality between your fingers.
Then raise your hand evenly: and raise the skin over which is marked with the sign, as we have told.
Then gather two lips of the wound with suture: and care for it, until it is healed.
But if indeed abscess happens at your incision, or your wound: dry up that abscess with charcoal, and with these similar, from ointments suppressing.

Therefore, you should use what we mentioned in the incision in that [place], but a stitch on both sides is more artificial. On the care of Ataxmir with dogs.

THEN YOU SHOULD MAKE TWO CANES, OR TWO THIN WOODEN STICKS: THE LENGTH OF WHICH SHOULD BE ACCORDING TO THE LENGTH OF THE EYELID, AND THE WIDTH LESS THAN THE WIDTH OF A FINGER: AND YOU ALREADY INCISED IN THE EXTREMITIES OF BOTH FROM BOTH SIDES WHERE YOU HOLD THE THREADS.

IF HOWEVER IT DELAYS, THEN CUT IT WITH FORCEPS. THEN CARE FOR IT, UNTIL IT HEALS.
WHEN HOWEVER IT CONSOLIDATES, LIFT THE EYELID: AND DO NOT PICK AT THE HAIR.

¶ On the care of Alexatrati which is made in the lower eyelid, and is a wrinkle or contraction upwards to the right and left.
Chapter 14.

And accidental is caused by a wound, or a cut, or a cauterization, and those similar things.

And the final word on the care of Alexander when it is above or below, is that the operation should be carried out in it, according to how it is prepared from the form of Alexander.
For indeed it is of many diverse forms: and the skilled craftsman prepares his skill with whatever way is possible to him, until he makes the figure return to its natural form, or near to it, and himself the sick person, according to what fits him from the operation and instruments in many dispositions.
Chapter 15.
Translation: Concerning the adherence of the eyelid to the eye, whether it be united with the conjunctiva or the cornea.
Sometimes this adherence occurs to many people in such a way that the upper eyelid becomes united with the white of the eye and prevents it from performing its natural functions.
Therefore, you should insert the tip of the ray under the eyelid and lift it up: or extend it with a spoon: then incise the adherence with a thin, blunt-edged knife, which is not sharp in its incision, but rather dull: so that the weak person does not suffer during the operation, and the knife is removed without damaging the eye with its sharpness: and your incision should be as if you are scraping off the adherence with ease, until when the eyelid returns to its natural form and the adherence is completely healed.
Then pour salt water into the eye with clear water to clean it: or sprinkle it with water from a sponge made of zinc dissolved in water.

Concerning the incision of the nail and the prominence of flesh in the eyes.
Chapter 16.
You should know that the nail is in two ways. Either it is nervous: and it is similar to a sponge hard and thin. Or it is not nervous, similar to the frozen moisture of a white substance: which when it touches the iron, or you try to take it with a knife, it is cut off and does not stick to the knife.
And both species do not begin, except from a larger lacrimal, until it gradually goes, until it covers the sight, and prevents light, and movement of the eye.
And the method of operation in its incision is: that he places his weak head in your lap. Then open his eyes, and raise the eyelid with your hand. Then gather the horn with a few notches of the scalpel, and extend it to the upper parts. Then take a needle, and insert a pin from horsehair, or goose, or chicken feathers: and let it be a strong thread, and double the tip of the needle slightly, and fix it in the middle of the horn: and pierce it with the needle, and tie the horn with the thread, and extend it to the upper parts: and scrape the side of the horn that follows the pupil, as if you were holding it with the pin until the end of its tail.
Then cut the remaining part at the root of the lacrimal with a thin saw, or with small forceps: and let go the natural flesh of the lacrimal, so that it does not happen from its incision that the course of tears is constant.
And sometimes the horn is extended with a single notch of the scalpel: or with a thread, as we said. Then scrape it with a thin saw, which has this form.
And beware, lest the saw touch the horn's skin, and it happens to it a breakage, and pierce the pupil.
Then after the incision, put something salty into the eye, or some powder made from sieves and zinc, and let it go until another day. Then care for him with what is necessary, until he is healed.
If the hoof is not nervous and you cannot insert an awl into it or attach a needle to it, then this type of hoof is often treated with medicines and heals as described in the division.
If you wish to cut it, then open the eye of the sick animal, and take a thin, weak, blunt awl according to this form. And shave the hoof from above with a razor with delicacy. If you see that it is becoming thin and broken, and you press a razor into it, then pour from your hourglass into the eye made from siif, or red siif, or finely ground salt: and oil the eye until another day.
Then repeat the operation on it until all of it is removed. Unless the opposite is true for you in the eye, an abscess of heat: then leave it and treat the abscess until it heals.
Then repeat the operation on it with a razor until it heals.

Then pour in the eyelid siif red, or made from siif, until it heals.
¶ On the incision of Algardhenic, and flesh born in the eye.
Chapter 17.
Flesh sometimes arises in certain human eyes, composed or placed red, until it covers the pupil, or approaches, or stretches over the eyelids, and perhaps turns the eyelids to the outside: and it resembles a rose of balm.
The operation on her is also that she places her sick head in your lap. Then open her eyes and gather all that flesh together with the suitable hooks to that: and hold it with one forceps, or with a pair of tweezers.
Then cut the flesh in the first place, until it ends all of hers with the incisor. When therefore your incision is completed, and all the guard-flesh has been removed, then fill her eye with crushed salt: or sprinkle in it red powder, and similar things to her from corrosive medicines: and place on the eye of the deformed one cotton with egg white: so that it is secured from pus hot.
If however there remains any of the guard-flesh, and hot blood rules you, and you fear pus hot: then let go the eye, and care for him with that which sedates the pus.
Then repeat over him with the operation, until he is healed.
And similarly do with the flesh added which happens in the eye from this kind.
However it is necessary that the treatment of all eyes of the weak person from the natural way, or from the accidental way, operating with iron: and you do not introduce your hand in any of these operations, until you see, that that member is tolerating that operation.
¶ On the collection of Sebel from the eye.
Chapter 18.
Beneath the eyelids are red veins that cover the eye and prevent their own operation, and weaken the eye over time.
Therefore, it is necessary for you to first consider whether the eye in which there is a Sebel is strong and has no other illness besides a Sebel, then gather the Sebel from that eye.
And it is your command to prescribe to the weak one, that he put his head in your lap.
Then suspend those veins with a needle one or two according to your wisdom: and the needle should be thin for suture, in this form, or there should be two needles gradually in one body, in this form.
Then gather those veins with fine forceps with delicacy, and wipe off the blood hour by hour, until you see those veins removed from the eye, and dissolve: and beware of not injuring the eye with the tips of the forceps.

Chapter on the reduction of Arissati to the nose.
Chapter 19.
The physicians call the fistula of Arris, which they treat with a cautery or with a sharp-burning medicine, according to what precedes its description.
And if it is not cured, then there is no skill in it: unless you find above the abscess at its birthplace and remove all the moisture that is in it and the pus, until the opening is cleaned.

If therefore the spot is consolidated and flesh grows in it, and the course of pus is cut off, and it remains for forty days without being renewed or becoming an abscess or any accident happening to it, then you will know that it has been cured.

Therefore then restore the place with astringent ointments, as I taught you.

On the reduction of the protrusion of the Eye.
Chapter 20.
When the eye protrudes with all of it, and no harm occurs in the sight, nor diminution: then you should dissolve the weak one: then you should bleed him: afterwards you should place aerosols in the neck without scarification, but with suction.

On making an incision in the eyelid.
Chapter 21.
When a tear occurs in the eyelid, it protrudes and extends outside the eyelids like a grain of sand, and disfigures the face due to this, and you want to cut it: then the operation on it is as follows: and it is to insert a needle into the root of the eyelid from the lower part to the upper part.
