On the treatment of almonds.
Chapter 22.
This disease which is called almonds, is not, unless it is pus, which collects in the eye, similar to water descending, and it is not itself.
The method of operation in this case is that you should make the infirm person sit on a prepared seat or a straight one.
Then take the head of the person in your hands from both sides and move it until you see health reach the lower parts of your eyes. Then it should be shaped and not go down, and the light should be completed: and the infirm person should see things as he used to: and if it does not go down lower, you will know that it is water.
But if the preparation of the descent of health does not go with what we said, then make the infirm person sit between your hands. Then take a fine lancet and prick with it above the corneal membrane slightly at the continuity of the connected cornea in the crown until the pus comes out.
When it comes out, then pour hot water into the eye in which you mixed honey: or water in which you already boiled fenugreek and honey: then it should be treated with the rest of the cure until he is healed.
¶ On the care of water that goes into the eye, or cataract.
Chapter 23.
Now we have mentioned the appearance of water in division, and what is appropriate for piercing with speech declaring and explaining, then take that same one according to health.
Then therefore you should make the infirm person sit between your hands squarely, facing the light, near the sun: and tie the healthy eye, and tighten it very much: then with your right hand the eyelid of the eye in which is the water, if the eye in which is the water is the left eye: or with your left hand, if the eye is right.
Then take with your right hand a lancet, if the eye is left: or with your left hand, if the eye is right.
Then place the needle near the edge of the cornea, close to the appearance of the radius' thickness in the whiteness of the lachrymal minor: then push the needle with force, and you turn it back with your hand until it penetrates into the sclera of the eye: and feel that the needle has already reached the empty space.
And it should be that the length of the needle is a measure of its journey to the depth, a measure of the space that is from the pupil to the end of the darkness: and it is the edge of the eye. You will see it in the pupil itself, for the clarity of the cornea's tunic.
Then place the needle until it reaches the place where there is water. Then press it down evenly, one after the other.
If therefore water immediately flows down, then the sick person sees it above what opens his sight immediately, and the needle in his eye.
Then rest a little. If therefore water flows down, then lay it down secondly, except that the needle should exit.
When therefore it is stuck, and does not rise: then pull the needle out easily: and you turn back your hand gradually.
Then dissolve some clear salt gem in water: and wash with it the eye from inside. Then place outside the eye all the bandage, or the dyed wool with rose oil, and the sclera of the eye: and tie it with the healthy eye.
But we, and those who are of our time, place on him ground glass with the sclera of the eye.
If therefore the needle does not obey you for entering into the eye because of its hardness, since from men it is, whose eye is very hard: then it is necessary that you take a small spatula, which is called Alberid, of which this is the shape.
Therefore, join the punctured part only, and do not insert your entire hand into the opening; rather, make a path to the subtle location of the almug tree.
Then introduce the almug wood, as we have said.
And at the completion of your work, prepare a properly made bed for the sick person to sleep on his back in a dark house; and he should be prohibited from all movements, and coughing: and place his food which soothes his nature; and he should not move his head with his right hand, nor at all with his left.
And let the bandage be according to his condition up to the third day.
Then dissolve it in that dark house, and test his sight; and make him see things. Then reduce the bandage up to the seventh day.
And it should not be done during the hour of healing, or immediately after the incision: rather, it should be done by others, because water rises quickly through a strong gaze.
But if a boil becomes hot: then it is necessary to dissolve the eye before the seventh day: and correct it with what soothes the boil, until it is soothed: then complete his sight, and place on his face an oral remedy which regulates his sight for several days, while he is still in that dark house.
Then he should exit the house gradually, and return to his own quarters.
And know that in zaltea the student is not exempted from vision several times: then he dares to perform the operation.
And indeed, one of those who are from Alayrach has come to us, who said that it happened in Alayrach that a man was pierced with a magdan, through which water is drawn.
Indeed, I have not seen anyone in your land who has done this: nor have I read it in any of the ancient books: and it is possible that it is new.
And those are the forms of species from the main, so that they stand above those who do not know them.
Let them be made of air properly: and their ends should be with this same subtlety triangular, and the sharp end.
HEAD XXIV.
OF THE CARE OF FLESH BORN IN THE NOSE.
Sometimes flesh is born in the nose of different kinds, from which there is something that resembles a scorpion of many feet: and from it is cancerous flesh, stone-like, of a dark color: and from it is that which is flesh that is soft, not of a dark color.
In that therefore which is from those flesh that is soft, not deceitful, nor cancerous, you should do that the infirm person is placed opposite to you, and open his nose, and thrust a hook into those flesh: then pull them out to the outside, and cut what you have grasped from them with a sharp, thin spatula on one side, until you know that all the flesh is removed.
If something remained from that of whose cutting is not possible: then shave it with one of the instrument's thin with ease, until there is nothing remaining from it. If however the blood rules you, or hot pus falls on you: then place it on him with what is necessary: or it is from malignant abscesses, then hurry to cauterize it, until the blood is cut off, and all the flesh is removed.
Then throw into the nose after incision vinegar, and water, or wine. If the nose opens and moisture flows out from it up to the palate, then you will know that he is already healed.
But if the moisture does not penetrate as it should, then you will know that there is flesh inside him born in the upper nasal bones, to which the instrument did not reach with the incision.
Then therefore you must insert a string with some knots in it and many knots: and between each knot a quantity of a finger, or less: and the weak one should put one end of the string into his nose with a probe, or with whatever is possible for him after he has done so similar to an azzer: and pull out his smell, until it reaches the bone, and comes out over his throat.
And often indeed they do something similar to this to boys in school: and it is an easy thing for him who wants to.
Then put two ends of the string, one end which comes out over the nose, and the other which remains in the nose. Then with a sharp knife cut the flesh with the knots that are on the string. Do this until you know that the flesh is now with the knots of the string.
Then remove the string: and put linen after washing away the blood into the Egyptian ointment which you imbibed: do this for three days, or more, until the ointment has corroded all that remains of the flesh.
Then put at the end of the matter into the nose a lead tube for several days, until he is healed.
But if he needs treatment which will dry out, use that.
To make the head purging, with which oil and other medicines distill into the nose, do this from silver, or air: that it be similar to a small lamp, open like a shell: and its passage similarly.
If you wish to make a closed cannula like a pipe.
And for making the concha of a purgative instrument, it should be full and emptied: with which is its handle at the end of it, with which you hold it when you heat oil in it, or whatever you wish to extract from solid or fluid substances.
Chapter 25.
The nose often develops at the end of the nose, and it grows and increases with age, until it becomes ugly in appearance.
And because of this, it is necessary to remove all of it at the beginning of its appearance. Then place on the spot, or a cauterizer, or a burning medicine that remains in its place.
If therefore the cutting of it is delayed until it grows large, then consider if it is hard, stony, of dark color, and few sensations: then do not touch it with iron: for it is an abscess that is cancerous.
For often I have seen that one who cuts an abscess has suffered great harm from it.
And if the abscess is gentle to the touch, not of dark color, and you see that it is possible to cut all of it, then evacuate the weak part, and cut it without fear, without pain: and care for the spot with what dries and contracts, until it is healed.
Chapter 26.
Chapter on sutures of the nose, lips, and ears.
Know that when dissolution of continuity occurs in one of these cartilages, it does not hold together well in that operation, except in some men.
Therefore, when something happens to someone, you should consider whether it is a fresh wound with its own blood. Then gather the edges of the wound with stitches, and then care for it until it heals.
And if the edges of continuity are already separated and each part has become healthy, then you must scrape off all the part from its apparent skin until it bleeds. Then gather two edges with a stitch and tie them, and sprinkle powder of dragon's blood on it, and powdered frankincense: and place above the powders a fragment of the plaster diafinicon, and some other fragment of consolidating plasters: and leave it tied for two days or three. Then dissolve it and change the medicine: and leave it until the stitches come off by themselves. Then care for it with ointment until it heals.
However, the method of stitching is to gather the edges of continuity, or with a needle, as we told you about the stitch of the belly: or gather it with thread, as I have shown you.
Chapter 27.
¶ On the extraction of lip knots.
Many people indeed suffer from hard abscesses in the inner parts of their lips, similar to grains of herb: and some of them are smaller, and some larger.
Therefore you should turn the lip over, and cut across all the knot of it, and hang it up with a hook, and cut it from every part.
Then fill the place after the incision with powdered zeig, until the blood is gone.
Then it should be bound with vinegar, and the place should be cared for with it until the wounds are healed.
Chapter 28.
Translation: On making an incision in the flesh of a newborn on the gum.
Often flesh is born on the gum above, which the ancients called abuluss.
Therefore you should suspend it with a spoon: or hold it with forceps, and cut it at its root, and let the wound run, or bleed.
Then place it on a place of zeig powder, or other stanching and drying powders.
If that flesh returns after healing, for often it returns, then cut it again, and cauterize it: for indeed it does not return after cauterization.
Chapter 29.
On the reason of teeth with iron.
Sometimes they gather on the surfaces of teeth from the inner and outer parts, and between the gums rough, discolored, and sometimes yellowish, until that corruption reaches the gum, and the teeth become foul through it.
Therefore you should make the weak one sit between your hands, and his head in your lap, and scrape off the molar and tooth, in which the roughnesses and sand-like things appear to you: until there is nothing left of them, and likewise do with discoloration, greenness, yellowishness, and other things until they are cleansed.
If therefore that which is at the beginning of their reason is removed, it is good: and if not, then repeat the file on them on another day, secondly, and thirdly, until you reach the end of your desire in it.
And know that the tooth needs filing of various forms, many figures: according to how it is prepared for your operation: because the file with which the tooth is filed from the lower part is different from the file with which it is filed between the teeth, according to other forms.
These forms of razors are prepared for you, which you see.
Chapter 30.
On the extraction of toothache.
You should remove the tooth from its pain with all your skill, and delay in its extraction. For its root does not fit when it is extracted: because it is a subtle substance: until when there is no excuse for its extraction, then when the sick person must remove it himself, he should do so to strengthen himself and be certain with you about the toothache.
For often the pain deceives the sick person, and he thinks that it is in the tooth and remove it: then the pain does not go away, until the weak tooth is extracted.
For we have already seen this from the operation of bloodletting.
When therefore the sick person himself is certain about the toothache, then you should scarify around the tooth with a sharp lancet, in which there is some virtue, until the gum is dissolved from all parts: then move it with your fingers, or with slender forceps gradually, until you shake it.
Then place large forceps in that location with good hold, and the head of the sick person between your knees: which you have already held well, so that it does not move: then pull the tooth according to straightness, so that you do not break it.
If therefore it does not come out, then take some of those instruments, and insert it under it from all parts with ease, and try to move it, as you did in the first place.
But if the tooth is perforated, or corroded: then you should fill the hole with a cloth: and tie it with the tip of a slender rod, so that it does not break in the hour of your constriction over it with forceps.
And it is necessary to carefully perform scarification around the circumference of the jaw from all sides by a lot.
And keep your strength, so that it does not break itself, and its part remains, and it returns above the weak one from that greater malice which is more of its pain first.
And beware, that you do not do what unknowing phlebotomists do in their haste, and the boldness of them beyond its eradication, besides what they administer which we have mentioned.
For they often happen to people great infirmities, of which some are difficult to break, and all its roots remain, or some of them: or that they extract it with some of the jawbones: as we have often testified about that.
Then it should be covered after its eradication with wine, or with vinegar and salt.
If blood flow occurs from the places (for it often happens), then you should wipe a little from zege, and fill with it that place: and if not, burn it if zege does not help you.
The forms of the fine forceps by which the tooth is moved in the first place, should be long at their extremities, short at the handle, thick, so that they do not duplicate when with them pressed on the tooth: they should be like the thick handles, until when you squeeze with them, they do not bite themselves, nor duplicate: short at their extremities, and made of iron, or of a well-made sharp edge, direct extremities: and in their extremities there should be teeth, some of which enter into certain ones, and squeeze with a proper constriction, strong.
And sometimes they are made like the extremities of the beak of a bird called a stork, and they are strong for constriction.
Chapter 31.
Translation: On the removal of teeth and the extraction of jawbone fractures.
When a tooth is broken and there remains something under the extraction, then it is necessary to place butter on the affected area for one or two days until the area becomes soft: then introduce lute or forceps, whose tips resemble the beak of a bird called ciconia. However, this is the form of forceps.
Their tips are made like a file inside or like an axe.
If therefore it does not submit to you with these forceps, then it is necessary to make a hole above the root and tear the flesh entirely, and introduce the tool called the "small pliers," whose form is as follows:
Let it be short in length, somewhat thick: and not wet, so that it does not break.
If therefore the root exits through that, it is good: and if not, you must groan with these other tools whose forms are as follows:
The form of the first triangular tip, in which there is a certain thickness.
The form of the fine triangular tip.
And with other tools and instruments that preceded in the ratio of teeth.
Also groan with this tool that resembles a large hook, of this form, a twisted triangular tip, in which there is a certain thickness, so that it does not break: and it is not wet.
And know that there are many tools for teeth: and similarly the other tools are not counted, and the wise craftsman, skilled in his art, has invented by himself the tool according to what signifies to him the operation and the pains of them.
Since from grudges are those things to which the ancients did not speak, due to their diversity in kinds.
But if the jawbone is broken from the jaw, or from other bones of the mouth, or rots: then examine above it in its place with that which is fitting for him from the instruments and forceps which I mentioned in the extraction of the root, and heal with the one whose form is this.
Let there be something of thickness gradually, so that it is bound or held with the jaw, and does not flee and float until the jaw exits: and restore the place with suitable medicines to that.
But if there is a small rot in the bone, then scrape it from its own rot, and heal it, until it is healed.
Chapter 32.
Of the extraction of teeth projecting above others.
When teeth do not project above others according to their natural course, it becomes ugly by that form: and especially when it happens in women, and girls, that is, in virgins.
Therefore you should consider. For if the tooth is born after another tooth, and does not fit, or is possible to be extracted, nor is it cut: then remove it: and if it is connected with another tooth, then cut it with this instrument, whose form is this.
It is similar to a small beak, and is made of iron, very sharp at the end.
And let your cut be where you cut it into many days, and because of the hardness of the tooth, and so that another is not moved from the teeth.
But if it is projecting exposed to its own cutting: then cut it with a file with a file, whose form is this.
It should all be done from the inside, and the handle of its needles and puncturers should be like a file with which sharp points are made: with which the tooth is gradually cut away over many days with ease, so that the tooth does not move and fall off; then it is gently rubbed, and in the end it is scraped with some rasors.
But if it is a tooth from which a part is broken off and hurts the tongue: then it is necessary that the edge of it even be filed away, until the roughness of that broken part is evened out; and it should be flattened, and not hurt the tongue, nor corrupt speech.
Chapter 33.
On the retention of teeth with gold wires.
When it happens to the front teeth that they are shaken and moved by a blow or by chance: and the weak one cannot string over what he eats so that it does not fall out; and you have treated them with stiptics, and the cure has not improved: then the ingenuity in them is, that they should be strung with gold wire: because silver becomes green, and rots after days: but gold never changes.
And let the wire be of medium thinness and thickness according to the quantity that it takes between the teeth.
Indeed the form of retention is, that you take the wire, and insert a double of it between two healthy teeth: then you weave with both ends of the wire between the moved teeth, whether one is, or more, until you reach with the net up to the healthy tooth of the other part. Then repeat the weaving up to the part from which you began: and tie your hand with thinness and wisdom, until it is not moved at all: and your constriction when you string the wire, at the roots of the teeth, so that it does not rot.
Then cut the excess ends of the thread with scissors: and gather both ends, and fold them over the gum: and hide each one between the sound tooth and the moving tooth, so as not to wound the tongue: then let it be left thus tight until it remains.
But if it is dislodged or cut, tie them again with another thread, and let it remain with it thus for the whole time.
And this is the form of the teeth, and the shape of the bite of two sound teeth, and two moving teeth, as you see.
And sometimes it happens that one tooth, or two after the loss of both, returns to its place and is held as we have mentioned, and remains: and this is done only by a skillful and experienced craftsman.
And sometimes something is fitted from the bones of cattle: and it is made into the shape of a tooth, and is placed in the place from which the tooth is protected and tied, as we have said: and it remains, and is served with it for a long time.
Chapter 34.
Sometimes this ligament that occurs under the tongue is natural, with which man is born, or accidental, from a wound that has already consolidated.
And the operation in it is that you open the mouth of the sick person in his breast, and raise his tongue: then cut this nervous ligament in width, until the tongue is released from its retention.
If there is something hard and knotted in it, and it is from the consolidation of a wound: then thrust into it a hook, and cut it through width, until you have cut the ligament, and released the knot.
And beware, lest there be a deep cut in the flesh, and you sever an artery there, and blood loss occurs.
Then the wound should be covered with a rosewater soaked cloth, or with vinegar, or with cold water.
Then place a linen bandage under the tongue, which the weak person should hold all night: so that it does not consolidate again on the second day.
But if blood loss occurs, then place on the wound a poultice of zegi powder. But if indeed the blood overwhelms you, then cauterize the place with a lentiginous cauterizer, which is suitable for that: then care for it along with the rest of the treatment, until it heals.
Chapter 35.
Sometimes a tumor occurs under the tongue that resembles a small stone, preventing the tongue from performing its natural function: and perhaps it grows so much, until it fills the mouth.
And the operation in it is, that you open the mouth of the sick person before the sun: and consider the tumor.
If therefore you see it of a dark or black color, hard, to which the sick person does not have sense: then do not touch it, because it is cancer.
And if it is inclined to whiteness, in which there is moisture, then push into it a hook, and cut it with a fine spear, and free it from all part. But if the blood overwhelms you in your hour of operation, then place on it a poultice of zegi powder, until the blood is cut off: then return to your operation, until you extract it with its fullness.
Then it is soaked with vinegar and salt: and care for it with the rest of the cure that is suitable to that, until it heals.
On the Cure of Two Abscesses in the Tonsils.
Chapter 36.
Sometimes abscesses occur between the throat and the glands, that is, the tonsils, which resemble almonds: and they are called two Tonsils: which when you treat with what we said in division, and do not heal, then consider.
If therefore it is a hard abscess, of brownish color, with little pain: then do not touch it with iron.
And if it is of red color, and its root is thick: then do not touch it even with iron, fearing the flow of blood, indeed leave it, until it ripens. And then either you will pierce it: or it will burst by itself.
And if it is of white color, round, and its root is thin: then it must be pierced.
And the operation in it is, that you consider before the operation of its abscess, if the hot abscess of it has been completed with quiet rest, or it has diminished by some diminution: then therefore make the sick person sit in front of the sun, and his head in your lap: and open his mouth, and let him take a servant between his hands, and press his lower tongue with an instrument, whose this is its form.
Let it be made of silver, or of brass, which is thin like a knife.
When therefore you press with it the tongue, and the abscess appears to you, and falls on it your sight: then take a hook, and fix it in the tonsil, and draw it out as much as you can, except that you pull with it some from its clothes.
Then, cut it with an instrument of this form, which follows. It is adapted to forceps: however, its extremities should be guarded, so that the opening of each of them is directly opposite and sharp: therefore, care should be taken that it is from iron indo, or alloyed with lead.
But if this instrument is not present, then cut it with a spatula of this form. It should be sharp on one side, not sharp on the other.
And after you have cut one almond, cut the other according to the same method of incision.
Then, after incision, the sick person should gargle with cold water, or with vinegar and water.
But if blood flow occurs to him, gargle with water in which the bark of beans has been boiled: or myrtle leaves, and similar things from stiptics, until the bleeding is stopped: then care for it, until it is healed.
And sometimes abscesses arise in the throat other than the two almonds. Then cut them according to what I said in the incision of two almonds equally.
And indeed, I myself have already healed a woman from an abscess, which was born between her throat, which was pulling to the esophagus, little sense, which had almost closed the throat: and the woman breathed through a narrow opening, and had already stopped her eating, and drinking water: and had arrived at death, if she remained for one day, or two days.
And the abscess had risen so much that it had emitted two branches, until they exited through two nostril holes.
I therefore acted swiftly and fixed one of their hooks. Then I pulled it out, and a large piece came with it.
Then I cut it off where I had grasped it from the nostril opening.
Then I did the same to the other one that protruded from the nostril opening.
Then I opened his mouth, and pressed his tongue: and afterwards I fixed a hook into the abscess: then I cut out part of it, and only a little blood came out of it: therefore the throat of the woman was cured, and she immediately began to drink water, and then she took food.
Therefore I did not stop cutting out of that abscess many times over a long period of time: and the abscess would take the place of what I was cutting out, until it had been prolonged too much and with it.
Therefore I devised, and I cauterized the abscess between the throat.
Therefore she stood up after the addition: then I walked away from that side, and I did not know what God had done with her after me.
Chapter on the cutting of abscesses in the mouth.
Chapter 37.
When the catarrh descends to the mouth, and becomes an abscess, and is long: then it is called a perpendicular one: and if it is in the lower part round and large, then it is called a wound.
When it is cured with what we said in the division, and the cure does not come together: and you see that the abscess has become warm and thin: then it is necessary to cut it out.
And what is gathered from it is round and not long, and is bloody, or of a yellowish or black color, and there is no sensation: then it is necessary to follow the cutting out of it. For it is in that place where there is fear of the weak.
Therefore, when you see it according to the manner I mentioned from its whiteness and length, you should make the infirm person sit before the sun: and press his tongue with an instrument, of which the preceding narration was made: then fix a hook in the wound, and pull it downwards: and cut it with one of the two instruments I mentioned for incision of the two tonsils.
And it is necessary that you do not cut from it, except that which is added above the natural limit without addition.
For if you cut from it more, you will damage the voice and speech.
Then after the incision, use that which we mentioned in the incision of the two tonsils: and care for it, until it is healed.
But if the infirm person fears the incision: then you must use your skill in cauterizing it without fear and cowardice.
And the method of cauterization in it is not, except with sharp water: and it is, that you place the head of the infirm person in your lap. Then press his tongue with the instrument which we mentioned. Then take from the water which I told you in the chapter of cauterizing, and mix it with unextinguished charcoal, and place it not thick nor thin, and fill the cavity of this instrument, whose form is as follows.
Let the extreme part of it in which the medicine is placed be a hollow, like the hollow of a needle.
And place the instrument with the medicine on the same hook: and let the infirm person be lying on his side, so that salt may run out from his mouth from the internal medicine, so that nothing may descend from it to his throat, and harm him.
Then hold your hand with the medicine. And you should apply it to the first part of the wound, in the amount of half an hour, until you see that it has become discolored and the pain of the medicine has been relieved.
And if you want to take a probe, and wrap it with cloth, and pour the probe with the medicine, and insert the probe with the cloth into a tube from above, until the cloth sticks to the wound.
Do this many times, until you achieve what you want from the cauterization of that wound. Then let it go: for it will dry up and fall off after three days, or four.
But if you need to repeat the medicine, repeat it: and after cauterization wipe around the wound with cloth dampened in butter, and clean it with what is around it from the medicine: and moisten it with cold water.
And it will be healed externally with an ointment, and internally with gargles, until it is healed.
Therefore this kind of treatment is healthier than incision and further from fear.
And sometimes the wound is also healed with that which is finer than cauterization and incision: it is healed with smoking, in this way. Take a poultice, and hyssop, and origanum, and rue, and seaweed, and chamomile, and abrotanum, and similar herbs to these: and gather all of them, or some of them in a pot, and immerse them with vinegar, and boil: and the pot should be glazed with clay properly: and there should be a hole in the middle of the pot, above which a concave instrument is placed according to this way.
Make it from silver or copper: and its tip is inserted into the mouth of the sick person, where there is a lemon, until the vapor rises to the nostril through the tube, until the nostril becomes obscured.
Then repeat this process on it many times, until it dries out.
And beware, do not make this treatment at the beginning of the appearance of abscesses. For it rather adds to the abscess: and you should not make this unless at the decline of its hot stage.
If however this instrument is not present to you, then take a tube, and place in its tip some wool: so that the mouth of the sick person will not be burned: because the wool prevents the vapor from burning the mouth: and this is from good treatment with safety.
¶ On the extraction of thorns from the throat, and bones.
Chapter 38.
Often a bone or thorn of a fish, or other thing, sticks in the throat.
Therefore you must extract what is apparent on top of which it falls, after you have placed your tongue with the instrument under the sun, and it is declared to you that it is in the throat.
And what does not appear to you and is hidden in the throat, you must make the sick person vomit before the food is digested in the stomach. Perhaps the attached thing will come out through vomiting.
Or the sick person may swallow a piece of bone, or the stem of lettuce, or a dry crust of bread: or he may receive a piece of dried sea sponge gently, and then tie it with a thread, and then swallow it. When therefore it has reached the place where the thorns, or bone, are, and is extracted, then it comes out.
If therefore it does not exit with that which we said, then use the tool made of lead according to this form.
Let it be larger than the radius by a little, and at its end there should be a narrowness which will enter into his throat with ease: and he himself should have his head raised up.
And beware of his own epiglottis, so that it does not happen to him coughing, and he pushes with it, or a spindle, or inserts himself the physician with his own hand.
But that the sick person inserts, this is better: because of his knowledge of the location of the attached thing: and he pushes downwards, or draws his hand with the instrument upwards, all that second according to the quantity which is prepared for him, until it exits.
§ On the extraction of a leech.
Chapter 39.
When the leech is treated with it which we said in division from cure with medicines, and does not attach, then consider in the throat of the sick person before the sun, or at the sun after you have placed his tongue with the instrument which I told you.
If therefore your sight falls upon the leech, extract it with a small hook, or with a delicate instrument.
If it is not possible with them: then take a hollow needle, and insert it into the throat of the sick person up to near the throat: then insert into the hollow of the needle burning iron with fire. Do this many times: and the sick person should avoid all water for the whole day.
Then he should receive a full glass of cold water, and open his mouth in it: and cover his mouth with it, and not swallow anything from it: and move the water one hour after another with his hand. Bloodletting is immediately affected when it feels water.
If, however, it does not exit with what we mentioned, then smoke the infirm person with cicadas, or with assa foetida using the instrument we mentioned in the smoking of the wound.
Do this often, because it will fall itself.
And the method of operation in smoking is, that you take a pot in which there are live prunes with fire: and the pot should be covered with a covering, in which there is a hole: and it should be arranged in that hole the end of the instrument.
Then throw the smoking, and place the infirm person's mouth at the end of the cannula, and close his mouth, so that the smoking does not exit, until you know that the smoking has reached the bloodsucker. For the bloodsucker will immediately fall.
If it does not fall, then repeat the smoking often.
And the infirm person should tolerate thirst, and eat with salt, and mallows, and not drink water.
It is therefore necessary that it exit with this regimen.
And this is the form of the instrument with which the bloodsucker is drawn from the throat, when it falls on it with its sight.
It is similar to forceps, as you see: unless that it has this curve which is inserted into the throat. And its end is similar to the beak of a bird which is called a stork, in which there is the roughness of a file: when it grasps something, it does not let it go entirely.
On the opening of abscesses, and their section, and care in general.
Chapter 40.
Abscesses are of many kinds, of many modes, according to how the remembrance of them comes, namely one, and one in this book: and they are diverse in their perforation, and section from two modes.
One of them is of the kind of boils that exist within themselves and which include moisture.
And the second method is due to the locations where it occurs from the body.
Because a boil that occurs in the head is different from a boil that occurs in the anus, and a boil that occurs in fleshy places is different from a boil that occurs in joints, and each of them has its own judgment according to its operation.
And from boils are those that do not require to be lanced unless after the maturation of pus in them and its suppuration: and from them are those that require to be lanced while they are raw and not matured according to their suppuration.
Such as boils that are near joints.
Because a boil when it occurs near a joint, and persists to be its existence until it putrefies what is in its vicinity perhaps the ligaments or nerves of that joint's connection are corrupted: therefore this is a cause for contraction of that limb.
Or it is a boil at the main member: for if you delay its lancing until it matures, it will harm either him or through that main member.
Or it is near the anus, lance therefore it immature: and it is not necessary to lance a raw boil that is not fully digested, except that which is near the anus so that it does not putrefy deeply and extend to the interior of the anus and become a fistula or become in its end that is not healed.
It is necessary to know the time of lancing boils that have matured according to their suppuration: and it is at the cessation of pain, recession of fever, and diminution of redness, and pulsation, and sharpness of the head's boil: and other signs.
And it is necessary to make the same incision in the lower part of the abscess and its most prominent elevation: and let the incision be made lengthwise along the body, if the abscesses are in the parts of the hands and feet, and in the back, and in the tendons, and nerves, and arteries, and finally in all equal places where there is no reflection.
But in those things which are reflected, go with the incision according to that member.
But when the abscess is in fleshy places, it is better to let the incision of it go until its digestion is confirmed, as we said according to the complement,
because if you incise it before that, the course of the virus from it is prolonged, and there are many and filthy discharges, and perhaps its lips are hardened, and its depth.
And some abscesses are incised according to the width of the body at necessity: or according to that by which the member needs.
And it is necessary for the attendant to make a small incision in small abscesses, and a wide incision in large abscesses: or many cuts according to the similarity of the size of the abscesses.
And there are abscesses from which the skin must be concaved: and it is incised when it has been made like a garment, and has become in the end, which is already dead: like that which happens in many, so that they doubt, and in buboes.
And there are those which are cut with a cut having three angles. And there is one from which it is incised like the figure of a myrtle leaf.
Like the inguinal abscess.
And there are those in which the incision is circular, and the lunar incision: and similar to them from the incisions.
That which does not have a head, such as soft, shallow abscesses, should be pierced with a shallow, flat incision.
And when the abscess is large and has already collected a lot of pus, it should be pierced so that you do not rush and remove all the pus at once, but rather remove some of it from that part. Then leave the abscess alone until another day. Then remove some more of the pus again.
Do this repeatedly according to the gradation until it is all out, especially if the patient is weak and lacking in strength, or a pregnant woman, or a small child, or an old man: for the animal spirit often dissolves with the exit of pus, and perhaps the weak one dies, and you will not notice.
Therefore pay great attention to this chapter.
And after your incision, by which you have pierced these abscesses, it is necessary to clean the wound and consider. If therefore the wound is small or a flat incision, then apply lint from linen, or old cotton. And if the abscess is large and there are many incisions, then you must insert lint into every incision until they all meet.
And if you have cut a part of the skin in the abscess, or have scooped it out: then you must fill it with old cotton, or as when a garment is sewn, or shorn of its wool without moisture: and bind it up until the third day.
Then raise it up, and care for it with what is necessary from an ointment until it heals.
If bleeding occurs during your surgical procedure, then apply cold water and vinegar to the cloth after it has absorbed the blood, and place it repeatedly on the wound.
If the bleeding persists, then you must apply the treatment and cure, as I have mentioned in various places of this book, and by division.
If it is during the winter season and there are many boils on the skin: then you must pour in powders with wine and warm oil, and place them on the affected areas.
And if it is during the summer and there are fleshy areas: then you must place powders soaked in water and oil, or with wine and oil, and make the whole thing cold. Until the third day, as we said, then you must dissolve the boils and cleanse it, and apply the treatment that is appropriate for its healing until it is healed.
This is therefore what is necessary for the universal knowledge of the treatment of boils.
Indeed, according to the method of distinction, I have already said about every boil, how the way to its cure is taken up separately in each chapter.
Chapter 41.
¶ About the incision of boils that occur on the skin of the head.
Small boils occur on the skin of the head, and are of the kind of nodes that contain the tunics which are like their sacks: as if they were themselves plucked chickens.
And there are many of these kinds.
From these there are fleshy ones: and from these there are those that contain moisture similar to lime: and from these there are those that contain moisture similar to flour and porridge: and from these there are similar ones, and from these there are those that are hard like stone.
In all cases of cutting and their removal, there is no fear as long as one does not perform the cut opposite an artery.
The operation in their cutting is to try it with the instrument whose form comes after these, which is called the "Intrumissus", until you know what it contains.
For if it contains moisture, then dry it with a cut according to the length of the surface cut: in this form.
And begin with a cut from line b to line g. When the moisture is drained, then scrape off the shell that contains that moisture, and do not leave anything from it completely.
For often it returns if something remains from it.
Then immerse the wound in Egyptian ointment if it is present: and if not, in water and salt: and fill the wound with it, and leave it until another day. For it will consume what remains from the shell.
Then repeat over it with Egyptian ointment second and third, and if you need it, until you trust that nothing remains from the shell, then care for the wound with ointment until it is healed.
If the abscess contains a fat knot: then dry it according to this form, with a cut having the form of a cross: and insert pins between the sides of the cut, and scrape it from all parts: and try your strength in extracting the tunic that contains it.
But if it makes a contradiction for you, an artery, then do what I will tell you after.
And likewise do in a stone abscess, from the cut and cure, as we said.
This section on lapidary abscess is easier: because it has little blood and moisture. Sometimes there are certain abscesses among these people, in which there is no moisture at all.
Which is: because I cut open an abscess on the head of an old woman, and found an abscess like a solid and hard, rough, white stone, which could not be broken: and if anyone struck it with it throwing, it would wound him.
But in other abscesses that occur on the head, namely those that occur in the heads of children, and at the roots of the ears, this section is all surface.
Or make an incision in them always from the lower part of them, so that the course of the pus may be relieved to the lower parts.
Then take care of those with what is suitable for their cure.
§ On the incision of Strophularia in the neck.
Chapter 42.
These abscesses often occur in the neck, and under the armpits, and in the groin: and sometimes they occur in the rest of the body.
And over those that occur in the neck, there is one and many: and they are generated from each other: and every Strophula from them is within its own tunic, as is in knots and abscesses of the head, as we have said.
And the species of these Strophularia are many. For from them there are stony ones: and from them there are those that contain moisture: and from them there are evil ones, which do not obey the cure.
In that one therefore which you see of good disposition in touch, whose color is near the skin, and moves to all parts, and is not annexed with the nerves of the neck, nor with the ganglia, nor with the artery, nor is deep: it is necessary to cut it with a shallow incision from the upper part to the lower part of the body along a line b. to a line g., and scrape it from all parts: and extend two lips of skin with a needle, or with many needles, if you need that, as we said in abscesses of the head, and extrahe it gradually.
And it is a precaution that the vein or nerve does not get caught.
And let the incision be not too sharp: so that it does not add to your hand with the incision, or disturb the weak, and you cut what is not necessary.
But if you cut the vein or artery, and it prevents you from the operation, then place in the wound some triturated zegium powder, or some powders that stop bleeding, and tie the wound, and leave it until the sharpness of the abscess subsides, and the wound becomes soft: or it begins to putrefy.
For the blood is stopped then. So return to your operation until you complete it.
Then with your index finger, check if there is anything remaining from the strophuli or small ones: so cut them and clean them.
But if there is a large vein in the root of the strophuli: then it is necessary that you do not cut that strophuli from its root: but it is necessary that you tie it with a strong doubled thread, and leave it until it falls off without harm.
Then fill the wound with old cataplasm that you have already immersed in Egyptian ointment. Then take care of it yourself.
But if the strophuli is cut entirely, then it is necessary that you gather the two wound lips: and suture it immediately, after you see that there is no remaining excess.
But if you see that there is remaining excess due to the size of the strophuli, then it is necessary that you extend to cutting its root, and removing it: and administer the suture that we said.
And what contains moisture from the strophuli, puncture it with a superficial puncture: so that you see its place of maturity to you: and place the puncture below the body, as we said.
After perforation, apply liniment with ointment and similar substances to cauterize the remaining part affected by corruption until you see that the wound is clean. Then treat the wound with a generative ointment of flesh until it heals.
Chapter 43.
On Sectioning the Epiglottis from an Abscess within the Throat.
The ancients performed this sectioning of the epiglottis, and I have not seen anyone in our land who has done it; and this is the written account of their words.
However, in those who have a synanche, it is necessary to avoid sectioning the epiglottis because a tracheotomy cannot be performed through it; since all veins and lungs are weak.
However, in those who have a hot abscess in the mouth, throat, or both jaws when there is no illness in the canal, it is necessary to perform sectioning of the epiglottis to escape from the danger that occurs from the praefication.
Therefore, when we want to do it, we should section the epiglottis under three or four circles of the epiglottis by a small cut along its width, in the part between two circles by an amount that is a section in the cartilage, not in the cartilage: and this location is convenient for sectioning because it is free from flesh, and the veins are far from it.
However, if the physician is afraid, then it is necessary to stretch the skin of the throat with a lancet. Then he should flatten the skin until he reaches the canal: avoid the veins if he sees anything from them.
Then he should cut the cartilage that we mentioned: and it is indicated to cut the canal from the phlegm that escapes from it, because it is broken, and the division of the voice.
And leave an open wound at some time.
When therefore the prefication is removed at the time when it is feared, gather the two lips of the wound together and heal the skin alone without cartilage.
Then administer medicines which cause flesh to grow until it is healed.
Albucasis says. The summary of this narrative that we have told is not an explanation unless when they see that some of these abscesses has already filled the throat of the sick person: and the sick person was raised up over death, and wanted to be cut off from his breathing: they go to cut the epiglottis, so that the sick person may breathe on the place of the wound with some breathing, and be saved from death: and for this reason they ordered to leave the open wound until the malice of the illness is consumed, and its malice is three days, and almost itself: then they ordered to heal the wound and cure it until it is healed.
And that which I saw myself is that one maidservant took a knife and sent it with her into her throat, and cut the part of the trachea.
And I was called for her cure, and I found her groaning, as is the groaning of the dead.
Then I untied her from the wound, and I found blood that had gone out of the wound in a small amount. Then I was afraid that she had not cut the vein, nor stopped it: and wind was going out of the wound.
Then I hurried and healed her wound, until it was healed: and nothing happened to the maidservant except a hoarseness in her voice: and she returned after days to a better condition of her affairs.
I therefore say: that in the section of the Epiglottis there is no fear.
Of the section of the hernia of the throat.
Chapter 44.
This apostema called hernia of the throat, is a large apostema according to the color of the body: and it is much in women.
And it is according to two modes: either it is natural: or it is accidental.
In the natural certainly there is no skill.
But in the accidental indeed there are two modes: of which one is similar to the fat knots. And the other mode, is similar to the apostema that is made from the bending of the artery. And in it is fear, and it is not necessary that a presumption be made to it with iron, unless in that which is small: and you probe it, and investigate it with the intromission. If therefore you find it similar to the fat knot, and it is not suspended with any vein: then cut it, as they are cut off the knots: and extract it with that which contains from the chest, if it is in the chest: and if not, then scrutinize all of it. Then care for the place with that which is necessary from the cure, until it is healed.
Chapter 45.
Of the section of the kind of knots.
There are many kinds of knots, and I have already said all the kinds of them in the division: and it is necessary that I tell here the difference between a knot, and an ulcer: since it causes doubt.
I say therefore, that when an ulcer is heat, and fever, and very sharp pains, until the boiling over of the superfluity is quieted, and the putrefaction is completed: then indeed the fever and the heat are quieted.
When there is a knot, there is no heat, fever, or pain, and it contains them in their own sifachin, which is their own sack and is according to the color of the body: and its beginning is like chickpeas, and it becomes like broad beans, and greater and smaller.
And they are according to two species: either fat: or they contain moisture. And the colors of moisture are many, as I said in the division.
Therefore, when you come to the cure of the knot, you must experiment with it and inquire about it first with the instrument called Intromissus, according to its form as it comes in the chapter that follows.
And the method of investigating the abscess and all knots is, that you take this instrument and insert it into a moister place, which you find in the abscess: and you turn your fingers with it gradually, until you know that the instrument has penetrated the skin. Then your last hand according to the measure of the size of the abscess.
Then extract Intromissus, and consider what comes out at its tread.
If therefore it comes out running moisture, whatever color it is: then dry it with a shallow cut, according to what I said in the other abscesses.
And if moisture does not come out at the tread of Intromissus, then you know that it is fat: then dry it with a cut having the form of a cross, according to this form, as I taught you: and suspend it with hooks, and excoriate the skin from all parts with ease: and guard the sac if you can over it, so that you may extract it whole with the knot.
But if the sac is torn by the operation, and it is not possible to extract it whole, often this happens: then extract it in pieces, until there remains nothing from it.
For if something remains from it, either too little or too much, it returns to the knot as much as possible.
If it wounds you and something remains from it too little: then fill the wound with certain corrosive powders at your completion, and tie the wound, and place on top of it what sits apostema hot, and care for it with the rest of the cure until it is healed.
If therefore it is a large knot, then cut its two lips, and care for it with that which fleshens.
But if it is contrary to you vein pulsatilis, or not pulsatilis: then hurry, and fill the place zegi ground, and let it be tied for two days, or three, until the wound rots, and the boiling of blood stops: then return to cutting that which remains from the knot.
Chapter 46
Paragraph on external instruments for cutting and piercing.
From them are the forms of intromissors, and they are of three kinds.
For from them is the large one, and from them is the medium one, and from them is the small one.
Let them be made from iron awl of square ends properly, so that they quickly enter into the apostema.
And these are the forms of experiens, and no, that is, piercing: and one of them is called beris, that is, piercing: and they are of three kinds.
For from them is the large one, and the medium one, and the small one.
They are used, so that they investigate through them the apostemata, and the exits, and the fistulas, and the bubones from that which is between them from the bones.
And others are made round, clean, soft, like the large awls which have seats, from citrine indeed, or from air, or from iron, or from silver.
And better among them are those that are made from citrine.
They are also made from black lead, which they use to experiment with fistulas, whose concavity is a reflection, so that they reflect gently with their own reflections.
And there are again three kinds. Because from them are the long ones, from them the medium ones, and from them the short ones, according to the extent of the length of the fistula and its tightness.
The shape of the Uncins, and they are many kinds.
Because from them are the simple ones, that is, those with one curvature: and they are three kinds as you see, large, medium, and small.
And from them are the blind Uncins: and they are three kinds.
And from them are the Uncins with two curvatures, and they are three kinds: and from them are the Uncins with three curvatures, and they are three kinds: and all of these are necessary in their place.
And these are the shapes of Scalpels, with which they cut and scrape Nodes, and abscesses: and they are three kinds: because from them is large, medium, and small.
Their extremities by which the section is made are sharp, other extremities are not sharp: and they are not placed thus, except that with them is made a gentle touch in scraping Nodes at the fear of incision of the vein, or nerve: and that the sick person may be healed by it, and find a little tranquility from the burning which he found at scraping abscesses.
They are made from air, and they are similar to the Rod, with which is made alcohol: and in the broad extremity is a hidden Spatula point: and in it runs to the insides, and to the outsides when you want, as you see.
The shape of the boils that are hidden between the fingers, at the opening of the pustule: and they do not feel them by the sick: and they are of three kinds, large, medium, and small.
The shape of the wounds from which blood flows: and they are of three kinds, large, medium, and small.
Let them be made of air, or yellow, round, to a certain length, as you see: and let they be at the subtlety.
And it is necessary that these species of wounds from which blood flows be large and small with you: so as to cut through them the blood with speed at need, and then when there is not present for you the medicine.
But you will not use them in the cutting of blood in every place of the body, and you will not use unless in fleshy places: as the arms of the legs, and the hips, and the arms of the arms, and the breasts, and the belly, and the groin, and similar to them, from fleshy places, moist.
And sometimes they are made of them small instruments similar to the shells of nuts, according to their shape: through which blood is cut when it flows from the place of phlebotomy, or at the incision of the vein, or artery: and sometimes they are made of them round according to this form.
Chapter 47.
About the care of the breasts of men which resemble the breasts of women.
Sometimes the breasts of certain men swell at the fullness of sleep (that is, when they begin to be polluted in sleep) until they resemble the breasts of women: and remain pustulous fiercely.
Whoever abhors that, it is necessary for him to cover the breasts with a crescent-shaped incision, according to this form from point b to line a, and then remove all the fat. Afterwards, fill the wound with flesh-colored medicament. Then gather both wound lips together with a suture, and care for it until it is healed.
If however the breast leans towards the lower parts and becomes soft due to its size, as often happens with women: then it is necessary for him to make two incisions in the upper two sides of his breasts, each containing one on either side near their ends, until a larger line contains a smaller one, according to this form from point b to line a, g. Afterwards remove the skin that is between the two lips, and take off all the fat, and administer what we said about sutures and powders, which is necessary for healing, until it is healed.
If however he cannot complete the incision that is necessary to make, due to the agitation of the sick person, or due to the flow of blood: then it is necessary for him to fill the wound with a dissolving ointment submerged, and leave it, until it corrodes what remains of the fat. Then care for it until it is healed.
Concerning the piercing of abscesses, which happens under the nipple.
Chapter 48.
These abscesses which happen under the nipple are from a kind of hard Strophularia, which contains pustules, and from these are those which contain moistures.
Those therefore which are from those which contain moistures, it is necessary for them to be dried with a crescent-shaped incision, according to this form from point b to line a, g. When however all that is in the abscess is evacuated through pus, then fill it with old ointment, and leave it until another day.
Then remove the bandage and treat it with an appropriate ointment until it heals.
If the abscess is of the type of Strophularia blisters, then cut it above, as we said in the section on Strophularia evenly.
If the wound extends so that it can discharge pus, then apply a cautery to it according to what we said in the one that was previously mentioned.
Chapter 49.
On incising abscesses that occur due to artery and vein.
When the artery is ruptured and the skin that is above it is consolidated, an abscess often occurs from this: and similarly, an abscess and swelling also occur in veins.
And the signs by which it is known that the abscess and swelling are due to the artery and vein, are: because when the abscess is due to the artery, it is long, gathered deep in the body: and when you press the abscess with your fingers, you feel as if there is a noise to it.
And that which is due to the vein, is round in the obvious body.
And incision on this abscess is an error, and especially that which is under the armpits, and groins, and neck, and in many places of the body: and it is great very much. Therefore it should be avoided with iron, and that which is from them also at the extremities, or at the head, should be avoided.
On that which is from them due to swelling of the artery opening, find in the skin incision in length. Then open the incision with hooks, then the artery: and free it from the tunics, until it is stripped.
Then introduce the needle under it and make it penetrate to the other side, and tie the artery with a double thread in two places, as I taught you in the extraction of the two arteries that are in the temples.
Then prick the place that is between two ligaments with a lancet, until all the blood that is in it comes out and the abscess is dissolved.
Then administer the treatment that generates pus until the ligaments fall off; afterwards care for it with suitable ointments until it heals.
If it is an abscess due to the cutting of a vein, then you must hold with your hand what is possible to remove from the abscess and the skin. Then introduce the needle under the place that you held with your hand, and make it penetrate; and let there be a double thread on it, until you remove it from the other side. Then tie it with the abscess with a good ligature: according to what I told you about tying a vein from two parts with two ends of the thread.
But if you fear that the thread will be pulled out, then introduce another needle with another thread under the abscess entirely near the incision of the needle: press and tie your thread in four places.
Then cut the abscess in the middle of it, until when it comes out what is in it: then cut the excess skin and let go what is tied from it.
Then place on it the swab that you immersed in wine and oil. Then administer the treatment that is made with linen and ointment until it heals.
Chapter L.
About an abscess that happens due to the twisting of nerves.
Just as it happens that an abscess forms in an artery and vein, similarly, an abscess can form in nerves. This occurs in them due to a blow or from excessive labor, and the like. It is most common in the regions of helpers, such as the heel, and in every place where the joints move. And it is a severe abscess.
Its color is similar to that of the rest of the body, and it occurs in many positions without pain. And when it is pressed with intensity, the sick person feels in it a sensation similar to a stupor.
And it is not an aggregated abscess in the deep part of the body, but rather under the skin, and it moves to every part, and does not go towards the front or before, nor behind to the back parts.
Therefore, what is in the joints, it is not necessary to pierce with iron. Perhaps contraction may occur.
But in that which is from them in the head, or in the forehead, pierce the skin with a small knife. If therefore it is a small abscess, then grasp it with forceps, and cut it away from the root.
And if it is large, then suspend it with a hook, and scrape it off. Then remove it, and suture the wound with a stitch: and care for it until it heals.
Chapter Ll.
Concerning the incision of abscesses that occur in the belly.
Sometimes many people have in their bellies and in the rest of their bodies, tumors, which are called mushrooms, due to a likeness of them to mushrooms.
Whose root is thin, and their head is thick, and their lips are turned over. And there are also those who are few in number: and there are also those who are highly praised.
And indeed I have seen a man, and in his belly were two thelils, which were more similar to other things than anything else: there was no difference between them, they were white, with small roots, and they opposed their lips, and they found each other, and moisture always flowed from them.
I therefore cut into them, and I found in the weight of one as if it were X and VIII ounces and in the other as if it were VI ounces. And the operation in their incision is, that you consider then, if the sick person is humid, and the color of the thelil is white, moist, subtle root: then cut him with a broad spatula, and there be cauterization in your presence in fire.
For often blood is driven out from his incision: therefore if the blood overcomes you, then cauterize it.
But if you see the sick person afraid and timid from the incision with iron, then take a thread made of lead properly, and tie with it athelul: whose mode we have said, and let him be for two days.
Then add to the lead seal. Therefore do not cease to tie the lead, as often as it is pressed into the thelil, until it is cut off and falls by itself without labor.
But if the thelil is thick of root, then in its incision there is a certain fear and timidity: especially because it is in the belly.
Nevertheless it is possible to cut into its middle. Then cauterize it, so that it does not return.
Then care for it, until the wound heals.
And beware of presuming to incise a thelil which is of a dark color, few sensations, and foul appearance, for indeed it is a cancerous abscess: and I will come with a memory of Cancer after this.
Chapter LII.
On the care of the prominent umbilicus.
The umbilicus becomes prominent for many reasons. Or from fissures of the skin, which is above the abdomen: and it exits through it an abscess, or intestine, according to what happens in other ruptures. Or from the blood that flows from the vein, or artery, according to what was previously mentioned. Or from the fatness enclosed in it.
But if it is due to a skin fissure, and the outlet is thin: then it is of a similar color to an abscess: and it is gentle, painless: and appears to be in different positions. And if it is due to the outlet of the intestine, then its position is with that which we have mentioned, of greater diversity. Therefore when you presume to touch it with your fingers, it disappears: then it returns, and perhaps it is with it a sound: and it is much magnified at the entrance of the bath, and the laborious movement.
But if it is due to moisture, it is gentle: then it does not disappear when you presume to touch it with your hand, nor is there any binding, nor addition.
But if it is due to blood, then with these signs an abscess appears to be of a dark color from the slope.
But if it is due to flesh born: then it is a heavy, thick, hard abscess, and it is shaped according to one quantity.
If indeed it is due to its moisture, then its touch is gentle.
And the operation in it is such that you should consider then, if the prominence of the umbilicus is due to blood from the Artery, or Vein, or moisture: then it is necessary to be prevented from its treatment. Chapter 62.
¶ On cutting for hernia aquosa.
Hydrocele is not present unless it is an accumulation of moisture in the sac under the skin of the testicle containing the epididymis, which is called the sac.
And sometimes it is in its own proper sac, which nature has prepared for itself in a part of the body, until it is thought to be something else, and that is another egg, and is the skin of the testicle between the sacs, which we have said: and this does not happen very often.

For if it is in the sac under the skin of the testicle which we have said, then the apostema is round to some length like the figure of an egg: and the testicle does not appear because the moisture contains it from every part.
If there is moisture within its own cloth, then the abscess is round with a part of the egg, and because of this, the man considers it to be another egg.
If there is moisture between the skin of the testicles and the white membrane, then it falls under the sense.

If you do not carefully examine it, there is no safety in the incision, so that water may not return.
But if you proceed with something from the outer part of its skin during your operation: then when you have completed the section, bring it back. Then gather two lips of the skin of the testicles with a stitch.

And if it is equal to you, that the operation be one, then do: then wipe off the blood. But if contradiction gives you in the hour of incision, or in the hour of cauterization, a hot abscess, or bleeding, or something else: then it is necessary for you to cure what contradiction gives you from that with the treatment that corresponds to it, according to what was previously mentioned.

Chapter 63.
¶ On the care of fleshy tumors.
Know that in the cut above this tumor, there is often brought about by fear a harmful outcome in many positions. Therefore it seems to me that its removal may be saved from that.
And I remember the operation in it, and the appearance of abscesses.
I say therefore that many abscesses occur in the bodies, from which the testicles are composed: and this is caused by many reasons, namely.
Either from an excess of sharp, or sharp, which is poured out to the testicles. Or from a blow.
And the appearance of abscesses is according to the color of the body, and there is no pain found in it: and it is a heavy abscess.
And perhaps it is a stone abscess, whose color is dark, and there is no feeling in it.
And sometimes it is caused by the knotting of the arteries, and their inflation: as has already been mentioned: or from the inflation of the veins.
What is caused by the inflation of the arteries can be known by the arrangement of the pus, when you press it with your fingers. And it is not necessary to touch it entirely.
However, that which is caused by the inflation of the veins is not dispersed from it at all when pressed with the fingers.
And now it is possible to make a cut of this kind and on the other flesh: and it is to separate the skin of the testicles. If therefore the siphon is consolidated with those fleshy parts, then it is necessary to draw out the siphon and cut it.
And if there is adhesion between something from the siphon, or in that which is between the vessels: then it is necessary to free the whole of that adhesion, and cut it with a round cut.
But if there is the birth of flesh in the place of adhesion which is behind: then it is necessary to cut all of it, and remove the siphon, as we said.
When therefore your operation is completed, then fill the wound with wool soaked in oil rose-scented, and wine: and then take care of it with the other care until it is healed.

Chapter 65.
§ On the care of the intestines.
The event of this injury is from a cut that occurred on the thigh, extended over the abdomen, in the part of the groin, from the inguinal region of the belly.
Why do the intestines descend from that rupture to one of the testicles? And this rupture is either from the thigh, or from its extension.
And these two types occur from many causes. Or from impact. Or from a sudden jolt. Or from a loud noise. Or from heavy lifting, and similar things.
And the sign when it is from the thigh's extension is that the intestines descend to one of the testicles. It is that which happens gradually over a long period of time, and does not happen suddenly: and it is an abscess equal in length and depth: therefore, because the thigh compresses the intestine.
And the sign of it when it is from the thigh's cut is because it causes pain to occur suddenly at the beginning: and it is an abscess different, appearing under the nearby skin: and that is because of the exit of the intestine, and its course to the outer thigh.
And sometimes it exits with the intestine fistula: and this is called an inguinal hernia, and a fistula: and sometimes it becomes with suppuration.
And sometimes feces run into the intestine, and are retained there: and it is with that harm to the weak: because it causes a dull pain, and especially when it is pressed.
And in the treatment of these kinds of illnesses with iron, there is fear: therefore it is necessary to avoid that case.
And the method of operation is, that you command the weak one, so that he may reduce the intestine with his own hand to the interior of its concavity, if it does not return. Then apply pressure to his neck between your hands: and raise his legs.
Then extend the skin that follows the skin to the upper parts, and dry the skin of the testicles entirely in length. Then fix two hooks in the two lips of the incision, according to what you need to open the incision with them: and the section should be in the amount that is possible so that an egg can come out from it.
Then scrape off the scrotum, and what is under the skin of the testicles, until when the white scrotum is detached from all parts: then insert your index finger into that which follows the testicle, in that which is between the white scrotum, which is under the skin of the egg, and between the white scrotum, and complete with it the adhesion that is in the posterior part of the egg.
Then move with your right hand to the interior of the skin of the testicles: and with this extend the white scrotum upwards, with your left hand: and raise the egg with the scrotum to the part of the incision: and order the minister to extend the egg upwards: and you dissolve the adhesion that is behind the completed solution.
And ask with your fingers, that there is nothing there from the unrolled intestine in the white scrotum hard. But if you find something from it: then push it down to the lower abdomen.
Then take a needle, in which there is a thick thread made of linen from ten threads: and insert it at the last scrotum, that is, the skin that follows the incision of the testicles: then cut the ends that project from the thread, until there are four threads. Then make some of them on top of some with the figure that is in the shape of a cross: and tie with them the scrotum, which we said was under the skin of the testicles by a strong ligament, until it cannot send any from the vessels that nourish them to send something to them: so that no hot abscess comes from it. And place the second ligature according to the first external ligature, about two fingers away from it. And after these two ligatures, let out from the sifach, which is under the skin of the testicles, an amount equal to the thickness of a finger: and cut the rest of it round and take out the egg.
Then cut in the lower part of the skin of the testicles, from which blood and pus flowed, as we mentioned in what was previously stated.
Then apply the immersed bandage in oil, and place it on the wound: and apply the ligature which we mentioned. And sometimes the white sifach which we mentioned is cauterized after its incision, in fear of blood flow. For this often happens. And let out the ligature until it falls off by itself.
But if its fall is delayed, then it should be rubbed with warm water: and place on it what we mentioned until it falls off.
Then care for the wound with the rest of the treatment of wounds, until it heals.

Chapter 67.
¶ On the hernia that occurs in the groin.
When a rupture occurs in the groin, as we have mentioned, and the location is elevated and does not extend down to the testicles from the intestines: and if it does extend, it is only slightly and returns to its normal position at all hours. Chapter 69.
On Castration.
You should know that castration is excommunicated in our law: and for this reason it was allowed to me not to remember it in my book: and the remembrance of it is not necessary, except for two reasons.
One of these is that it may be in the knowledge of a physician when he is asked about it: and that he may know its healing to him who has it happen to him.
And the other reason is that we often need castration of certain animals for our uses, because of our wool and milk, as cattle, horses, and similar animals.
I say therefore that castration is done in two ways. Either by crushing. Or through an incision and a cut.
However, in the method that is done by attrition, the way of operation is: we make the animal sit in hot water until the testicles are softened and soothed, and hang down; then rub them with your hand until they dissolve and do not appear under touch.
However, in castration by incision and cut, it is necessary that you hold the animal and press the skin of its testicles with your left hand.
Then tie the suspensorium, and cut over every part with one cut, until when the two eggs proceed: then cut them after you have peeled each one, and do not leave on them any of the sifaket except the fine sifac on the vessels.
And this method of castration is better than that which is done by attrition: because attrition perhaps leaves something in the testicles, therefore the animal desires copulation.
Then care for the wound until it heals.
Head 70.
¶ On the care of Hermaphrodite's two methods.
Hermaphrodites are from men according to two methods. One of them is because it appears in him that follows the space, or on the skin of the testicles, in that which is between two testicles, a shape like a woman's vulva, in which are hairs: and sometimes urine runs from that which is on the skin of the testicles.
In women, however, there is one species, and it is a woman's vulva on the breasts like small male testicles projecting to the outside: of which one is like the man's priapus, and two are like two testicles.
And the care of three species, two from men and one from women, is: because it is necessary that you cut the added flesh until the impression of them disappears. Then take care of the rest of the wounds with the same treatment.
However, in the second species of men, from which urine exits through the skin of the testicles, there is no operation and no treatment at all.

Chapter 72.
The alratica is that it is the vulva of a woman not pierced, or that there is a small opening. And it is either natural or accidental.

And knowledge of that is gained through the observation of a midwife, if the swelling appears to be near.

And place cotton on the two lips.

Then take a piece of cloth and soak it in oil, and place it on the spot: and let the woman cover it every day, so that it does not become hardened by another substance.
But if the sponge is thick, foul-smelling: then it must be separated from the thin branch of a myrtle leaf.
But if the swelling is from a piece of flesh born: then suspend it with hooks, and cut it: and let there be medicines with you that stop the flow of blood without causing pain, such as acacia, and dragon's blood, and a lump of frankincense mixed with egg white.
