Chapter 73.
Regarding the treatment of hemorrhoids, Atrehelil and Botor, red in the vaginas of women.
Hemorrhoids are the opening of the veins being dilated, until much blood flows from them continuously.
Therefore, when hemorrhoids are treated, they become Atrehelil: and I have already spoken about their division and signs in my previous work, and now I will say what kinds of them can be cured and what cannot.
I say therefore that hemorrhoids which are in the opening of the womb and do not appear to sense, then there is no cure with iron.
But those which are in the opening of the womb above which sensation falls, are those that can be cured.
Therefore, it is necessary to insert the woman into a cold house. Then extend Atrehelil with forceps, or with rough cloth, and cut them from their roots.
Then powder over them at the flow of blood from one powder of cut pieces without biting: such as acacia, and dragon's blood, and thistle, and similar to them.
Then press her feet against the wall for one hour. Then lay her down in cold water.

Then take barley flour, and mix it with honey and vinegar, and make a plaster with it on her back.
If therefore blood is removed with it, it is good: and if not, make feathers and sponges stick to her back without incision.
Then take wool and immerse it in the juice of tarathite, or the juice of arnoglossa, or the juice of the leaves of the alaulat tree, that is, the wild vine, with sea water, and make it stick to the wound.
When therefore the abscess has settled, then care for the place with ointments until it heals.
Albarth indeed is red like the heads of the alhaise, and has a rough appearance.
Therefore you must cut off what appears from it, as I said in the thistle evenly: and care for it until it heals.
Chapter LXXII

Chapter 70.
Of the teaching of obstetrics, how the fetuses are healed who have exited in a form not natural.
It is necessary for the obstetrician to know in the first place the form of natural birth.
For this is the sign of it that when you see a woman being pressed down to her lower parts, and desires to smell the air, and is relieved above her which is over her from birth, and hastens the exit of the fetus: then know that this birth is according to the form of nature, and its exit is on its head, and the placenta with it: or suspended, or hanging from the navel.
When therefore you see these signs, then it is necessary that her belly be pressed, so that the fetus may descend quickly.
For when it has descended on its head, it has descended with the placenta, and is cleansed of those superfluities by good cleaning.
But he who is other than this birth, is unnatural, undeserving.
For when sometimes the fetus exits above its feet, and exits the body before its head, and its body, and one of its hands, or one of its feet: or exits its head and one of its hands: or exits its belly: and perhaps it turns over on its neck, and similar from undeserving figures.
It is therefore necessary for the midwife to be wise and clever in all these matters, and to beware of error and deception: and I am showing every figure from them, and what kind of nature is in it, and how it is signified by it, and stands above it.
When the child exits its head with its own natural exit, and becomes violent upon the woman, and difficult birth becomes for her, and you see that its strength is already weakened: then make her sit on a seat, or let women hold her: and vapor of wormwood with fenugreek decoction, and with wet oils.

The exit of the embryo is upon its feet. When the fetus exits upon its feet, then it is necessary to push it upwards: afterwards, he should gradually turn the fetus: then, he should balance it.
Then, he should take one of its feet and extend it gradually.
When therefore they exit up to the hips, then command him, that he be compressed, and make her sneeze with a wet cloth: it will exit, if God wills.
And if it does not exit with what we have said, then reduce the fetus gradually, until you place him according to the natural form. For he will exit then with an easy exit.

The exit of the fetus upon its knees and hands. When it exits according to this form, then he should gradually insert his hands. The exit of the fetus hangs laterally from her hands. Her hand is supported in the reduction. If she cannot reduce it, then lift her up and make her walk.
If indeed she cannot walk, then make her lie on the bed: and shake her legs with great force.

If she accepts it in labor, then make her sit on a chair. Then strive in the reduction of her hand and equalize the fetus according to its natural shape: and make the woman sneeze, and tell her to compress herself until it comes out.

Chapter 76.
Rememoration of the extraction of a dead fetus.
When you care for a dead fetus with that which I said in the division of medication, and it does not exit, and you must use an operation with your hand, then you should consider.
If therefore the woman is of sound virtue, and is not with any of those accidents from which danger is feared for her: then it must be that the woman lies on the bed, on her back, and her head is inclined downwards, and her legs are raised: and the assistant holds her from two parts, or she is tied to the bed, so that her body is not drawn out during the extraction of the fetus.
Then moisten the mouth of the womb with warm oils mixed with a lot of mucilage, and of fenugreek, and of the seed of linseed.
Then let the midwife anoint her hand with these oils and mucilages: then she should insert it into the womb with ease. Then let her seek with her the place where she can hook the nails from the fetus, and the suitable places to that.
Therefore, if the fetus is prepared to descend upon its head: then fix hooks in its eyes, or on its neck, or in its mouth, or in its palate, or under its beard, or in its shoulder blades, or in nearby ribs, and under its armpits.
But if the descent is upon its feet: then in the shinbone, and in its middle ribs.
And it is necessary that he holds the hook with his right hand: and place the curve of it in what is between the fingers of his left hand: and insert it with his left hand with facility, and fix the hook in one of those places which we mentioned, until he arrives at the empty place.
Then he should fix another hook, or a third if necessary, on its opposite side, so that the contraction is equal, and does not lean to one side.
Then the extension should be made equally, and not be extension only in a straight line, but move to all parts, so that his exit is facilitated: just as it is done with the tooth when it is being extracted.
And it is necessary in that which is between them, that the extension be softened. If a part of it is held back from that: then it is necessary for the midwife to put some fingers with oil on them, and insert them from one side, so that she rolls it with what is being held back.
If therefore a part of the fetus comes out, then they should change the hooks to another place which is higher: do this until the whole fetus comes out.
If therefore the hand comes out before the other, and it is not possible to reduce it, because of its tightness: then it is necessary for a cloth to be rolled over it. Then take it out until when it comes out whole, cut it at the joint of the foot, or at the elbow: and so it is necessary to do in the other hand, and in two feet.
If the fetus's head is large, or if there is a constriction at the outlet, or if there is water accumulated in its head: then it is necessary to insert the Spatula-like spiny instrument between the fingers, and strike with it against the head, and remove the water; or to break it with the instrument called Almisdac, whose form comes with the forms of the other instruments in the chapter that follows.
Similarly, if the fetus is naturally of large head: then it is necessary to separate the alengengematu: or to extract it with the misdach, as we said. Then extract the bones with forceps.
If the head emerges and is constricted at the fork: then it is struck, until the moisture that is in the chest flows out.
If it does not constrict, nor obey the outlet: then cut the head in small pieces, as much as possible for you.
If there is an abscess below the belly, or if there is dropsy in it: then it is necessary to pierce it, until the moisture flows out of it.
If indeed the fetus is above its feet: then its extraction is easy, and its direction towards the mother's bones is light.
If it is constricted at the belly, or the chest: then it is necessary to extract it with the cloth that you have wrapped around your hand: and strike the belly, or the chest, until what is in them flows out.
If the other limbs are removed, and the head returns: then the midwife should insert her left hand. Therefore, if the mother's bones are open: then she should insert her hand into the depth of the mother's bones, and seek with it the head, and draw it out with her fingers until the mother's bones: then she should insert a hook, or two hooks, into it, and draw it out with them.
If the mother's mouth is closed due to an abscess that has occurred to her, then it is not necessary for her to be forced upon it, but rather it is necessary at that time to administer a moist effusion, a thick one: and apply ointments, and let her sit in waters that will soften and moisten.
If the fetus is on its side, then it is possible to do so: then what we said about the living fetus will be administered.
If it is not possible to do that, then it is cut into pieces and removed.
And it is necessary not to let anything remain inside the secondina at all.
Therefore, when you have completed your operation, then what we said about hot abscesses that occur in the mothers will be administered.
If bleeding occurs, then it should go down into stop-bleeding waters, and the rest of the cure will be administered.
And indeed I have seen a woman whose belly had a dead fetus: then she became pregnant over it with another, afterwards the other fetus also died. Therefore it happened to her after a long time that an abscess occurred in her navel, and it swelled up until it was open: and she began to emit pus.
Therefore I was called for her cure, and I treated her for a long time: and the wound did not heal.
Therefore I placed on it some strong attracting ointments: and the bone came out of the place. Then some days passed by her, and another bone came out. Therefore I was amazed from there, since in the belly there is no bone.
Therefore I thought that they were from the bones of the dead fetus.
I have examined the wound, and extracted many bones, with the woman being in her better conditions: and she has now lived for a long time in this manner, and she is now discharging some pus from the place.
And I did not apply this foreign matter here, unless there is knowledge and assistance from the skill and craft of the physician artist with his hand for the cure.
Chapter 77.
¶ On the forms of necessary instruments in the extraction of the fetus.
The form of the pulley that opens the womb.
Here below is the form of the Strictorium, by which the rib bones are equalized, with two pulleys evenly placed on the two ends of two wooden rods. However, this pulley should be more delicate than the Strictorium: and it is made from either ebony or from smooth wood.
And the width of each wood is as if two fingers: and the edge of each of them is as if one finger, and the length of each of them is a palm and a half: and in the middle of the two woods are two additions of the same type of wood, which have already been fixed in both, whose length is a palm and a half or more, and the width of each of them is as if two fingers, or more.
And these two additions are inserted into the mother's ribs, so that it opens with them when you turn the two pulleys.
Another form similar to it, but more delicate and lighter.
It should be made from ebony or smooth wood, according to the similarity of a pair of tongs. However, at the end of it there should be two additions, as you see above: and the length of each addition is as if a palm: and the width of each of them is as if two fingers.
When you want to open the mother's womb with it, then make the woman sit on the bed, with her feet hanging down, opening what is between her legs. Then insert these two additions connected into the womb: and you are holding the lower end of the instrument between her thighs. Then open your hand with the instrument, as you do with forceps, equally according to the quantity that you want from the opening of the mother's womb, until the midwife does what she wants.
The form of another tilt than they said of the ancients, namely the form of Impelling which impels the fetus.
The form of Almisdac, by which the large head is crushed: and it resembles forceps, which have teeth at the end, as you see.
And sometimes it becomes a tongue, like forceps according to this form, as you see, which have teeth like the teeth of a saw, by which it cuts and crushes.
The form of having one spine.
The form of having two spines.
The form of Spatumilis which has two ends for cutting off the head.
The form of two Spatumilium and also pullers.
These instruments are all exercised, and the more multiplied their species, and they are prepared by the craftsman, is faster to their operation, and higher among men, because of their quantity.
Therefore do not despise from them an instrument, that it is prepared by you. Their necessity is indeed inexcusable.
Chapter 78.
On the Extraction of a Second Tooth.
When the second tooth is retained during childbirth, then it is necessary to instruct the weak one to hold their breath. Then make her sneeze with a wet cloth: and press your hand on her mouth and nose. If it comes out this way, it is good.
If not: then take a pot, and pierce the lid with a hole: and put in it opening drugs for the mother's mouth, such as calamint, rue, and aneth, and chamomile, and seseli, and cassia wood, and centaury: take all these herbs, or some of them, and mix them with water, and put them on fire.
Then put a reed bundle on the hole of the lid of the pot, and the other end in the mother's mouth: and hold it until the steam reaches the hollow of the mother.
Then make her sneeze, as we said. The second tooth will come out with ease.
If however it remains after this treatment, and does not come out: then instruct the midwife to immerse her hand in sisamin oil, or a thick decoction of althea. Then she should insert it into the vulva, and seek for the second tooth with it. When therefore she finds it, then she should take it, and stretch it slowly.
If however it is attached deep in the mother's womb, then she should insert her hand, as we said, until when she finds the second tooth, and takes it out slowly according to straightness, so that the mother does not fall during strong attraction: indeed it is necessary, that it be changed with ease to the right and left sides: then add in the amount of attraction. It dies then and is preserved, and avoids sticking.
If the mother's mouth is closed, as we have already mentioned: treat it with nasal irrigation and with the herbal remedy from the bowl.
If however it does not come out with all that we have mentioned, then be careful not to exhaust it with repeated extraction.
However, it is necessary that what comes out from the mother's mouth should be tied to the woman's groin. Then cleanse it with the Tetra Pharmakon ointment. For indeed it will rot it after days, and dissolve, and come out.
However, when it rots, the bad smell is removed from the stomach and head, and harms that weak one. Therefore it is necessary that appropriate fumigations should be administered to it.
However, some of the ancients have already experienced the fumigation of nasturtium and dried figs.
The form of the instrument by which the woman is fumigated during retention of Secundine and menstrual blood.
Let a hollow instrument like a pipe or a jar be made from clay: and place its wide end over the fire: and the fumigation should be placed on the branches: hold it until that fumigation is consumed: and repeat another.
Chapter 79.
On the treatment of the unperforated anus.
Many children are born, and their anuses are not perforated, which he has already covered with soft shavings. Therefore it is necessary that the midwife should pierce it with her finger: and if not, she should pierce it with a sharp spatula: and beware of the hand, lest it touch it.
Then place a wool soaked in wine and oil on top of it. Then care for it with the ointment until it is healed.
But if you fear that it will swell, then place a lead tube with a hole in the opening for many days, and remove it when the boy wants to go out.
And now swelling of the anus also occurs from the consolidation of the wound or abscess. Therefore it is necessary to cut away that consolidation, then care for it with what we said about the cure and lead.
Chapter 80.
¶ On the treatment of fistulas that occur in the lower part.
Fistulas that occur in the lower part are Nodosities and Swelling which occur near the anus, deforming: or in the space of one part: and it is a fistula, or more.
When therefore that nodosity is opened, water flows out from it, or thin pus.
And sometimes they are from these penetrating fistulas. Therefore the penetrating ones are known by what comes out from defecation, and softness, when an invalid is used for defecation: and perhaps it comes out from those worms.
And they are from these fistulas when they are in the space penetrating up to the bladder, and up to the vagina. And they are from these penetrating up to the junction of the hip, and up to the tailbone.
From that however by which it is known that the penetrating fistula reaches to the anus, even from the non-penetrating one, is that you insert your finger into the anus: and you insert a thin probe into the fistula from air, or iron: when there is no twisting.
If there is twisting in it, then insert a thin lead probe or a horsehair needle from the horses' hair into it, until you feel the probe, or the needle in your finger.
If you do not feel it entirely, and nothing protrudes from the opening due to excretion, nor is there wind or worms as I said, then you know that it is not punctured: therefore hasten to treatment.
And when the fistula is punctured up to the bladder or the urethra, then its signification is the exit of urine from it, and its prevention from this so that the place can consolidate with medicines.
But if it is punctured up to the hip joint or the hip bone: then its sign is that the probe reaches there, if there is no twisting in it up to the bone: and the discovery of pain in the circumference of the part, and that pus always escapes from it: and that medication does not hold in it, nor consolidates with ointment.
And in all these fistulas that penetrate, there is no cure at all: and the cure of them is a labor and vanity to him, from foolish doctors, on which it is based.
But in that which is not punctured, and is not ancient, there is hope of healing with a splint: according to what I tell you, and I have already tested: and it is, that the sick person lie under your hands on his back: and raise his legs up above his hips, and his hips be inclined towards his belly. Then he will insert the thin lead probe, or of air, if there is twisting in the fistula, until you know where the probe reaches.
But if the sick person feels it around the anus, then you must insert your finger into the anus.
If you feel that the prick has already penetrated itself through your finger, apart from what you felt between your finger and it, or flesh: then you must certainly know that it is a prick, and therefore do not labor in it, since there is no cure for it, as we have said.
But they said that flesh is healed in some men, and from the medication by which it is hoped for healing, it is, to apply a thin hot cauterizing iron according to the size of the Fistula, as has been mentioned before, and to insert the burning one into the Fistula, until it reaches around the anus. Then repeat that twice or three times, until you know that all the added flesh has been burned, which are like the filtered feathers that are similar to the quill of a bird's wing.
Then care for that with rolled linens in butter, until those burned flesh comes out: then care for that with ointments generating and consolidating flesh.
If therefore it is healed, good.
And if not, then it will never be healed with other cure.
And if it comes out and does not reach to your finger which is in the anus, and is between it and the thick, slimy skin from flesh or flesh: and you see the Fistula in what follows the surface of the skin, then dry the skin from the beginning of the Fistula, and you go drying with the tent which is in the Fistula, until the drying reaches where the end of the tent comes out, and the tent is freed and falls.
Then clean those filtered flesh which are similar to the quill of a bird's wing, so that nothing remains from them.
If, however, the blood adheres to you and dissolves between you and the operation, so that you separate those flesh: then it is better and faster to cauterize it with fire, or with sharp medicine.
Because the cauterizer with fire gathers good conditions, it adds burns of those flesh, and separation of blood, and drying of moisture.
Then care for it with unfolded bandages in butter, or crushed bread, until the place emits pus, and those burnt flesh come out into pus.
Then care for the wound then with consolidating ointments, generating hard flesh: and they are medicines in which there is stipticness and drying.
For when it is restored, then already it is healed: and do not fear repetition.
If however the fistula has already reached to the depth of the anus, and is stretched from the excess of the body: then insert your finger into the anus, and inquire with it.
If therefore you feel a touch, and between you, and it is a linen from sifac, or flesh, and is near penetration: then there is no operation in that, except according to the way of trust and hope.
That is, because it is administered in it one of three ways: either to cauterize it, as we said: or to separate it, until you reach the depth of it, so that it is possible for you to insert bandage, and healing from nearby. And do not proceed much with the cut, so that you do not cut the muscle containing the anus, and it happens that the weak exit of excretion without will. Then care for it with what we said.
Perhaps it will be healed: or extend the same bandage, and cleanse it after you have dried it nearly up to near the anus, as we have said, or with another sharp-ended instrument. Then cleanse those filtered fleshy parts which are in the incision, as far as you can with thorough scrubbing.
Then attempt the healing of the wound entirely with the incision, and at the upper opening where it is solidified: and there remains an open fistula in the inner part of the anus, and it will be lighter on the weak one.
And sometimes the fistula will follow in this manner: and it is, when you insert the probe into the fistula: and it is on the side of the anus around the surface of the body with the skin and margin of the anus: then take the probe with sharp-ended extremities, which is like a needle made of aleskef, that is, prepared leather, in this form. And insert it into it a wrapped thread from five threads, and about it. Then insert the probe with thread into the fistula, until it reaches its concavity.
If therefore it penetrates into the inner margin of the anus near, then draw out the thread from that opening: so that you insert your finger into the anus, and draw out the end of the thread, and gather both extremities together: and tie both, and let it go on one day, or two days: and as much as the thread falls on the flesh, tie it well, until those fleshy parts which are between the two ends of the thread fall off: then care for the wound, until it is solidified, and healed.
But if the opening of the fistula is not penetrating: then make it penetrate in whatever way is prepared for you, unless it is very deep. For it is not necessary for you to do this because of the shoulder, so that you do not cut it.
Then treat her as we said, until she is healed.
The shape of the Spatula's spinous process, in which the fistula is found, has a very sharp curvature, and the other part is not sharp, so that it does not cut what is not necessary, as you see.
Chapter 81.
On the stitching of hemorrhoids, from which blood flows from their incisions: and the treatment of fissures.
Hemorrhoids are of two kinds. For indeed they are inside the anus, like coal or plums: or rather they are like the grains of wheat. And from them there are small and large ones: and blood flows from them always, and it is one, and they are many. And they are outside the anus, and at its extremities.
However, those that are outside the anus, are for the most part few in moisture, from which yellowish water flows, or little blood flows constantly: and they are according to the color of the body.
And the treatment of those that are inside the anus is, that you order the sick person to sit on a stool: and it is expressed, until the anus opens, and the fissures appear to you. Therefore also hang them with hooks: or hold them with your nail. Then cut them at their roots.
But if they are not held in them with hooks, because of their moisture and softness: then take them with a rough cloth, or with a rough cloth made of double woolen fabric, and extract them with your fingers. Then, make an incision on them and apply hot powder on top of the incision some powders, so that they remain in place as a cauterizing agent. Or cauterize them according to what was mentioned in the previous chapter on cauterization. Then care for them with the remaining cure until they are healed.
If the patient does not obey the call to defecate, then apply a small amount of clyster in a clyster containing a small amount of bitter herbs, so that it cleans out what is in the anus and obeys the call to defecate quickly when the patient excretes.
But if the thorns are outside the anus, then the matter is light and easy: and it is to take them with your nail, or take them with a spoon, and cut them. Then care for them with what we mentioned, until they are healed.
And if one dislikes the incision with a knife, then it is necessary for the administrator to suture them according to this method. Take an untwisted thread, and insert it into the needle. Then take out the thorns to the top, and make it penetrate with the needle from the root on the other side: and untwist the two ends of the thread in the lower part of the needle, and they should be wide apart: and tie the thorns with a strong knot. Then tie the thread, and take out the needle.
Do this with all the thorns, and take out one from them: and do not let it run out of it to prevent excessive bleeding.
Then place a piece of cloth soaked in rose oil or carron oil on the anus and place it on the anus: and order the sick person to rest. Then take it out when it falls off.
When, therefore, the hernias fall, take care of them with ointments and other means of healing until they are healed.
¶ On the Care of Wounds. For often, due to the dryness of dung and the constriction of nature, many wounds occur.
When, therefore, they are dry and do not respond to medicine: then it is necessary to scrape them with the spatula of Spatam, or with your ointment, until they become moist, and remove the upper skin that prevents their consolidation. Then care for them until they consolidate as they should.
But if they do not consolidate: then repeat them with a stronger blade than the first, until they bleed much, and then peel them, and care for them until they are healed.

Chapter 82.
You should know that an Almirmar is not other than a round knot similar to the head of a nail: and it forms throughout the body, especially in the lower parts of the feet, and fingers: and pain occurs from them during walking.
Therefore it is necessary to follow what is around the head of the nail, and hold it with forceps, or with a hook, and remove it from its root.
Then care for that: and if you wish to cauterize it according to what preceded in its chapter.
From the hernias that are dry, one is a small elevation, rough, filtered, round above the surface of the body. And often they occur in the hands of children.
And its care is, that you extend the hernias, and cut it: or string it with a silk thread: or with hair, until it falls. And if you wish, cauterize it according to what was previously mentioned with fire or with sharp medicine: and now the ingrown hairs will be eradicated, and not with the instrument that I say.
The ant is also a small bumpy, porous, and rough surface on the body, leaning into a very deep valley: and when it finds cold, it feels like an ant bite in it, and it happens throughout the body: and it does the most harm to the hands.
And its cure is that you take a cannula from the feather of a goose, or the feather of a strong-winged bird: and place the cannula on the ant, until it contains a circle of the cannula from its parts. Then turn your hand with the cannula until it separates what is in the circumference of the ant: and place it in the deep flesh, and remove the ant from its root.
And if you wish, do it with the cannula of air, or iron, according to this form.
Let the upper cannula be pulling the dull uncovered, so that it is relieved from the apprehension of its height and its rotation.
And if you wish, cauterize the ant according to what was previously mentioned in the cauterization of ingrown hairs in the chapter on cauterization.
Chapter 83.
§ On the forms of instruments that are administered to cleansing in the ailments of the anus, and the solution of the belly, and the colon.
Sometimes cleansing is made of silver, or of gold-plated, or of bronze, or of hammered.
And sometimes it is made of these instruments small and large, according to those in which they are administered.
That which is administered for the treatment of small children should be of a small quantity: and those whose anuses are weak or painful, so also their stools.
A large stool.
The cannula of his, that is, the upper part in which the uterus is tied, should be large according to this manner: and there should be a distinction for it so that the uterus is tied as you see, and the lower part which enters into the anus, should be deaf, that is, not open, soft, rather drawing towards subtlety: and in one of its sides there should be two holes, and in the other side there should be one hole.
And the width of the hole should be according to the thickness of the rays, and a little less, and the uterus in which the medicines are placed from the animal's bladder: or from the small paper which is according to the form of the asafetida root, whose root is one palm.
And it should be pierced through the holes as it unfolds, and there should be a space which is the thickness of a finger between each hole. When therefore it is placed in that uterus, it should be tied at the head of the stool with a strong constriction between two distinctions. Then draw up the stool with it.
And this is the form of the circle of these utensils and holes drawn here.
But the quality of drawing up the stool with it is: that you fill the jug or bladder from the medicine which is heated according to the quantity of the weak tolerance: and beware that it is not very hot, or very cold.
Then the sick person should lie face downwards on their back, and raise their legs upwards: and place a cloth or linen underneath them.

Then remove the Clisteris and raise the sick person's legs against the wall.
If the medicine makes him want to go to the bathroom, then hold onto it as much as possible. And if he sleeps with it all night, it is more likely to be effective.
But if the Clisteris is used during the illness of diarrhea, and he wants to go quickly: then repeat the Clisteris until he is healed.
But if there are hemorrhoids or painful abscesses in the anus, then the Clisteris should be fine, very mild, and made from the same Clisteris that children are treated with.
And this is the form of a fine Clisteris on top of which there is tight skin.
Chapter 82.
I have already said in the division of the treatment of wounds that it was convenient for this book, and now I will say here the treatment of them with hand, and with medicines according to the complement.
I say therefore that wounds are diversified according to how they become wounds, and according to the place on which the wound falls.
The wounds that are made frequently are like the throw of a stone; they are either from the cutting of a sword or knife, or by striking with a lance, a stick, or an arrow, and similarly from many other things.
However, the wounds that are made according to the parts of the body are like a wound that falls on the head, neck, chest, abdomen, or back, and similarly from other limbs.
And I am telling the cures for some wounds, so that I may set forth a reason and rule for all other wounds.
And I will begin with simple head wounds, because the memory of compound ones will come at the beginning of the third chapter.
I say therefore. When a simple wound occurs in the head and there is no fracture of bone, consider whether it is from the throw of a stone or similar things, and if it has already broken the skin only: and it is a large wound, and you fear for the bad outcome of a hot abscess: then hurry, and let blood from the cephalic vein immediately: and do not delay in doing so: and remove from him according to the amount of its power: if there is nothing preventing bleeding from phlebotomy, especially if it is little blood that flows out of the wound. And let the bleeding be from the opposite side of the wounded part.
And let the bleeding be from the opposite side of the wounded part. And let the weak one beware of overfilling himself, and wine, and coarse foods.
But if something prevents him from having a diet, then he should be reduced in his food, and not approach meat, nor wine.
And put on the wound if it happens to him an abscess hot, cotton infused in rose oil alone, or with wine in which there is astringency.
If you are secure from the hot abscess, then place on the wound, if it is recent with its own blood, and has not changed the air, the powder that I will tell you about shortly: and if it has already changed the air, then place on it certain ointments until it heals.
But if the wound is large, or is from a sword cut, and similar: and if the lips of it do not come together with gauze, then stitch it together according to what I will tell you about wounds of the belly regarding their stitches.
But if the wound has already been removed from the bone, and hangs, and there is no retention of it except in a small sling: then cut it. Then care for the wound with medicines, and restore hard flesh to the place of skin, and order the sick person to be fed on foods in which there is bulk, such as heads and cooked wheat, until it is like a porridge: and similar things.
If you find putrefaction in the skin, and it does not stick to bone: then cut off the whole putrefied part, and throw it away: then care for that.
But if there are these wounds an artery, or a vein from which the blood flows: and it is not cut through by medicines, then examine the artery. Then if you find it not cut, then secure it with a ligature, or tie it. But if necessity provokes when it does not bring what we said: then cauterize it, until the blood is cut off.
But if these wounds are small, simple, then the matter of them is easy, light: so that powder is placed on them this powder: because it consolidates them before it changes them from the air.
The method of making a powder for flesh wounds is as follows: Recipe for treating a wound with the juice of garlic, two parts of dragon's blood, and three parts of unburnt chalk: Grind all the ingredients thoroughly and sift them. Apply this mixture to the wound and bind it tightly with a bandage until it adheres well and coagulates with the blood.
Then bind the wound from above with bandages and leave it undisturbed until it heals, without removing the bandage prematurely to prevent reopening of the wound. For this remedy will not be removed until the wound is healed.
And sometimes chalk alone can perform the same function in many large wounds when it is applied and bound, especially when the wound is fresh and still bleeding, as air has not yet altered it.
If the wound has already been altered by air, especially in the summer season, then this powder is not suitable for use: therefore, treat it with the remedy mentioned earlier and apply some digestive ointments or bandages made of barley flour mixed with water and honey until the pus is expelled. Then continue treating it with the remaining remedies until it heals completely.
If indeed a small fragment of bone is embedded in the wound, then remove it with a pair of forceps: and I will now describe the treatment for broken bones in the following section.
¶ On Wounds of the Head
If a wound occurs on the head, there is no difference in treatment between a simple wound and a more complex one.
If the nerve or artery has already been cut, there is no cure for it except with strong hemostatic agents such as zinc, zegi, and similar substances. Because they harm the eyes and contract them.
And do not place anything very cold on the wound at all, for the substance of the nerves is cold and its continuity is with the brain, which is higher than the limbs: and let that which heals be taken from medicines that are mild, such as chalk soaked in sweet water several times infused with oil, or with rose oil and turpentine, when it is washed even with sweet water; and the remaining mineral stones, in this manner, and wet ointments.
But if the wound is large, then administer a suture: or cut the lips of it with cotton. Then take care of it until it heals.
But if the wound is deep, or it occurs in it a sinus in the lower part of it, in which already pus has accumulated, then perforate it in a more depressed place in it.
But if the artery has already been cut in the wound and blood flowed from it: then separate, or dry it, and ligate it: or cauterize it, if necessity requires this.
But if the spinal cord of the neck has already occurred, or all of it, and the larynxes have been saved: then gather the lips of the skin with a suture on a tube of the neck, and do not touch the neck, but rather even it, and reduce it to its natural shape. Then bind it with a proper binding, and leave it for several days. Then take care of it with ointments in which there is styptic and drying, until it heals.
But if the wound has already made an impression on the bone, then seek it: then if there are fragments of bone in it, extract all of them, or what you can from them: and that which is not prepared, leave it, until the wound rots, and its discharge separates and heals.
If the wound is recent, then apply powder on top of the powder I mentioned. But if it appears that there is a bone in the wound and a fistula forms, then treat it along with the one I mentioned in its own chapter.
Chapter on Wounds in Forceps.
If it is a puncture from a lance or knife, and you see its depth, then consider. If therefore gas escapes from the wound when it is difficult for the patient to breathe from it, then know that the wound is mortal.
But if it is not deep and is recent with its own blood, then do not apply powder to it from the first hour, nor bind it up, so that the blood does not remain in its depth and return to the heart and kill the patient: but apply an attractive ointment to it and dissolve it twice a day.
But if indeed the ointment is not present to you, then place a piece of old cloth in the wound opening, so that it sucks out what escapes from it due to moisture: and make the patient sleep over the wound, so that what collects in it may pass.
But if indeed three days or more have already passed since the wound, and no spasm has occurred to the patient, nor a bad trembling of the heart, nor tightness in breathing, and you see other dispositions of it are good: then know that the wound is safe. Therefore treat it and with liniments, and with the rest of the cure, until it heals.
But if indeed the healing of it is excused, and it always opens, then know that it has already become a fistula. Therefore, treat it from its own chapter.
And if the wound is from an incision by a sword or knife, and it is simple on the surface of the chest or back: then treat it with what preceded from stitching, if it is large; or with powder, if it is small.
But if it has already made an impression on the bone, and it has cut from there fragments: then inquire about the wound, and hasten to remove those fragments, if they are separated. But if they are not separated, then leave them until the wound rots, for it is relieved by their extraction.
But of the remaining wounds that have occurred in other members, the judgment in their treatment is the same as what we said.
Concerning wounds of the belly, and the exit of the intestines, and their exit.
The rupture that occurs in the belly is great, and medium, and small.
From a great one, sometimes the intestine exits, or the number of intestines.
Therefore, their introduction is, and their stitching, more violent and difficult.
And the small rupture also becomes difficult from another way. Therefore, it follows that their reduction is difficult, if you do not hasten to their introduction to their place immediately: because it swells, opens, and fills up: therefore, its entrance is difficult.
For this reason, the medium rupture becomes better: because with it, the reduction of the intestine is not difficult, as it is difficult in these two kinds.
You should know that the stitching of the belly is according to four modes.
Two common sutures meet in the ventral suture, and in the suture of other bodily wounds; and two other sutures properly communicate with the remaining wounds. However, they are more proper with the ventral suture; and I tell you each one with explanation, and declaration.
I therefore say, because when a wound is small, and something escapes from it into the intestine, and it becomes difficult to reduce it: then that is for one of two reasons. Either because of the smallness of the rupture, as we said: or because there is inflation in the intestine due to cold air.
When therefore it is so, then it is necessary to heat it, so that you submerge the sponge, or wet cloth in warm water alone. Or boil it in water with vinegar, and cumin, and clove, and embrocation with it the intestine, until the inflation is resolved.
Sometimes that wine in which there is astringency does it: and it is better than water alone in the resolution of inflation.
When therefore you see the inflation already resolved, then moisten the intestine with the water in which it was boiled, or warm. For through that it soothes the entrance of his stomach with a small amount.
But if the return of his escape after this cure is excused, then find in small rupture, with the instrument by which hemorrhoids are cut.
And the first cure is better when prepared, than section: and it is not forced to cut after necessity and lack of instrument.
Let one part of his be curved, sharp, and another part not sharp, and the extremity subtle not with subtlety Spatumilis, but rather obtuse: and it is that which resembles a lancet, as you see.
When a wound becomes large and enters the intestine, it is necessary to reduce it back to its natural shape in its proper place, if possible, because this is better.
When indeed the rupture is large in the lower part of the abdomen, then you should make the person lie on their back and place their higher legs above their head. And if it is in the upper part of the abdomen, then place their head and make their higher chest higher than their lower chest.
And similarly if the rupture is in one of the two parts of the abdomen, then place your attention and always consider this, that the part where the wound is should be higher than the other part.
And thus you should administer it in large wounds and in medium-sized wounds.
But in small wounds, place it according to what is prepared for you.
Then make sure that a pious assistant is present between your hands who holds the rupture entirely with their hand: and gather their lips. Then remove from it to him who follows a suture, something after something: and this is the common method of suturing one at a time.
And it is, that you take a needle, or a number of needles according to the size of the wound. Then let go from the end of the rupture a quantity of a finger's width, that is, a doctor's: and fix the needle one on the other, with two ends of the skin, with two ends of the sinew that is under the skin from the insides, until you make it penetrate from another part, and now you have gathered two ends of the skin, and two ends of the sinew: and four rows are made.
Then tie with a double thread around the wound, several times from two parts at once, until the two lips of the wound are gathered together decently by aggregation.
Then let go of the thickness of the finger, and fix a needle in it: afterwards, straighten it with the thread, as you did with the needle first. Therefore do not cease to do this with that which you need from the couch, until you complete the constriction of the wound entirely.
And let the needles be of medium thinness between thickness and fineness: for a thin needle very quickly enters flesh: and thick ones are difficult to pierce skin: therefore it is necessary that they should be of medium thinness in thinness and thickness.
And it is not necessary, that the needle should be fixed in both extremities of the skin near, much: so that flesh does not quickly enter, and the wound is opened before its consolidation, and they do not extend even with the suture, so that the wound is not prevented from consolidation.
Then cut the end of the needle, so that they do not wound the weak one while asleep: and put pullovers of cloth from all parts, which hold the ends of the needle: and let them go, until you know that the wound is already consolidated.
And this kind of suture with the couches is indeed more suitable for small wounds. For it is enough in their suture one needle, or two, or about those.
But the second suture is common, so that it gathers with the suture the ends of four: ends, two of skin, and ends two of silk in one vice, with the needle in which is the thread rolled up equally in thinness and thickness.
Then, when you have penetrated with the needle these four extremities, reduce the needle from the part from which you began, so that a thread soaked in oil may fall from the upper part of the wound: so that it may be a suture, just as they string together pieces of cloth. And place between every suture an amount of thickness equal to the little finger.
This suture, however, is known by men.
And with this suture, I closed the wound that had occurred to a man in his belly, who had been wounded with a knife, and the wound was a tear larger than a palm: and it had exited from the intestines about two palms from the middle intestine, and there was a tear in the middle of the belly.
I therefore reduced it after it had stood the intestine of his outside the wound for twenty-four hours.
The wound therefore became healed in the space that was about fifteen days: and I took care of him, and he was healed: and he lived after that for many years, returning to his former dispositions.
And the physicians had judged that he would not be healed.
And it was a miracle that I did not take care of him with ointment. Because I was in a place where ointment was not found, nor anything from the medicines. I therefore placed on the wound an old cloth twice a day, and I took care of his washing with honey water, until he was healed.
Two however species of suture proper I will say according to the narrative of the language.
And it is, so that you begin with a sharp suture: and you insert the needle from the outer to the inner part.
When therefore the needle penetrates the skin, and goes into the muscle going along the length and width of the whole body: let go the end of the suture in the side in which you inserted the needle, and make it to penetrate in the other extremity from the inner part to the outer in the other end.
When you have made it penetrate, then make it penetrate thus in the same extreme part from the outer side to the inner: and leave off the extreme part which is in this side, and make the acum penetrate into the other extreme part from the inner side to the outer: and make it penetrate with your penetration as you make it penetrate in that extreme part of the mirach, which is in its part, until it penetrates into the whole of it.
Then also begin from this same side, and pull out that itself with its extreme part, which is from the sifac on another side and outside, and draw out the acum from the skin which it has penetrated.
Then bring it back into that skin, and pull out that extreme part of the sifac, which is on another side, with this extreme part of the mirach: and draw it out from the skin which is on its part, and make one with the other, and make it one after the other, until you have pulled out all of it outside according to that example.
And the last of this stitching is that you stitch with the stitches by which they stitch the skins: so that you stitch one extreme part of the skin on one side with the other, until you have completed it.
The second kind of proper stitching, which he said Galen.
This his speech was told in order that you stitch it according to the likeness by which some physicians stitch them, so that they gather all part to its suitable corresponding part by nature: and they apply the extreme part of the sifac to its other extreme part, and the extreme part of the mirach to its other extreme part. And that is done according as I tell you.
You should make a groove in the tip of the mira near you from the outer side, and make it penetrate to the inner part within that soil, and release its two ends. Then turn the mira back, and make it penetrate from the outer side to the inner part within both ends.
Then turn both of them back, and also make them penetrate from the inner part to the outer side within both ends, in the two other ends of the mira which are on the opposite side.
And this method of suture is better than a common easy suture, and it is a suture preceded by remembrance.
Therefore, this is also the word of Galen.
And some said. The suture of the belly should be corrected with two needles. Which is, that you insert one thread into both of them: and begin with the insertion of the needle which is with you, and make it penetrate to the other side, according to the suture of those who equalize the hides.
And you should know that when the rupture is in the middle of the belly: then its suture is more difficult than the other parts of the belly.
The judgment of the medication of wounds, however, is the judgment of the other wounds.
Which is, because when you seek the recent wound with its own blood before it changes due to air: and you reduce the intestine, and its own, and make it suitable for itself: then place it on powder of flesh.
But if the air has already changed the wound: then place on it some ointments which are present with you until they make pus: and fall off the threads, and strengthen them again, and the mira. Then take care of that wound as you would with the treatment of other wounds, until it heals.
But if you do not have the necessary medicines at hand, then immediately place on it an old piece of cloth that has been used before, and change it twice a day as I taught you, until it heals.
For you do not need other treatment in many situations when the wounds are simple.
But if you fear that the wound will communicate to the main members in a fracture, then it is necessary to immerse a soft cloth in warm oil of tempered heat, or in rose oil: and place it in the circumference of the places that are between the groins, and under the armpits.
But if he feels pain, or pricking, or putrefaction in his intestines (for this often happens), then enema him with a strengthening wine, black, warm: especially if the putrefaction has already reached the intestine, and has become a penetrating one up to its concavity.
And know that what is from the large intestine is easier to heal: and that what is from the subtle ones is more difficult to heal.
But the intestine that is called the Jejunum does not receive healing from the wound that happens in it at all: and this is because of its multitude, which is from veins, and their size, and because of the subtlety of its body, and its proximity to the nature of nerves.
But if that which proceeds from the wound is pus, and you seek it out recently: reduce it according to your reduction, by which you reduce the intestines equally.
But if it has passed a time, and it has already become green, or black: then it is necessary to tie it with a thread above the place that has become discolored from it, so that blood does not flow. For in the zirbo are the veins and artery.
Then cut what is beyond that ligament, and place the two ends of the thread hanging from the lower part of the wound outside it: so that the pull on you will be relieved, and the extraction of it in case of a zirbo fracture, and the discharge of pus from the wound.
Reminder of the wound that occurred in the intestine.
When the fracture occurs in the intestine and is small: then it is possible for some people to be restored: because I saw a man who was wounded in his abdomen with the impact of a lance, and it was a wound from the right stomach, and it was an old wound: and a fistula formed, and there was diarrhea and flatulence.
Therefore I placed the treatment, until I was not confident in his healing: nor did I stop sophisticating him, until he was healed and the place was consolidated.
After I saw the place already consolidated, I feared for the weak, that a bad thing would happen to him in his abdomen: and it did not happen to him from that bad thing. And he remained in better conditions, eating and drinking, and having sex, and entering the bath, and exercised in his meals.
And now some experimenters have said, that when the wound in the intestine occurs and is small: then it is necessary to bind it according to this method. And it is, that you take ants of large heads. Then gather two wound lips, and place one ant from those that have an open mouth on top of the two wound lips. When he places it on that, and clenches his mouth, cut off his head, for it sticks and does not come off.
Then place another ant near the first one, and do not stop doing that with the ant after the second one according to the amount of the wound for the whole.
Then bring him back, and heal his wound. For those heads remain attached in the intestines until the intestine is eaten, and healed, and no harm completely occurs to the sick person.
And now it is possible to tie the intestine even with a thin thread: which is removed from the animal's intestine, attached with it when it is inserted into the needle.
And there is, that you take the end of this thread from the intestine, and it is burned much. Then tie the thin thread of the line unrolled at its end. Then insert that thread into the needle, and heal it with the intestine. Then bring him back to the rupture.
And this method of suture with ants and intestine is not but according to the way of trust and hope.
You know that a wound which is large, wide, especially if it is in one of the thin intestines: then there is no cure but suturing, and there is no healing at all.
¶ Of the care of Zucchini, and Fistulas.
You know that every wound, or an apostema when it becomes old and aged, and becomes an ulcer, and does not consolidate, and emits pus always, and is not cut off: then it is universally called in whatever member it is Fistula, and we call it Zucchini.
A fistula indeed is truly a strained, hard, white swelling; it has no pain, and no concavity of a bird's feather; and because of this some call it a "pennam," that is, a feather.
And in certain hours it emits pus, which is moist. Perhaps the moisture is torn apart in certain hours. Sometimes this moisture is much and little, and it is coarse and fine.
I have already mentioned in the division, when I said wounds, that every ulcer which does not heal, and no flesh is born in it, is not that except for one of nine causes.
One of which is that because of the lack of blood in the body; or because of its evil nature; or because there is hard flesh between him and his lips, preventing the birth of flesh; or because it is full of dirt and filth; or because the ulcer itself is putrid, and the matter that is put into it is of bad quality; or because the medicine is inconvenient in its cure; or because corruption is falling in the region, which is a kind of pestilence, or by the nature of the region, as happens in Caesaraugusta, where digestion of sufferings becomes difficult, and healing of the abscess is delayed by nature; or because there is one bone, or a number of bones.
And I have already shown all these causes and signs of them, and their cures with medicines in the division; and it is necessary for me to make you know the cure of Fistula and Zukon, which is made by the way of operation with the hand.
Know therefore that a fistula occurs in all parts of the body. For from these are the fistulas that reach to great veins and arteries, or nerves, or sciatica: or to the intestines, or to the bladder, or to some part of the ribs: or to some part of the spine, or to the joints composed together, such as hands and feet: and from these are those that approach to the proximity of the main member, and similar ones.
Therefore, from these fistulas, according to this method, is difficult healing due to illnesses, and does not receive cure, and occupation with it is labor and ignorance.
But if it is from some fistula whose depth does not reach these places that I mentioned: and you hope and trust in its cure, and wish to approach to knowledge of it, then receive a probe from air, or iron, if the fistula tends towards straightness, and seek it with itself.
But if there is twisting in the fistula, then investigate it with a thin lead probe. Because lead, with its own gentleness, is relieved and cured around twisting.
But if the fistula has many openings, it is not possible for you to signify over it with a probe. Therefore, cleanse from these openings one opening from its own openings.
For the moisture by which you cleanse itself goes towards other openings, and runs out from them.
Then carefully investigate according to what manner it is possible for you: so that you know what is the bone, or nerve, and whether the fistula's concavity is long or near: or whether it is one fistula which has many openings, and stands on the whole of it, with utmost strength of yours: with interrogation of your question, by which you interrogate the weak one, and invention of pain at compression with your hand on the place, and similar signs and causes of abscess.
When you stand at that true station, then go to the cure according to your confidence: and it is, that you consider then, if it is a fistula near-appearing, or in a safe place far from the joint, or from the nerve, or artery, or vein, or one of the places I told you: then seal the fistula according to what was previously said by me, and remove what is in it from filtration, and corrupt flesh, which is born in its opening from the flesh, or scar tissue, and similar things: and cure that, until it is healed.
But if the fistula is of great depth, and is according to straightness: then it is necessary for you to seal it in the depth as much as is possible for you. Then cleanse it from all its corrupt flesh.
Then administer untouched linen in sharp medicines: and insert it up to the concavity of the fistula which you comprehended with iron: do with it several times, until the sharp medicine eats away everything that remains in the concavity of the fistula from corruption.
Then restore it with ointments which generate healthy flesh, until it is healed.
But if it does not heal by that, then cauterize it according to what we have said.
But if the cause of the fistula is a bone, and it is certified to you that it is so: then inquire into that, and seal it according to what I have told you: if something does not prevent you from the vein, or nerve, or principal member, as we said.
But if a bone is revealed to you, and there is something of corruption and discoloration in it: then scrape it, until the corruption of it is all removed. Then take care of that wound with the same thing that caused it, until it heals.
If it does not heal and emits pus as it did before, then you know that you have not reached the complete elimination of corruption.
Then clean it again with a second layer, and carefully make a thorough examination of it, and its cleansing with your utmost strength.
Then restore it. If it heals, then it is good; but if not, then you know that the corruption is deep within the body, which you have not reached. Therefore, it is not your ability to cure it, unless you let go of nature.
If the corrupted part is small and it is possible for you, then pull it out with fine forceps that are suitable for it.
But if there are many bones, then carefully make the extraction of all of them, and do not leave anything with your strength.
But if something gives you opposition from the moistures, and there is no fear or error in the incision of them, then cut those moistures and flesh, if they are there, and free the bones.
But if you do not have the preparation to remove the bones at your time, then place on the wound that it may putrefy itself: and let go of it, until what is in the vicinity of those bones from flesh and moistures putrefies.
And guard the wound so that it may not consolidate. And be bound the incision that you cut in your operation. But if you fear, then place on it, a piece of cloth soaked in finely ground sulfur with oil: or a piece of cloth soaked in Egyptian ointment, or some green herb of unguents.
When those moistures putrefy, and the bones are separated from them, the removal of them is relieved, and their attraction.
If however there is one great bone, such as the thigh bone, or the hip bone, and similar to them, and what is corrupted from it is a large part: then shave it with the last reason, until that blackness and corruption is removed. Then restore the wound.
But if what is in it corrupted is a large part, and corruption has already followed the marrow of the bone, then it is necessary to saw it, and cut it all the way to where corruption reached: then care for it, until it consolidates.
And I tell you zuken, which happened to a man in his thigh: so that you may place that example and help on your operation.
There was a young man about thirty years old, to whom pain came in his thigh, from a cause that moved over him within the body, that is, from inside, until the matter reached the leg, and there was a large abscess: and he did not have an external cause.
Therefore he was extended with him for a time with the error of doctors, until the abscess was opened, and many matters came together with him. And the cure of him was postponed until the leg was fistulated, and there were made in it many openings: all of which emitted pus and body moistures.
Therefore he was cared for by many doctors for about two years, and there was not in him a wise one in the art of hands, until I was called, and I saw his leg, and the matters that were running out from those openings with great speed: even all his man's body had become shriveled, and his color was yellow.
If you insert a probe into one of the body's openings, and it reaches the bone.
Then I examined all the openings: and I found that they all reach each other from all parts of the leg.
I therefore cut through one of those openings, and I found that the bone itself was rotten: which was already decayed, discolored, and rotten, and perforated, until it reached the marrow.
I therefore cut off what was found by me, and prepared it from the rotten bone.
And I appointed that there was not in the bone except that corruption which I cut and prepared. And I had already removed it.
Then I placed the healing of the wound with consolidating medicines for a long time. And it was not consolidated.
Then I probed and cut above the first detection, and I found continuous corruption with the bone: and I prepared what appeared to me even from that corruption.
Then I attempted its healing. And it was not healed.
I therefore cut through it again, and I did not stop cutting the bone individually, and trying to heal it: and it was not healed until I cut through the bone almost a span, and extracted it with its marrow.
Then I healed it with medicines, and it was quickly consolidated and healed: and there was no need for this repetition in the operation of it, and its cutting, except because of the weakness of the infirm person, and the scarcity of his tolerance, and my fear of him regarding death: because he was dying from excessive evacuation diseases every hour.
The patient was healed by a complete cure: and flesh was born in the place of the bone, and it was good for the arrangement in his body, and his strength returned to him: and he returned to his proper conditions: and he did not do him any harm at all in walking.
But if the bone is already broken in the place of the body: then it is necessary to bind it thus: and it is as follows: take a bandage, and tie it at the end of the protruding bone: and order someone to pull it upwards: and put another bandage made of thicker wool first. Then tie it over the flesh, which is under the bone: and extend its end, so that you can pull the flesh downwards: and cover the flesh on the place that you want to saw, so that it does not cut the flesh.
Place a piece of wood, or a board under the lower bone, because when you do this, it does not prevent the flesh from becoming rotten.
And it is necessary that the cut be on the place of the corruption for a little while, so that there is no corruption in the hollow of the bone: and it does not appear in its appearance to the sense, and forces it to its own purpose another way.
But if the bone is corrupted, and it is not protruding, but rather it continues with its part: and the corruption is in the middle of it, or in its own part: then cover the flesh from all parts completely. Then place the wood underneath.
Then saw it from the first side, where the corruption is, until the cut continues from the other side: and let the cut be according to the length from the corruption for a little while, as we said.
But if the corruption is in the joint, cut the corrupted joint, and saw the bone from the other side where it continues.
If indeed there is corruption in the continuity of two joints, then there is no skill in it except for amputation.
If however the corruption is in the pectine of the hand or the pectine of the foot, then the matter is quite difficult indeed. However, you must indeed investigate how the corruption appears to you. And amputate it, and clean it according to any possible arrangement that is possible for you, and with any ingenuity, correct it for you, when it does not give you opposition of the vein or nerve.
And know that there are many teeth and saws for cutting these bones according to the position of the bones, and their preparation, and their thickness, and subtlety of them, and magnitude, and parity of them, and hardness of them, and rarity of them. Therefore, you must prepare every kind of instrument suitable for that operation.
And know that these operations signify to you above the kind of instrument that you lack, when with you is the study of a long time. And knowledge of this art is a testimony of the ways of ailments, for then you will already find through yourself that which is suitable to him from the instruments for every infirmity.
And I am strengthening you at the last number of this chapter's instruments, which you will place examples upon which you will cut, and proof by which you experiment on others.

It is not suitable for anything other than to rub against the heads of joined wounds when they are decaying, or for a large mouth, and it is very large.
