On Incising the Extremities, and Sawing Bones.
The extremities putrefy, either from an external cause or an internal one.
When therefore you have cured that corruption with medical treatment, and the cure does not take effect: and you see the corruption spreading to a member, which nothing rebounds against: then it is necessary for you to incise that member as far as the corruption follows, so that the weak one may pass through it from death, or from the malice which is greater than the defect of the member.
And the sign that this happens is that the limb becomes discolored, until it is thought to have been burned by fire or has decayed after a gangrenous condition: until that putrefaction spreads to the following limb, and spreads throughout the whole body.
Therefore, as soon as the incision is made, and if the cause of corruption is from the impact of certain poisonous creatures: such as sea scorpions, and vipers, and rattle snakes, and similar ones.
If therefore the corruption or impact is at the end of the finger, then cut the finger, and do not leave space for the corruption, so that it does not spread to the rest of the hand.
And similarly if it happens in the hand, then cut it from the root of the forearm, and do not leave space for the corruption, until it reaches the elbow.
And if it invades it, then cut the arm at the elbow in its joint.
But if the corruption passes through and you see it around the elbow: then there is death of the weak one. And to administer besides that from the cure, is a quantity of power.
And similarly do with the foot, when the corruption invades in the finger, then cut it at one joint: and if it reaches the patella of the foot, then cut the foot entirely. But if it climbs up to the knee, then cut the leg at the joint of the knee.
But if the corruption has already reached above the knee, then there is no cure in it, except release, and leaving the weak one to death.
And the way of cutting the limb, or of clamping it is, to tie the ligament in the lower part, which you wish to cut: and tie the ligament above the place. The assistant should extend one of the ligaments downwards and the other superior ligament upwards. And you should separate the flesh that is between the two ligaments, with a narrow spatula, until the flesh is completely exposed. Then it is cut or squeezed.
And it is necessary to place bandages on all parts of the cloth, and not touch the healthy part with the saw: and an added injury occurs to the sick person, and a hot abscess.
But if blood flows internally while operating, then cauterize the place quickly: or place on top of it some powders that absorb blood. Then return to your medical treatment until it is completed.
Then bind the wounded limb with the appropriate ligament to it, and care for it, until it heals.
And I tell you what happened to a man in his foot, the same thing that I am telling you.
That is, because blackness occurred in his foot, with burning that resembles the burning of fire: and that corruption first occurred in his finger, until it began to affect the whole foot.
Therefore the man removed himself from himself, after he saw the corruption spreading in his member with its intensity, which he found from the pain and burning of it: and it happened to him at the junction, and he was healed.
And after a long time had passed, the same corruption happened to him in his finger of his hand index.
Therefore he came to me, and I tried to recover that excess with him which I put on his hand from medicines after the cleansing of his body: and the excess was not reflected back, and it began to spread to another finger: until the corruption began in the hand.
He therefore called me to cut off his hand: and I was unwilling to do it, hoping for a reflection on the excess of that fluctuation: and I also feared even for him at the time of the cutting off of his hand. Because the power of man was over the fall.
After he therefore gave up hope in me, he returned to his land: and he came to me from him, because he hurried, and he cut off his hand entirely: and he was healed.
And I did not bring this story, unless it be a help on that which falls from this kind of sickness: and that there be a signification by which it is signified, and according to which it is done.
On the care of sinews, and the quality of cataplasm with medicines.
When an abscess occurs in certain fleshy members, and the time of the abscess is prolonged until it makes a collection of pus: then it bursts or is pierced, and what is in it from the pus goes out, and the place remains empty as if it were a vessel: and the skin that is on top of it like a fabric that has already become thin: and it does not reach to its final corruption, nor does it touch the mouth, nor the nerve, nor the ligament: it deserves to be called a sinus: and it is not called a fistula: but if the time of its duration is prolonged until it touches any of these members with corruption, then it is called a fistula, or zuken.
And its care is, that I cut off that skin entirely as it rolls back: and especially when it has become thin, and made like a fabric: and you trust that it will not stick to the place, because of its corruption.
But if you hope that the skin will stick to the place, and that final corruption will not follow from it: and if there is thickness in the skin from flesh, then care for it with cataplasm: and it is, that you consider towards the sinus.
Then, if it is large and the pus that emits from it has a foul odor, cleanse it with the Egyptian medicine, which is acetum, oil, and zinziber, equal parts mixed together in a vessel. Heat them over fire until the medicine turns red and thickens like honey.
Then take what you need from it and dissolve it with water and honey, and cleanse the sinus with it. Close the opening and leave the medicine in it for two hours.
Then remove it with expression and do this for several days until the sinus is cleaned and the odor is removed.
And sometimes cleanse it with water and ash when you do not have this medicine present: take charcoal from willow or holm oak trees and throw water on it. Then wash it and cleanse it with it until you trust that the sinus is now cleansed.
If the patient does not tolerate the Egyptian medicine or water and charcoal, then cleanse it with water and honey to which some crushed zinziber has already been added. Or cleanse it with mixed honey and wine because of the property of honey that it cleansses and washes: and wine makes the sinus stick, especially when there is an excess of astringency and dryness in the wine.
When you do this several times and trust that the corruption is now removed, then cleanse it with what causes flesh to grow in it.
And it is, that you take from the plaster dyafinicon and dissolve it with rose oil and astringent wine: or cleanse it with certain other medicines and ointments whose properties I have written about in my treatise on ointments.
If the orifice of the sinus is narrow and does not accommodate a catheter, then slightly widen it with a needle: or place a piece of lint soaked in Egyptian oil or basilikum ointment inside it until it is widened.
Similarly, if the orifice is also large, then gather its lips with a suture and allow the amount that the catheter enters without adding anything.
Similarly, if the orifice from which the pus flows is elevated, then dry it in a lower position that is inside it, so that the pus flows out downwards: for when pus is confined in the depths of the sinus, it prevents flesh from growing in it.
If it is not possible for you to dry the sinus around its lower part as you wish, then try to prepare the member by the preparation by which the pus flows out of it with ease according to what is prepared for you. Try to ensure that nothing at all from the pus remains in it: and take consolidating medicines that are placed on the sign, suitable for what you wish. And extend them on linen cloth. Let the cloth be of such a quantity that it covers the entire sinus. Then cut with forceps directly into the orifice of the sinus, more than the orifice of the sinus slightly. Then extend from the mild ointments on another cloth, according to the quantity of the opening: and place it on it with a long position away from the orifice of the sinus, so that the exit of the pus from it is relieved: and do not remove a large cloth unless after several days.
But the one that is on the orifice of the sinus is the one that you remove every hour, so that what accumulates in it from the pus exits: and so that you know whether the thing that flows out of it is much, or little: or digested, or undigested.
And again consider this place of the sinus, whether the master feels pain there, or if there is no pain in it, and whether there is an abscess in it, or if there is no abscess in it.
Therefore, when your medication is applied in this way, and you see the material that issues from the opening of the sinus, then you know that the sinus has already adhered or is approaching adhesion: then therefore dissolve it in the morning, or on the third day: and when you heal the wound, then replace the cloth with a new one, and renew the ointment.
But if a subtle virus issues from the sinus after a long time, then do not despair of its adhesion, for its healing is approaching, because there are men who delay the generation of flesh in their wounds, and there are those who act contrary to that.
But if a undigested pus issues from the sinus after many days, then you know that the sinus does not adhere.
Therefore, if the adhesion of the sinus is delayed and its matter is prolonged: then add to the drying of the medicines, but let the doctors make them so that they are medicines in their wet substance and in their dry virtue, as is the ointment dyafinicon when superfluity of addition is added to it from zegi.
And from the last thing that is cured, it is, that you take the ointment dyafinicon and dissolve it with rose oil, and moisten it with equal old wine in its substance.
Then finish it with that, and use it.
And now he performs a similar action when there is no ointment dyafinicon present for you, honey, when you dissolve it, until it thickens, and use it. Take myrrh, aloe, and frankincense, pound them all together, and powder it over melted honey while it is still on the fire. Then apply the linen cloth above it, and tie it over the wound: and with the honey that you have boiled, while it is still hot, fill it until it is full: and powder the specified species on top of it, and place it on the cloth, and tie it.
And sometimes aristolochia longa, and the roots of the blue lily, and the lily itself, and the flour of the herb, and centaury are administered in it. Use them either simple or combined, grind them, and grind the mortar itself: and powder it on the honey that I have boiled, and use it.
If the wound persists and is not healed by this treatment, then you will know that there is corruption in its depths: or it has already made an impression on the bones, or on the other hard members, or ligaments: then cure it with the treatment of fistulas, as it was previously prescribed.
¶ On the care of onychia and the worn nail, and the incision of the finger added, and the section.
Onychia is an abscess that arises under the nail of the thumb of the hand, or of the foot: and perhaps it arises in the other fingers as well.
When therefore the matter persists and is neglected in its treatment, and it becomes an abscess with hot abscess: or it rots and emits pus, until it corrodes the root of the nail: and perhaps it rots it entirely, and perhaps the corruption reaches the bone, until there is a foul odor to it: and it becomes the end of the finger broad, and its color is dark.
When therefore you are treating it yourself, since as we said in the division, and you do not apply your own cure: then it is necessary that you cut with a knife all the remaining superfluity that remains from the nail. Then cauterize the wound after that. For a cauterizing iron is very helpful.
If indeed the mouth is healthy, and the nail is also healthy, and the empty spaces of the nail are already compressing the flesh to the interior, and they begin to prick it, and they wound it: then it is necessary that you place a fine radium under the angle of the nail which is pricking the flesh, and push it upwards: and cut the flesh with ease, and put on top of what remains of the flesh from medicines burning, corrosive, until all of it is removed. Then treat it with ointments until it is healed.
But if the corruption has already pressed into the mouth, then it is necessary that you cut that mouth, and remove it: for it will never be healed as long as the corrupted mouth remains in it.
But if you see the corrosion and corruption proceeding into the finger, then cut it at one node, according to what was previously mentioned. Then treat it, until it is healed.
But if an accident occurs to the nail, such as a break or blow: and pain occurs in it, then it is necessary that you let blood from the sick person first. Then cut the nail with a sharp spatula transversely from above to the sight.
And guard, that the cut does not reach the flesh which is under the nail, for you will cause an accident to occur through it above the sick person's severe pain, and it will be a cause of new birth of flesh in that place.
Then care for the place with that which soothes pain.
However, the digitus added to some people's hands, which is born in some people's hands, perhaps it is entirely fleshy: and perhaps there are bones in them, and perhaps there is a nail in it: and some of them are born at the root of the joint, or its birth is in some knots of the finger. Therefore, that which is born in some knots of the finger, does not move: and that which is born at the joint of the finger, perhaps moves.
Therefore, for him who is fleshy from among them, his cutting is easy. That is, so that you cut it at its root with a broad spatula.
But for him whose birth is at the root of the joint, his cure is difficult. Therefore, refrain from cutting it.
However, for him who is born in the finger at the last knot, then you should cut into the first flesh of his round cut up to the bone. Then saw the bone with one of those saws that are suitable for that. Then care for it, until it is healed.
However, the consolidation that happens to fingers together often happens from the birth of man, that is, he is born with it, or from the consolidation of the wound, or from the burning of fire, and similar things.
Therefore, you should separate that consolidation, until the fingers return to their natural form. Then place between them a lint, or cloths soaked in rose oil: so that they do not consolidate quickly, and separate between them: or place between them a thin sheet of lead, until the place consolidates as it should.
Similarly, if a consolidation occurs between certain fingers and the palm, then dry that consolidation according to how it is prepared and fits the figure of the member.
On Incising a Wound.
Veins are often twisted, thick, and full of melancholic superfluities that occur in many parts of the body: and their greatest event is found in the legs, especially in the legs of those who walk, work, and carry.
Therefore it is necessary for caretakers to frequently shake the body with strong shaking from black choler.
Then, the vein of the patient is bleeding in the basilica.
The cure of these with iron, however, is according to two modes. One of them is that they are dried and the black blood is drawn out. The other mode is that the vein is raised and all the blood is drawn out.
The section of it, however, is according to this method. First, warm water is applied to the leg, until the thick, dirty blood is dissolved. Then, the weak leg is tied from its upper part of the hip to its lower part with a ligature, with a rope. Then, the vein is cut in one place, or two, or three places, with a wide incision.
Then, raise it, that is, draw the blood from the lower part of the leg, upwards, and from the upper part, it is necessary for the phlebotomist to first. Then, cut the nail with a knife until it goes down to the blood: until the amount of blood that you see is enough and what the strength of the sick person can tolerate.
Afterwards, tie her up: and order her to abstain from foods that generate black bile: and repeat evacuation and phlebotomy when the veins are full, and it harms the sick person.
However, his evacuation is done in this way. Shave the leg of the sick person if there are many hairs on it. Then introduce him into the bath: or broil him in the leg of his thigh with hot water until it reddens, and the veins are full: or exercise strong exercise, if there is no bath present, until the limb warms up.
Then dry the skin directly over the vein section along its length: or at the last of his knee, or in the lower part of his heel.
Then open the skin with hooks, and scrape the vein from all sides, until it appears to the sense: and at its appearance, that you see it reddening towards the descending blackness. When therefore it goes out of the skin, you see it white like a string.
Then introduce it under it Radium, until when it is evacuated and goes out of the skin: suspend it with a blind hook, gently.
Then dry another section near that section three fingers. Then scrape the skin from the upper part of the vein, until it appears. Then evacuate it with Radii as you did, and suspend it with another hook, as you did first.
Then dry another section, or several sections, if you need that one. Then evacuate, and cut the last section at the heel.
Then remove it to the section that is above it.
And make him do this, until you extract it from the higher or more elevated section than all others, until when it comes out completely: then cut it.
But if it does not obey you in being extracted and raised: then insert a sharp needle with strong thread doubled, and tie it, and extract it: or insert under it Radium: and turn your hand to all parts, until it comes out. And beware, do not cut it. For if it is cut, it becomes difficult for you to raise it greatly, and enters into the weakest part of it, causing harm.
Then when you have extracted it all: then place it on the wound with immersed thread in wine and rose oil, or oil: and care for it until it is healed.
But if the wound is contracted, having a twisted shape to which there is no covering to all parts, and it is not as we said according to straightness: then it is necessary that you suture over it to all part of its twisted shape, and locations of its covering.
Then suspend it with sutures, until you raise it all: and beware at your cutting on it that you do not cut the vein, or wound: for it will be difficult for you to raise it, or extract it. Therefore preserve your wisdom.
The Form of Incision for the Healing of a Wound.
The Form of Suturing a Blind Wound.
It does not have straightness like other sutures, nor is it sharp at its extremities, so as not to wound the vein: and it is thick in its twisted shape, mild: because if it were subtle, it would cut the vein with its subtlety: indeed it should have excessive thickness, as we said.
On the Extraction of the Leg Vein.
This vein is generated in the legs in warm lands, such as those of the Almohads and the Arabs, and in dry, warm, thin lands, that is, where there grows neither herb nor tree.
And perhaps it is generated in other parts of the body besides the legs.
And its generation indeed is from the putrefaction that occurs beneath the skin, just as snakes and worms of ascarides occur within the bodies, and worms generated between the skin and flesh.
And the sign of the beginning of this vein is that which occurs in the leg, a severe inflammation. Then the location is incised. Then the vein begins to exit from that location of incision, as if it were the root of a plant or an animal.
When therefore it appears from that end of it, then you must wrap around it a fragment of lead, whose weight is from a drachma keil, up to two drachmas and the knot: and let the lead suspended from the leg.
Whenever therefore something exits from it to the outsides, wrap that in lead, and knot it. If it is prolonged much, then incise its part, and wrap the remainder. And do not incise it root and branch before it has all exited. Because if you incise it, it contracts, and enters into the flesh: and causes an abscess, and putrefaction in that location, and an evil wound.
Therefore it is necessary that it be gently handled, and extracted gradually, until it exits from its last part, and nothing remains of it in the body: and from this vein indeed some men exit with that which is in its length five palms and ten. And now he has reached me, because a man has departed from twenty palms.
But if it happens to you at the time of your medical treatment: then introduce the radium through its hole, and perforate it with a long one, with the body, until everything that is in it is evacuated from the matter: and administer putrefaction of the site with medicines for several days. Then care for him with the care of the abscess.
And this vein sometimes has many branches, especially when it appears at the joint of the foot, or in the foot itself: and many openings occur to him, and he goes out from every opening.
Then care for it, as we said in the division, and with that which was previously mentioned.
¶ About cutting the worms generated under the skin, and it is called 'Bouina Disease'.
This disease is called 'Bouina Disease' in a certain land among us: because often it happens to worms, and it is a small worm that is born between the skin and flesh.
And it goes through the whole body, ascending and descending: and it shows itself to the sense during its walk from member to member, until it breaks wherever it breaks in the skin, and goes out.
And its generation is from the putrefaction of certain humors. As worms and snakes, that is, roundworms and ascarides, happen in the belly.
And it is feared from its malice. Because when it goes through the body, and is raised to the head, and reaches the place: then perhaps it opens in it, and goes out, and destroys the eye: and this happens often.
When therefore you wish to cure him and extract him, then it is not done except at his walking and the appearance of himself to his sense.
Therefore, you must bind what is above him and what is below him with a strong bandage in constriction. Then cut above him, and extract him.
If it is deeply embedded in the flesh and you cannot find it, then place a hot iron on the spot until it dies.
And the greater danger is its corruption, by which it corrupts the eye, as we have said.
But if you see that it has already reached the head near the eye, then bind under it with a good eyebrow bandage. Then cut above him, and extract him.
And it is necessary that the sick person cleanse his body with a medicine dissolving foul humors badly.
And he should beware of foods that generate putrefaction in him.
¶ On cutting above a soreness of Nakir.
This soreness is called Nakir in our land: and it is a pain that occurs in certain members, then it changes from member to member.
And indeed I have already seen it myself, as I tell you. I was called to an ill woman in certain villages. And she exposed her arm, and I saw a small inflation in the vein of the forearm.
And after I remained for an hour, I saw one inflation moving with the fire, like a snake, ascending to her shoulder more quickly than is possible: so that it was like live silver when running from place to place.
The pain therefore departed from that place, and it was fixed on her shoulder.
Then I sat for one hour, and it rushed into the remaining body, until it reached another arm.
Then he told me that it was turning around in his whole body, as I had seen.
I was therefore amazed at the speed of its movement from limb to limb. And indeed, I had not seen this illness with my own eyes in this way before. Nevertheless, I had seen many who found pain moving from limb to limb, and I had not seen it with my own eyes as I had seen it in that woman.
And I do not think that it is otherwise than because she was from those who are from the dry uterus of the detected veins, hence it appears to the senses that this movement is caused by wind.
And it is necessary that they do not appear according to this reason in those who are delicate and have moist bodies, of hidden veins.
When therefore you wish to cure him, and the patient feels that pain: then if it is apparent to your eye, as we said, then bind quickly above it, and under it: and dry above it, until that windiness is confined: and cauterize the place.
But if you do not see it with your own eyes: then cure him with the shaking of his body, and with that which expels windiness, and charm them with fetid pills, and pills of juniper, and similar things.
CONCERNING THE EXTRACTION OF ARROWS.
ARROWS DIFFER ACCORDING TO THEIR KIND AND ACCORDING TO THE PLACES IN WHICH THEY FALL FROM THE BODY.
BUT THIS DIVERSITY IS GREAT, BECAUSE THERE ARE SOME WHICH HAVE LARGE AND SMALL, SHARP AND BLUNT POINTS: AND HOLEY AND DEAF ONES. And among them are those which have three angles. And among them are those which have a tongue. And among them are those which have stars.
Those however which are according to the members in which they fall, are according to two modes. For indeed the members are from the principal concave members, such as the brain, and heart, and liver, and lung, and kidneys, and intestines, and bladder, and similar things. Therefore when it falls into any of these members, and signs of death appear to you, which I tell you afterward, then you should avoid the extraction of that arrow from them, for death follows him in whom it is, in many positions. And when those evil signs do not appear to you, and the arrow is not hidden in the depth of the member, then extract it, and care for the wound.
For from the signs of the brain when the arrow falls into it, and penetrates the mouth, and exits that which is on top of the brain, there are: because they happen from it strong pain, scotomia, vertigo, redness in the eyes, inflation, redness of the tongue, spasm, and confusion of the intellect, and vomiting of cholera. And perhaps it exits blood from the nostrils, or from the ears. And perhaps speech is cut off, and voice is destroyed. And it exits from the place of the wound white fluid similar to pus. And it exits from that similar to the humidity of flesh.
Therefore if those signs appear to you, then avoid the care, and extract the arrow if it does not exit.
The signs of the arrow however when it falls into the heart are: that it is near the left nipple: and feels with it as if it is fixed in a hard thing, not in a vacant one. And perhaps the motion of an arrow is similar to the motion of a blow: and black blood runs from the wound. And then follows extreme coldness, and cold sweat, and syncope. Therefore know that death is certainly approaching.
And the sign of an arrow when it wounds the lung is the frothy discharge of blood from the wound: and the boils that follow around the neck become inflamed, and the color of the sick person changes. And he will breathe out a great, deep breath: and he will seek the cooling of cold air.
If the arrow falls into the breast, which is in the chest: then it is near the small ribs: and a great panting with intense pain, with a sigh: and all the limbs of the shoulders are moved.
And if the arrow falls into the stomach, then perhaps something undigested from food comes out of the wound.
And if the arrow falls into the belly, and is fixed in it: something of feces comes out of the wound, or a mass, or an intestine that is already torn. There is therefore no hope for his cure, nor for the extraction of the arrow.
If the arrow falls into the bladder, and urine comes out of it: and something proceeds from it to the outside, and the pain is stronger on the sick person: then you will know that it is mortal.
But the other limbs, such as the face, and the neck, and the throat, and the shoulder blade, and the ribs, and the wings, and the hip, and the leg, and the like are saved from these members according to many arrangements: when the arrow does not find an artery, or a nerve: and it is not a poisonous arrow.
And I tell you what I have seen of these arrows, as you indicate in your treatment.
Because an arrow fell into the lacrimal duct of a man's eye, at the root of his nose. Therefore, I extracted it from the other side, under the ear's fat: and he was healed, and no harm came to his eye.
And I extracted an arrow from a Jew, which had fallen into the fat of his eye under the lower eyelid: and the arrow was already hidden, and I could only get out of it except its small tip, with which it adheres to its reed: and it was a large arrow among the arrows of the Turks, with a weak iron, in which there are no ears.
The Jew was therefore healed, and no harm came to his eye.
And I extracted an arrow from the throat of a Christian.
And it was an Arabic arrow, and it is that which has ears. Therefore, I cut it above it between two tongues: and it was already submerged in his throat. I was careful with it as I extracted it: and the Christian was healed.
And I extracted an arrow from a man which had fallen into his belly: and we thought he would die from it.
After therefore thirty days had passed over him, and nothing changed on him from his dispositions, I cut above the arrow: and I peeled it off, and extracted it: and he was healed, and no harm came to him.
And I saw a man on whom an arrow had fallen on his back, and the wound was consolidated over it. After therefore it was after seven years, the arrow came out at the root of his thigh.
I saw a woman who had an arrow lodged in her womb and the wound was healed over it, and the arrow remained inside her: and there was no change in her posture or condition, and she did not find any harm from any of her natural functions.
I also saw a man who had an arrow lodged in his face: and the wound was healed over it, and he did not find much pain from it: and there were many similar cases.
I also extracted the arrow from a man of high rank, who had it lodged in the middle of his nose, and it had already begun to lean towards the right side a little: and the arrow was hidden completely.
I was therefore called to treat him after the accident with the arrow for three days. I found the wound of the arrow to be quite tight.
I therefore examined it with a fine probe, and I did not feel it: but he himself found a pricking and pain under his right ear. I therefore hoped that this pricking was from the tip of the arrow.
I therefore applied a plaster with a property that attracts and digests, confident that the wound would become an abscess and I would be able to see the sign of the arrow so that I could cut it above: and nothing happened in that place which indicated that the arrow had followed its path.
I therefore applied the plaster to him for many days: and nothing happened which was not intended, and the wound healed in the meantime: and he remained weak from the extraction of it for several days, until he felt the arrow inside his nose on a certain day. And he told me that.
And he told me that. I therefore placed a sharp and corrosive medicine on that wound for many days until it was open: and when I examined him with a fine probe, I felt the tip of the arrow which adhered to the wood.
Then I added to the incision of the wound through that sharp medicine, until the visible end of the arrow appeared to us: and it passed by me with it a certain period of time, approximately four months.
Then, after the wound had been enlarged, and it was possible for me to insert pincers into it and move it, but it did not obey my commands: then I did not cease to sharpen and devise various ways of using the pincers on it, until I began to extract it on a certain day with well-made pincers, according to the form of their ends at the end of the chapter, until I extracted it. Then I restored the wound.
And indeed, the doctors judge that the cartilage of the nose is not restored. I therefore restored it, and the wound was healed, and the sick person was cured with complete health: nor did anything at all harm him.
And I tell you the quality of extracting some arrows: so that you may place that rule and signification on that which I have not said.
Because the parts of this art and their distinctions are not comprehended with narration: nor does that book comprehend it, and a wise craftsman compares with little on much: and with what is present, he compares to what is absent: and he finds a new operation and a new instrument among the descents of things extraneous to this art when they happen.
I say therefore, that arrows do not exit from the members in which they are fixed, except according to two ways. Either by attraction from the place from which it entered. Or by the opposite part.
And that which exits from where it entered is either an arrow proceeding in a fleshy place: and it is attracted and exits.
If it does not comply with the outcome from the hour in which it falls: then it is necessary to let it go for several days, until the flesh that is around it rots: and its attraction is eased, and its exit.
Similarly, if it sticks to the bone, and does not comply with you for exit, then let it go also for several days: and repeat it with attraction and motion every day, until it exits.
If it does not comply with you for exit after days, then it is necessary to bore through the circumference of the arrow in the same bone from all parts with a thin drill, until the arrows are enlarged. Then attract it, and extract it.
But if the arrow is already hidden in the place of the body, and it is hidden and concealed from sense: then seek it with touch. But if you feel it, then attract it with some instruments that are suitable for its attraction.
If you cannot place it above the wound due to its constriction and the length of the arrow in a deep location where there is no bone, nerve, or vein: then pierce it on top of the wound until it expands, making it possible to extract the arrow.
If there are ears to which it can be tied, then free the attached flesh from all parts, with every skill you have, and skills, if it cannot be placed above the flesh in the fracture of the ears and their twisting, until it is removed.
And when you administer the extraction of the arrow in any location, then use the twisting of your hand with forceps to all parts, until you make it escape: and with subtlest subtleties, so that the arrow is not broken, and it becomes difficult for you to attract it and extract it.
If you cannot place it above the wound in one hour, then let it go for several days until the rotten parts around it are putrid. Then repeat it: for the tunica will be healed if indeed it causes you opposition in the flow of blood, then administer what we said from the cure in its chapter: and guard your skill from incision of vein, or nerve, or string.
And administer skill in every way that is possible for you to escape the arrow: and let it be with facility, and tranquility, or slowness, and firmness, as I have told you.
And it is necessary that when you pull the arrow, it should be weak according to its shape, according to which it was at the accident of the arrow in itself. For it is more beneficial. But if it is not possible for you, then administer what is possible from the figures.
The arrow that exits from the opposite side of the other part, or has already begun to protrude from it towards the outside: or it causes a swelling at the tip of the arrow by sensation from the upper part of the skin near it, and you see it protruding: therefore cut above it, and make the incision according to the amount that the forceps can take in it.
Then pull it out: for it will become easy to exit.
If indeed it is retained in the bone, then twist your hand according to its roundness, until the arrow is pressed into the bone and expands itself: then pull it out.
And if not: leave it for several days: then repeat it, until it exits.
If the wood of the arrow is in it, then push it with it.
But if the wood has fallen off, and you want to apply a blow: then insert a concave instrument into it, so that its concavity enters into the tail of the arrow: then push it with it.
But if the arrow is concave, then push it with an inserting instrument. For the arrow is relieved by that.
But if the arrow is poisoned, then it is necessary to hollow out all the flesh in which the poison is: if it is possible for you. Then care for it with what suits it.
But if the arrow is falling in the chest, or in the belly, or in the bladder, or in the side: and it is near what you touch with a probe, and it is possible for you to cut above it: then cut, and avoid the incision of the vein, or nerve, and remove it.
Then care for its wound, if you see it, and heal it, until it is healed.
This is the form of forceps used for removing arrows.
The tips of these forceps are similar to a bird's beak, made of iron, and when they grip the arrow, they do not let go of it.
There are many varieties of these forceps, large and small, medium-sized, according to the size of the arrow, its flexibility, and the width and constriction of the wound.
The shape of the pusher is concave.
The shape of the pusher is blind.
This is the blind tip of the pusher, shaped like a radius, to facilitate its insertion into the concave arrow and to be pushed with it.
On bloodletting from veins.
The veins that are usually bled in the body are thirty.
Of these, there are sixteen in the head: two pulsatile veins behind the ears, called the "herbs"; and two arteries that are visible on the temples; and two veins at the corners of both eyes, called the "aspirants"; and a prepared vein in the middle of the forehead; and a vein at the end of the nose. And two jugular veins that are in the neck. And two veins that are in the upper lip of the mouth. And two veins that are in the lower lip. These are called the "alche-rich" veins. And two veins that are under the tongue.
In the arms, the veins that are bled are five in each arm.
One of them is called the cephalic vein, and it is located on the sulcus of the elbow; people also call it the arm vein. And the dark one. And there is the median vein, which is composed of a branch of the basilica and a branch of the cephalic; people also call it the body vein. And there is the basilica vein, which is located on the domestic sulcus; it is also called the titilous vein. People also call it the abdominal vein. And there is the brachial cord vein, which is located above the elbow; it is the one that is bled from and the one that appears above the thumb.
And there is the salivate vein, which is located between the ring and the little finger; it has two branches.
And in the leg and foot, there are three veins. One of them is located under the thumb arch on the sulcus of the elbow. And the second one is the saphenous vein; its location is near the heel, on the domestic sulcus. And there is the nesse vein; its location is near the heel, on the sulcus of the elbow.
And in the leg, there are three other veins similar to those mentioned earlier.

Bleeding from the two veins that are after the ears is a remedy for ancient cataracts, hemiglanea, sahefati, and old head sores.

Then clean your hand with the vein and skin to the upper parts, and cut the vein with the Incisor incision. And let the length of the incision be the amount of two fingers joined together, or about that: and make it bleed out as much blood as you wish.
Then bind it with bandages, and let it go, until it is healed.

About the Cephalic vein. Phlebotomy of the cephalic vein is a remedy, because it draws blood from the head and brings it to eye ailments.
And it is proper in this vein, if you wish, to perform phlebotomy by puncturing with an olive oil phlebotome or a myrtle phlebotome: because it is safer than all veins, since it does not have an accompanying artery or nerve.
However, it is appropriate for you during phlebotomy to direct the phlebotome towards the head of the lizard and seek a less painful spot: and it does not harm it if it is not found with the first blow, but can be repeated with phlebotomy several times.
However, it may perhaps abscess in some people when it is not performed with the first blow, but it does not harm them with that abscess in some place.
On the usefulness of phlebotomy and precautions to be observed in it. The quality of phlebotomy and its accidents from which you should think of its correction.
First of all, you should know that phlebotomy is not administered except for the preservation of health and its continuity, and caution against the onset of ailments.
And so that phlebotomy may be performed in one of the three veins that are in the elbow, namely the cephalic, fusca, and basilica. And so that phlebotomy may be performed at the beginning of spring on fasting, in spring, and in summer: and in autumn and winter after eating, when the signs of repletion appear.
And it should be performed on the first day, or on the third, after three hours have passed since the previous day.
Phlebotomy, which is administered in ailments, does not have a determined hour: but when it is provoked by convenience and necessity to that, at night, or at day, and in every hour, and in every time.
And it is not necessary for children to be bled until they reach fourteen years of age. Neither should a pregnant woman be bled, unless from the fourth month until the seventh. Nor should elderly people who have already passed sixty years be bled.
When therefore someone wants to be bled for any reason whatsoever, it is necessary that he clean his intestines before the bleeding with a mild enema, if there is much feces retained in them: so that the veins at the time of the bleeding do not draw out from the intestines superfluous putrid things harmful to the principal members.
Nor should a patient with nausea, that is, satiety of vomiting, be bled, nor one who is full, nor one who avoids drunkenness, until it is removed from them. Nor a sick person with hydropsy.
And let it be guarded against bleeding again after colic pain, and vomiting, and diarrhea, and multiplication of coitus, and labor, and exercise, and vigils, and fasting, and every thing that dissolves the strength from the body or animal.
Then consider the subtlety of the humors before that, if the blood is thick with food and drinks, and medicines: if it is possible for him to have that.
Then he should enter the bath, if nothing prohibits it: or he should be exercised in some exercise, so that the blood is made subtle.
And place a bloodletting on his chest, around the third day, as we mentioned: and try to make him vomit his chest that day from all the animal misfortunes: such as distress, anger, and fear: and from all bodily misfortunes, such as labor, punishment, and excessive sweating, and similar things.
And let his bed be present with the things of which he became accustomed to use through custom among people from aromatics, and perfumes, and dancing and similar things by the amount of possibility.
Then the bloodletter should sit on a pillow, which is higher than the pillow for bleeding: afterwards he should draw his arm, and rub it with his hand twice or three times. Then he should tie a bandage with a roller, and wrap it twice.
And let the binding be temperate, because when the binding is unequal, or by excess in the binding, then it prevents the course of blood: or in softening, then also it prevents the course of blood.
Then after the binding, it is necessary to rub the bled person with his hands simultaneously, until the veins are filled and the sensation is lost.
Then the bloodletter should clean the bled person with a little oil, anciently properly.
Then he should place his finger of his left hand on the vein under the place where he wants to bleed, a little: so that the vein does not escape, and it is covered by the blow. Because from the veins is what is found as a fleeing cord at bleeding: and from them is what is full of venosity: and when you place the bled person on it, it contracts under the bleeding, and deceives the bloodletter, and does not open the vein: and if it opens it, it is tight: for that reason therefore it is necessary to strengthen the bloodletter, and to be careful in all these things.
Then remove the phlebotomist. If therefore a vein is opened from one wound, then it is good. And if not, then repeat that wound another under that place slightly, or above it with haste: if the location does not become an abscess.
But if it becomes an abscess, or the weak man swells, then let him go on the day, or two days: and do not tighten the bandage. Perhaps the abscess will attract hot. Nor should he enter the bath.
Then repeat the phlebotomy, if he loves it.
But if the opening is small, or the blood flows slightly: and you fear that not to come out of the blood quantity as you wish: then repeat the phlebotomy in the same hole according to straightness, and add in the operation slightly.
And do that with haste, before the location becomes an abscess, for the location becomes an abscess in many men at the small operation.
But if you see him already swollen, then do not repeat on it at all, for not to excuse anything to you. And put on it something from the oil of faeces: because it will relieve the course of the blood. And it is better in this place than the oil itself, and than the other oil.
And similarly administer the oil of faeces in all your phlebotomies, where the phlebotomist veins at the prohibition of the course of the blood: and they make it tyriaca alfarach, and sagzenea, when it is put on one of them over the location.
For the blood thins and dissolves, when it is thick.
But if an abscess happens in the location of phlebotomy great, for often it happens, especially to him who is not phlebotomized except that vein, or is a small opening of the vein, then hasten and put on the location sponge soaked in water and salt, warmed slightly: and tighten it at one hour: because it will dissolve.
You should perform this procedure after the blood has stopped flowing from the same vein or another one, with its own completeness.

Of Ventilation and its Quality
Ventilation is made from horns, air, and glass.
Indeed, ventilation is made in two ways. With incision and extraction of blood: and the other is ventilation without incision.
And this ventilation that is without incision is in two ways. For indeed, it is with fire. Or it is without fire.
And ventilation that is administered with incision and extraction of blood are fourteen locations of the body. Of which one is, Ventilation of the Almonds, and is the last of the head: and Alkehel, and is in the middle of the neck: and ventilation of the Alhagdahim, and are two layers of the neck from two parts at once: and ventilation of the mouth, and is under the jaw in the lower part of the mouth: and ventilation of the two spoons: and ventilation of the Alachosos on the end of the tail: and ventilation of the two foci, and are in the middle of the two arms: and ventilation of the two legs: and ventilation of the two calves.
And ventilation indeed does not draw blood from you from the small veins scattered in the flesh, and therefore its virtue does not fall out of them, as is the case with its effect from phlebotomy. Nor is it necessary that ventilation be administered with fire or without fire in any ailments that arise from overfullness until the whole body is evacuated.
But if necessity provokes ventilation from ailment or for custom, we administer it in every hour at the beginning of the month, at its end, and in the middle of it, and at whatever time it is.
Because there are men who, when the blood multiplies within them, until they need its extraction through ventilation, find a swelling and an ulcer on their head, and they heal it.
And from them is one who finds a swelling and redness on their face, on their head, and on their neck. And from them is one who finds itching on their face, and on their forehead, and darkness, and dimness in their eyes.
And from them is one who itches the place of their ventilation. And from them is one whose laughter multiplies. And from them is one who finds the taste of blood in their mouth: or their tongue swells and they vomit blood. And from them is one whose sleep multiplies. And from them is one who sees in their sleep blood and redness, and dead people, and wounds, and things similar to them.
Therefore, when we see something from them, and if it is truly in the third day of the month: we command then for ventilation to be done, after two or three hours have passed since sunset.
However, the remedy for ventilation of the neck is: because it brings about heaviness in the head, and what is poured out to the eyes. However, it should be after the evacuation of the whole body.
And this is indeed ventilation in the place of cephalic phlebotomy.
And it is not allowed to use it for those who are of cold complexion, or in whom there is a catarrh. For it brings about great harm to them.
And therefore, it is not allowed for the elderly, and in whose head there are cold pains.
Whoever becomes accustomed to it develops a habit of it.
And therefore you should command the Windblower to lay his hand briefly on the lower parts, fearing the generation of habit.
Ventosatio or Alkehel is a place for phlebotomy of the Fusco and Basilic veins, and for that reason it helps with asthma, constriction of breathing, splitting of instruments of breathing, cough, and repletion.
And it should be applied briefly to the Windblower Alkehel, because if it is placed below, it generates weakness in the heart and stomach.

If indeed the blood is very foul, then a third incision should be made: to reach the end.
And finally, when we want to extract the blood gradually or a little at a time, one incision is sufficient for us. If we want to extract the blood in large amounts, then we make many incisions.
And if we measure the blood to be thick, then it is necessary to make a deep incision: and the limit of equality in the incision is the depth of the skin.
What is that which must be administered from oils at the position of the Ventosators, and what should the ventosator beware of.

FORM OF VENTOSIITY ADMINISTERED WITH FIRE.
LET THE WIDTH OF ITS MOUTH BE TWO OPENED FINGERWIDTHS, ACCORDING TO WHAT WE FORMED: AND LET ITS QUANTITY IN DEEP BE HALF A PALM: AND LET IT BE IN SIDE OF IT IN PLACE WHICH IS AROUND MEDIUM OF IT, A SMALL HOLE, ACCORDING TO QUANTITY THAT ENTERS ITSELF ACUS: MAKE FROM AIR SIMULTANEOUSLY, OR YELLOW, MARGIN OF ROUGH, LENGTHENED, EQUAL, WASHED: THAT NOT HURT MEMBER AT ITS POSITION ON IT: AND LET BE IN MIDDLE OF IT TRANSVERSE STICK FROM AIR, OR IRON, WHERE PLACE IS CANDELA WITH FIRE.
AND NOW THIS VENTOSIITY IS MADE GREAT, GREATER THAN WE TOLD, AND LITTLE LESS THAT ONE, ACCORDING TO ITS AILMENT AND AGE WHO USES.
FOR VENTOSIITIES OF BOYS, AND WEAKENED ARE OTHERS, THAN VENTOSIITIES OF MEN, AND ROUGH BODIES.
BUT THE QUALITY OF PLACING THIS VENTOSIITY WITH FIRE ON MEMBER IS, THAT ACCEND LICINIUM WITH FIRE FROM LINEN DECENTLY, OR SMALL CANDLE FROM CLAY: AND PUT IT OVER MIDDLE OF TRANSVERSE STICK WHICH IS IN MIDDLE OF VENTOSIITY: THAT BE ACCENSED FIRE ABOUT LOWER PART OF VENTOSIITY, THAT NOT BURN BODY WEAK.
Then place it on the limb: and let the finger be on the hole that I mentioned, until when we grasp the puffy part: while we lack, we remove the finger, and the steam comes out through that hole, and the puffy part is dissolved immediately.
Then apply the lime according to its usual method, and repeat it if you lack that.
However, in the puffy part that is administered in the pain of pleurisy with water, it is not a knife that passes through, nor a hole: and it is not administered, unless because the water is filled, and it is placed on the limb only.
And this is its form.
And this puffy part, the greater it is, so that it can hold much water, is better.
¶ On the suspension of Sanguisugarum.
Sanguisugarum are not administered in many places, unless in those limbs in which the position of the puffy parts is not possible, due to their size, such as the lip, and the jaw, and the like. Or in a limb stripped of flesh, such as the finger, and the nose, and the like.
And the quality of using them is: that from the puffy parts that are in sweet waters, clean from putrefaction.
Then they are released during the day and night in sweet water, until they are hungry, and there remains nothing in their stomach. Then the body is purged in the first place with phlebotomy, and with puffy parts. Then clean the limb of the sick person, until it reddens. Then they are placed on top of it.
When therefore they are filled, and fall, and it is possible to suck the place with puffy parts, then it is more final in the cure: and if not, then wash the place with vinegar. Then, with much water, it is rubbed and squeezed out.
If the course of the blood is prolonged after the amputation of the Sanguisugar, and there is dripping: then pour cold linen cloth into water and place it above, until the dripping is removed.
If the blood multiplies, then powder is sprinkled on top of it, such as Zigi crushed, or galbanum, and similar things from stoptics: until the blood is removed.
Or they are placed on the place of the cut open beans: and they are let go, until the beans stick in the place, because the blood is removed.
And it is necessary if it is necessary to repeat the amputation of the Sanguisugar, when it is possible, to change them.
But if the Sanguisugar are prevented from hanging, then the place is cleaned with fresh blood. Or a plug is placed in the places, until something comes out of the blood. Then they are placed, because they themselves when they feel something from the blood, stick immediately.
When therefore you want them to fall, powder is sprinkled on top of them something from crushed aloe, or salt, or ashes: and they fall immediately.
